# Podium Implementation Gap Report

This report records gaps, inconsistencies, and bugs found by reviewing the Podium implementation against the specification in `spec/`. Each spec subsection was reviewed on its own against the Go code, and every finding cites `file:line` evidence. The report represents the `fix/spec-gap-remediation` branch at commit `e8e4210`.

This is a fresh audit run. One agent reviewed each of the 82 subsections against the code, superseding the prior report; all previously closed findings were removed. Every finding below is `OPEN`. The per-subsection source files are under `tmp/build-gaps-new/F-{section}.md`. Generated 2026-06-02.

Each finding has an ID of the form `F-{section}.{subsection}.{n}`, a severity in brackets, and a status. Every finding starts at `OPEN`. The description of each finding begins with a kind tag: `(gap)`, `(inconsistency)`, or `(bug)`.

## Totals

- 104 findings across 42 of the 82 reviewed subsections. 40 subsections had no findings.
- By severity: 5 High, 40 Medium, 42 Low, and 17 Info.
- By kind: 34 gap, 60 inconsistency, and 10 bug.

Severity meanings used by the reviewers:

- **High**: spec-mandated behavior missing or broken in a way that affects correctness, security, data integrity, or auth; bugs causing wrong results, crashes, data loss, or access bypass.
- **Medium**: partial implementation or behavioral deviation with limited blast radius or a workaround; missing validation; wrong edge-case handling.
- **Low**: minor deviation, missing non-critical field, or naming and cosmetic mismatch.
- **Info**: ambiguity, observation, or item to confirm, with no clear defect.

## High-severity findings

- F-4.6.1 — Runtime-registered layers never enter the effective view in an authenticated deployment
- F-7.3.1 — `GET /v1/layers` leaks the inbound webhook HMAC secret
- F-8.5.1 — Erasure leaves caller_email and caller_groups unredacted
- F-13.4.1 — Metadata store never adds columns to existing tables
- F-14.10.1 — layer commands ignore the bootstrapped sync.yaml registry

## F-0.0 — 0 Quickstart

_Reviewed spec/00-quickstart.md §0.0 against the implementation._

The quickstart presents the end-to-end author and consumer flow: the dual-file artifact layout (`SKILL.md` plus `ARTIFACT.md`), the frontmatter fields each file carries, the `podium layer reingest <id>` command and its confirmation output, and the MCP `load_domain` and `load_artifact` responses. Every concrete contract the section states is satisfied by the code. The dual-file layout and the skill-requires-`SKILL.md` rule are enforced in `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:191` and `pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:96`. The `ARTIFACT.md` frontmatter field names (`type`, `version`, `when_to_use`, `tags`, `sensitivity`) match the YAML tags in `pkg/manifest/types.go:100`, with `low` a valid sensitivity value at `pkg/manifest/types.go:34`, and the `SKILL.md` fields (`name`, `description`, `license`) match `pkg/manifest/types.go:213`.

The `podium layer reingest <id>` command exists at `cmd/podium/layer.go:352` and prints one `artifact: <id>@<version>   layer: <layer>` line per ingested artifact at `cmd/podium/layer.go:414`, matching the quickstart's sample output verbatim. The backing endpoint `POST /v1/layers/reingest?id=ID` returns the `layer` and `artifacts` (with `id` and `version`) fields the CLI consumes (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:927`). The MCP `load_domain` response is the registry's `LoadDomainResponse`, whose `subdomains` and `notable` JSON keys are explicit at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:397`, and each notable entry carries `id` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:421`. The MCP `load_artifact` response carries `manifest_body` and `materialized_at` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1422`, and for a skill the `manifest_body` is the `SKILL.md` body, not the empty `ARTIFACT.md` body, per `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1045`. The materialized skill output includes a `SKILL.md` path at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1373`, consistent with the example `materialized_at` entry.

The example registry URL in the quickstart command omits `--registry`, which the CLI requires (`cmd/podium/layer.go:372`), but the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` environment variable supplies it (`cmd/podium/layer.go:355`), so this is an illustrative omission rather than a defect. The materialization path `/workspace/.podium/runtime/.../SKILL.md` is an illustrative example; the host supplies the destination root at `load_artifact` time (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1341`). No checkable contract in the section diverges from the code.

No findings.

## F-1.1 — 1.1 What Podium Is

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md §1.1 against the implementation._

Section 1.1 is the high-level overview of what Podium is. Most of its text is conceptual framing that states no checkable wire contract. The concrete, checkable claims it does name are the meta-tool set, the built-in artifact type names, the cross-type dependency edge field names, the `TypeProvider` and `HarnessAdapter` SPIs, the `podium-py` and `podium-ts` SDK packages, the `podium sync` one-shot and watcher modes, and the merge precedence rules (most-restrictive-wins for security fields, last-layer-wins/child-wins for descriptions). Every one of these is satisfied by the implementation.

The meta-tools `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` are dispatched in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068-1077`. The built-in artifact types `skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`, and `mcp-server` are defined in `pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25`. The cross-type dependency edges `extends:`, `delegates_to:`, and `mcpServers:` are defined in `pkg/dependency/graph.go:13-15` and carried as frontmatter fields in `pkg/manifest/types.go:124,140,149`. The `TypeProvider` SPI is `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:39` and the `HarnessAdapter` SPI is `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:92`. The SDKs expose `Client` classes with the catalog operations in `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:338` and `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:349`. The `podium sync` watcher is wired in `cmd/podium/main.go:201,332` over `pkg/sync/watch.go`. The merge precedence rules are implemented in `pkg/manifest/merge.go:32-64`, with scalar child-wins for `description` and most-restrictive-wins for `sensitivity`, `sandbox_profile`, and `search_visibility`. The built-in adapter roster (`none`, Claude Code, Claude Desktop, Claude Cowork, Cursor, Codex, Gemini, OpenCode, Pi, Hermes) registered in `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:155-167` matches the roster the section's §6.7 cross-reference names. No findings.

No findings.

## F-1.2 — 1.2 Problem Statement

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md §1.2 against the implementation._

Section 1.2 (`spec/01-overview.md:33`-`46`) states the problems Podium addresses and is primarily conceptual prose. The concrete, checkable elements it enumerates are the first-class artifact types, the cross-type dependency edges, the named harness adapters, and the consumer paths. Each of these resolves to real code. The first-class types `skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`, and `mcp-server` are defined in `pkg/manifest/types.go:21`-`27`. The cross-type dependency edges the section calls out (`extends:`, `delegates_to:`, and `mcpServers:` resolving to `mcp-server`-type artifacts) exist as edge kinds in `pkg/dependency/graph.go:13`-`15`, with the corresponding manifest fields `DelegatesTo` and `MCPServers` in `pkg/manifest/types.go:140` and `pkg/manifest/types.go:124`.

The cross-harness portability claim names Claude Code, Cursor, Codex, and Gemini as delivery targets; adapters for these exist in `pkg/adapter/builtins.go` (for example `Cursor` at line 49 and `Gemini` at line 124, with the Claude Code and Codex adapters in `pkg/adapter/claudecode.go` and `pkg/adapter/codex.go`). The consumer paths the section describes are all present: the language SDKs at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py` and `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts`, the MCP server under `cmd/podium-mcp`, and the `podium sync` command dispatched in `cmd/podium/main.go:47`.

Every concrete claim in §1.2 is backed by code, and the section states no wire format, endpoint, error envelope, default, or invariant that the implementation contradicts. No implementation defects attributable to this subsection were found.

No findings.

## F-1.3 — 1.3 Design Principles (incl 1.3.1 When Podium Helps)

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md §1.3 against the implementation._

I reviewed the design principles in `spec/01-overview.md` lines 48 to 74, including the §1.3.1 "When Podium Helps" sub-subsection. §1.3 is a list of design principles, most of which restate concrete contracts that are specified in detail in later sections. I extracted every checkable claim that §1.3 states and traced each to code. §1.3.1 is advisory prose about when Podium adds value over a file-copy script and states no checkable implementation contract, so it carries no findings.

The concrete claims §1.3 makes all hold in the current implementation. The artifact type system `skill`/`agent`/`context`/`command`/`rule`/`hook`/`mcp-server` is defined exactly as written (`pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25`). The dependency edge kinds `extends`/`delegates_to`/`mcpServers` are first-class and span types (`pkg/dependency/graph.go:13-15`). The immutability invariant per `(artifact_id, version)` is enforced on ingest for both Git-source and local-source layers through the metadata store, which rejects a re-put of the same id and version with a different content hash and treats an identical hash as an idempotent no-op (`pkg/store/memory.go:61-90`, `pkg/store/sqlite.go:202-250`). `load_artifact` materializes bundled resources to a host destination path atomically through a stage-then-rename tree write that leaves the destination unchanged on partial failure (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:205-280`). High-sensitivity artifacts are signed under a sensitivity-driven verification policy (`pkg/sign/sign.go:95-103`). The project is MIT-licensed (`LICENSE` line 1). Manifests are markdown with YAML frontmatter, with the leading `---` block parsed off the prose body (`pkg/manifest/parse.go:36-41`). A single MCP binary selects its identity provider by configuration, defaulting to `oauth-device-code` and accepting `injected-session-token` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:241`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:345-349`). The meta-tools `load_domain`/`search_domains`/`search_artifacts`/`load_artifact` are registered and dispatched under those exact names (`cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:49-89`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068-1077`). The `HarnessAdapter` translates canonical artifacts into harness-native form and provides a `none` adapter for raw output (`pkg/adapter/none.go:9-21`). Both language SDKs exist (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts`).

No findings.

## F-1.4 — 1.4 Constraints and Decisions

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md §1.4 against the implementation._

Section 1.4 is a decision/rationale table whose concrete, checkable claims are: the built-in adapter roster (`spec/01-overview.md:83`), the single `admin` role per tenant with no per-artifact roles (`spec/01-overview.md:88`), the default cap of 3 user-defined layers per identity configurable per tenant (`spec/01-overview.md:89`), the layer source types `git`/`local` and per-layer visibility public/organization/groups/users (`spec/01-overview.md:86`), the absence of registry-side polling with ingest via webhooks or manual `podium layer reingest` (`spec/01-overview.md:90`), the PostgreSQL+pgvector default with sqlite+sqlite-vec standalone and pluggable vector backends and a pluggable `RegistryStore` (`spec/01-overview.md:91`), the workspace overlay at `.podium/overlay/` and content-addressed cache at `~/.podium/cache/` (`spec/01-overview.md:92`), and immutable semver-named versions with content-hash cache keying (`spec/01-overview.md:93`).

Each claim traces to code and holds. The adapter roster (`none`, `claude-code`, `claude-desktop`, `claude-cowork`, `cursor`, `codex`, `gemini`, `opencode`, `pi`, `hermes`) is registered in `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:155-168`. The default cap of 3 is `DefaultMaxUserLayers` at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:28`, resolved with override/tenant/default precedence at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:174-182` and enforced at register time at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:572-598`. Layer source and visibility fields are present at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:184-197`. The `podium layer reingest` and `reorder` commands exist at `cmd/podium/layer.go:24-55`. The overlay default `.podium/overlay/` is at `cmd/podium/main.go:1108` and `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:32`; the cache default `~/.podium/cache/` is at `cmd/podium/cache.go:42` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:323`. Immutability is enforced uniformly across `pkg/store/memory.go:61-90`, `pkg/store/sqlite.go:202-204`, and `pkg/store/postgres.go:216-335` via `ErrImmutableViolation` keyed on content hash. The single admin role lives at `pkg/registry/core/admin.go:16-20` with no per-artifact role type. The `RegistryStore` SPI is `pkg/store/store.go:1` / `:381`, and the pluggable vector backends (`pgvector.go`, `sqlitevec.go`, `pinecone.go`, `qdrant.go`, `weaviate.go`) all exist under `pkg/vector/`. No registry-side Git polling is present; the only internal interval loop is the vector-outbox drainer (`internal/serverboot/vector_outbox.go:78`), and ingest is driven by the webhook endpoint and the manual reingest path.

No findings.

## F-1.5 — 1.5 Where Podium Fits

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md §1.5 against the implementation._

Section 1.5 is a competitive-comparison table that positions Podium against adjacent product categories. Most of its content is conceptual prose about when each alternative wins, which states no checkable implementation contract. The section does assert a small set of concrete capabilities that the implementation must exhibit, and each one maps to real code. The listed artifact types (`skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`, `mcp-server` at `spec/01-overview.md:100`) are all defined in `pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25`. The `extends:` ordered-layer composition claim (`spec/01-overview.md:107`) is implemented in `pkg/registry/filesystem/extends.go:29`. Per-OIDC-group visibility (`spec/01-overview.md:106-111`) is backed by `pkg/identity/group_mapping.go` and the scope intersection in `pkg/layer/scope.go:26`. The cross-type dependency edge claim, "`mcpServers:` from skills and agents resolving to `mcp-server` artifacts" (`spec/01-overview.md:112`), is implemented as the `EdgeMCPServer` edge kind in `pkg/dependency/graph.go:15`. The published harness-adapter contract for foreign harnesses (`spec/01-overview.md:109`) is present in `pkg/adapter/adapter.go`. The MIT license claim (`spec/01-overview.md:108-109`) matches the repository `LICENSE` file, which is an MIT license.

No findings.

## F-1.6 — 1.6 Project Model

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md §1.6 against the implementation._

Section 1.6 is project-model and governance prose. It states the license, the governance model and its `GOVERNANCE.md` reference, distribution policy, the existence of a public reference registry, multi-vendor neutrality, and standards engagement (`spec/01-overview.md:116-124`). Most bullets are policy statements with no checkable implementation contract. The concrete, verifiable claims are the MIT license, the presence of `GOVERNANCE.md` describing a maintainer model and RFC process, and the existence of a reference registry with curated example artifacts.

Each verifiable claim holds. The license is MIT (`LICENSE:1`). `GOVERNANCE.md` exists and documents a maintainer model and an RFC process for spec changes (`GOVERNANCE.md:3-24`). A reference registry with example artifacts is present in the repository under `testdata/registries/reference` (for example `testdata/registries/reference/org-defaults/onboarding/welcome`). The remaining bullets on distribution, multi-vendor neutrality, and standards engagement describe project policy and impose no contract on the Go implementation, the wire formats, the CLI, or the configuration surface.

No findings.

## F-2.1 — 2.1 High-Level Component Map

_Reviewed spec/02-architecture.md §2.1 against the implementation._

§2.1 is a high-level component map. Its checkable contracts are the consumer identities and their providers, the meta-tool names, the `load_artifact` MCP wire path, the identity-provider built-ins, the workspace overlay path, and the rule that `podium sync` is the only consumer that works against a filesystem-source registry. Every one of these claims is satisfied by the code. The meta-tools `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` are registered both in the MCP bridge dispatch (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068`-`1077`) and in the registry HTTP route table (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:327`-`330`). The `load_artifact` sequence holds: the MCP bridge issues `GET /v1/load_artifact?id=<id>` carrying identity (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1161`), the registry handler reads the `id` query parameter and returns the manifest body plus presigned resource references (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:812`-`818`, `LoadArtifactResponse` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:463`-`497`, `LargeResourceLink.URL` JSON-tagged `presigned_url` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:508`), and the bridge then verifies, adapts, and atomically materializes before returning to the host (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1290`-`1378`).

The identity-provider built-ins `oauth-device-code` and `injected-session-token` are registered in `pkg/identity/registry.go:63`-`67` and consumed by both the MCP bridge (`cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:37`) and the SDKs (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:350`, `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:404`-`407`; `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:363`). The developer-host deployment uses MCP elicitation for the device-code flow (`cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:180`-`207`), stores the token in the OS keychain (`pkg/identity/keychain.go:11`-`34`), and defaults the workspace overlay to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:908`-`928`, `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:62`). `podium sync` supports one-shot and `--watch` (`cmd/podium/main.go:201`, `pkg/sync/watch.go`). The exclusivity claim on §2.1 line 9 holds: the MCP server explicitly rejects a `file://` or bare-path registry with `config.filesystem_registry_unsupported` and directs the user to `podium sync` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:298`-`304`), while the SDKs are HTTP-only clients.

No findings.

## F-2.2 — 2.2 Component Responsibilities

_Reviewed spec/02-architecture.md §2.2 against the implementation._

Section 2.2 is largely architectural prose describing the registry, the MCP server, `podium sync`, the language SDKs, the pluggable interfaces, and the shared Go module. I extracted the concrete, checkable contracts it states and traced each to code. The `IdentityProvider` built-ins `oauth-device-code` and `injected-session-token` are registered in `pkg/identity/registry.go:63` and `pkg/identity/registry.go:66`, with IDs asserted in `pkg/identity/identity.go:64` and `pkg/identity/identity.go:93`. The `HarnessAdapter` roster named on `spec/02-architecture.md:101` (Claude Code, Claude Desktop, Claude Cowork, Cursor, Codex, Gemini CLI, OpenCode, Pi, Hermes, plus `none`) is registered in `DefaultRegistry` at `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:153`-`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:170`. The `none` adapter writes the canonical layout (`ARTIFACT.md`, `SKILL.md`, bundled resources under `<artifact-id>/`) per `pkg/adapter/none.go:21`-`pkg/adapter/none.go:43`.

The `LocalOverlayProvider` reads `ARTIFACT.md` for every type plus `SKILL.md` for skills from a workspace path, implemented in `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:40` over the filesystem walk in `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:166` and `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:192`. The manifest parsers for `ARTIFACT.md`, `SKILL.md`, and `DOMAIN.md` exist at `pkg/manifest/parse.go:56`, `pkg/manifest/parse.go:72`, and `pkg/manifest/parse.go:111`. The SDKs accept a `harness` parameter on `materialize()` per `spec/02-architecture.md:101`: `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:175` and `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:50`. The `podium sync --watch` mode (`spec/02-architecture.md:93`) is wired at `cmd/podium/main.go:201`, and the MCP server's local state (OS-keychain credentials in `oauth-device-code` mode at `pkg/identity/keychain.go:34`, an in-memory overlay index at `cmd/podium-mcp/local_search.go:23`) is present.

Every concrete contract stated in §2.2 is satisfied by the implementation. The remaining text in the section is conceptual and states no additional checkable behavior beyond what is verified above.

No findings.

## F-3.1 — 3.1 The Problem

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md §3.1 against the implementation._

Section 3.1 of `spec/03-disclosure-surface.md` (lines 3 through 5) is a motivating statement about capability saturation. It asserts that tool-call accuracy degrades past roughly 50 to 100 tools in a single system prompt and falls off sharply past about 200, and it concludes that discovery has to be staged for larger catalogs. This text states no concrete, checkable contract: there are no wire formats, JSON field names, HTTP methods, paths, status codes, error envelopes, CLI commands, config keys, environment variables, default values, file layout entries, or validation rules tied to this subsection. The concrete realization of the "staged discovery" idea lives in §3.2 and later subsections (the meta-tools `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact`), which are assigned to other agents and out of scope here.

I confirmed that the implementation does not encode the numeric thresholds in §3.1 as an enforced contract. A search for capability-saturation identifiers and for tool-count thresholds or limits across `pkg/`, `internal/`, and `cmd/` returned no matches, which is consistent with §3.1 being motivating prose rather than a behavioral requirement. There is therefore no implementation surface for §3.1 to diverge from.

No findings.

## F-3.2 — 3.2 Three Disclosure Layers

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md §3.2 against the implementation._

This subsection maps the disclosure layers onto the meta-tools: Layer 1 (`load_domain`, `search_domains`), Layer 2 (`search_artifacts`), Layer 3 (`load_artifact`). All four tools are registered as HTTP routes in `pkg/registry/server/server.go:327-330`, dispatched by the MCP stdio bridge in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068-1079`, and exposed by both SDK clients (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:507-662`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:497-614`). The Layer 1 claim that `load_domain` with no path describes top-level domains and with a path describes that domain's subdomains and notable artifacts holds: the handler at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:606-633` returns `subdomains` and `notable`, and the core path is in `pkg/registry/core/core.go:459`. The `search_domains` hybrid-retrieval claim (BM25 + embeddings fused via RRF over each domain's projection of `description` + `keywords` + truncated prose body) is implemented in `pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go:56-168`, ranking over `domainpkg.EmbeddingProjection(dom)` and fusing through `RRFFuse` at line 145, returning ranked descriptors carrying `path` so the host can drill in.

The Layer 2 claim that `search_artifacts(query?, scope?, type?, tags?)` accepts all-optional args, runs a hybrid retriever over manifest text, and returns descriptors only is satisfied: `pkg/registry/core/core.go:999-1118` runs `scoreBM25` over manifest text and RRF-fuses vector ranks (line 1065), the empty-query-with-scope "browse all artifacts in a domain" move returns matched records with score 0 (lines 1049-1052), and the server handler clears `Frontmatter` from every search result so the manifest body never rides along (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:686-690`). The Layer 3 claim that `load_artifact(artifact_id)` returns the manifest body inline with large blobs delivered via presigned URLs is satisfied: `pkg/registry/server/server.go:857-880` returns `manifest_body` inline and `attachResources` (line 922) presigns any resource above `objectstore.InlineCutoff` while returning smaller ones inline, with the MCP bridge performing lazy host-side materialization (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1100`).

The §3.2 contract holds across the registry, the MCP bridge, and the SDKs. One Info-level observation about the informal descriptor-tuple field naming is recorded below.

### - [ ] F-3.2.1 — search_artifacts descriptor tuple uses `description`, not `summary` [Info] — DEFERRED

Deferred: the only remediation named is read-only spec wording. The §3.2 `(artifact_id, summary, score)` tuple is an illustrative sketch; §7.6.1 governs the search-result schema, which the read CLI now emits (`frontmatter`, whose `description` field carries the summary the §3.2 sketch labels). The wire descriptor's `description` field serves that role for the human and MCP renderers, and the codebase reserves the `summary` field for `load_domain` notable entries. No code defect remains, and Ground Rule A keeps `spec/` read-only. Not unblocked by code in this batch.

(inconsistency) The spec at `spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:19` states that `search_artifacts` returns a ranked list of `(artifact_id, summary, score)` tuples. The wire descriptor produced for a search result carries `id`, `description`, and `score` rather than a field named `summary`: the core descriptor sets `Description: m.Description` with no `summary` field on the search path (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1739-1750`), and the server descriptor exposes `description` as the JSON key (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:421-424`). The `Summary` field exists on `ArtifactDescriptor` but is populated only on `load_domain` notable entries (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:552`), not on search results. The richer search-result schema is governed by §7.6.1 and the `description` field fully serves the role the spec sketch labels `summary`, so this is an informal-illustration field-name difference rather than a missing capability. Suggested direction: treat the §3.2 tuple as illustrative and, if exactness is desired, align the spec wording to name the `description` and `frontmatter` fields the read-CLI schema in §7.6.1 already defines.

## F-3.3 — 3.3 Three Enabling Concerns

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md §3.3 against the implementation._

I reviewed the three enabling concerns in `spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:25-33` against the registry core, lint, ingest, and serverboot code. The section is largely conceptual, but it makes several checkable claims: every request carries OAuth identity and the registry filters the effective view by each layer's visibility; the registry lints for thin descriptions and flags clusters of artifacts whose summaries collide; `search_domains` retrieves over `description`, `keywords`, and the prose body while `load_domain` returns descriptions; and the registry records loaded artifacts (correlated within a `session_id`) and uses that signal to rerank `search_artifacts` results and the `load_domain` notable ordering.

Each claim is satisfied in code. Visibility filtering is applied per-request through `visibleManifests` and `visibleLayerIDs` on the read paths for search, domain load, and artifact load (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1017`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1301`, `pkg/registry/core/domain_load.go:116`). The description-quality checks `ruleThinDescription` and `ruleCollidingDescriptions` exist in `pkg/lint/description_rules.go:73` and `pkg/lint/description_rules.go:107`, are bundled by `DescriptionAdvisoryRules()` at `pkg/lint/description_rules.go:42`, and the registry ingest pipeline runs them over the ingested record set at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:490`. The domain projection that `search_domains` ranks over includes description, keywords, and the truncated body (`pkg/domain/embedding.go:22-37`, consumed at `pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go:89`). The learn-from-usage signal is recorded on a successful load at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1297`, threads `session_id` from the MCP bridge and CLI (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:498`, `cmd/podium/main.go:985`), feeds the `search_artifacts` rerank at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1079`, and feeds the `load_domain` notable ordering at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:624`. The `MemoryUsageSignals` store is wired into the registry by default in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:717`, so the reranking is active in production rather than a no-op. The two further uses the spec marks as "planned and not yet implemented" (import-candidate suggestions and underperforming-description flagging) are correctly absent, which matches the spec's own negative statement.

No findings.

## F-3.4 — 3.4 Discovery Flow

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md §3.4 against the implementation._

Section 3.4 (`spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:35-39`) describes the discovery flow a host session follows: it calls `load_domain()` for the top-level map, `search_domains(query)` to find a neighborhood, `load_domain("<sub>")` to drill into a subdomain, `search_artifacts(query, scope="<domain>")` when the request is specific, and `load_artifact` when it has an artifact ID. The section also states the invariant "Only `load_artifact` writes to the host filesystem. The catalog lives at the registry; the working set lives on the host."

The checkable claims are the existence and naming of the four discovery operations, the `scope` parameter on `search_artifacts` and `search_domains`, the empty-path-means-top-level semantics of `load_domain`, and the filesystem-write invariant. All hold. The four MCP tools are declared with these names and parameters in `cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:49-94`, where `load_domain` takes a `path` (omit for top-level, line 54), and both `search_domains` (line 67) and `search_artifacts` (line 82) take a `scope` domain-path argument. The MCP dispatch routes `load_domain`, `search_domains`, and `search_artifacts` through the read-only HTTP proxy (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068-1076`; `proxyGet` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2164-2191` performs only an HTTP GET and returns JSON, and `searchArtifacts` at `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:13-73` reads the overlay snapshot and registry response without writing to disk), while only `load_artifact` reaches `deliverLoadArtifact` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1290`), which materializes under `materializeRoot` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1336-1390`). The registry handlers honor the same parameters: `handleLoadDomain` reads `path` and passes it through (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:606-609`), and `handleSearchDomains` and `handleSearchArtifacts` read `scope` from the query (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:643`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:673`). The discovery flow and the write invariant described in §3.4 are implemented as specified.

No findings.

## F-3.5 — 3.5 Scope Preview (Pre-Session)

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md §3.5 against the implementation._

I traced every checkable claim in §3.5 (`spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:41`-`71`) to the Go implementation and both SDKs. The claims hold. The `GET /v1/scope/preview` endpoint is registered and is GET-only at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:334` and `pkg/registry/server/server.go:782`-`799`. The core projection `PreviewScope` at `pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:100`-`159` returns the exact response object the spec illustrates: the `ScopePreview` struct at `pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:89`-`94` carries only `layers`, `artifact_count`, `by_type`, and `by_sensitivity`, with no per-artifact identifiers, descriptions, or bodies, matching the §3.5 requirement that the preview returns aggregate counts only. The preview is a read-only projection of the same composition a real session sees: both `PreviewScope` and `EffectiveView` derive their record set from `visibleManifests` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1695`-`1719`, consumed at `pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:109` and `pkg/registry/core/effective_view.go:35`), and the `layers` array is built from the precedence-ordered `EffectiveLayersWith` (`pkg/layer/composer.go:108`-`119`).

The tenant gate is implemented per spec. The config key `tenant.expose_scope_preview` defaults to `true` and is parsed in `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:76` and `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:321`, also overridable via `PODIUM_EXPOSE_SCOPE_PREVIEW` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1540`). The tri-state pointer defaults to enabled at `pkg/store/store.go:65`-`67`, and `scopePreviewEnabled` returns `true` when the tenant row is absent (`pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:165`-`174`). A disabled tenant yields `ErrScopePreviewDisabled` (`pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:106`), which the HTTP layer maps to `403 scope_preview_disabled` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:790`-`793`. The `by_sensitivity` buckets use the documented `low`/`medium`/`high` values from `pkg/manifest/types.go:34`-`36`, and an omitted sensitivity floors to `low` via `sensitivityBucket` (`pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:224`-`229`).

All consumer paths named in §3.5 expose the preview. The MCP server registers a `scope_preview` tool that proxies `GET /v1/scope/preview` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1084`-`1091`, `cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:117`). `podium sync --preview` calls the endpoint and prints aggregate counts without writing (`cmd/podium/main.go:199`, `cmd/podium/main.go:277`-`283`, `cmd/podium/scope_preview.go:80`-`98`). `podium status` surfaces the same aggregate block (`cmd/podium/status.go:62`-`70`). The Python SDK exposes `preview_scope()` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:739`-`748`) and the TypeScript SDK exposes `previewScope()` with a matching `ScopePreview` interface (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:260`-`265`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:685`-`687`). The endpoint uses the caller's verified OAuth identity through the shared `s.identity(r)` resolver (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:1081`-`1094`), so layer composition and read-scope narrowing apply exactly as for a real session. No findings.

No findings.

## F-4.1 — 4.1 Artifacts Are Packages of Arbitrary Files (first-class + extension types)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.1 against the implementation._

I checked the §4.1 contracts that are mechanically verifiable: the artifact directory layout (one or two manifest files, `ARTIFACT.md` required, `SKILL.md` required for skills), the type taxonomy (first-class `skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`; built-in extension `mcp-server`; extension types via the `TypeProvider` SPI), the manifest size lint (~20K tokens), the SKILL.md body soft caps (5K tokens, 500 lines), and the three resource size thresholds (256 KB inline cutoff, 1 MB per-file warning, 10 MB per-package error). Most of these hold. The type taxonomy matches exactly in `pkg/manifest/parse.go:170-171` and `pkg/manifest/types.go:18-26`, with `IsFirstClassType` excluding `mcp-server` correctly. The size thresholds are defined and applied with the right severities in `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:16` (`PerFileSoftCapBytes = 1 MB`, warning at line 78), `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:19` (`PerPackageSoftCapBytes = 10 MB`, error at line 89), `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:29` (`ManifestErrTokens = 20_000`), and `pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:41` (`InlineCutoff = 256 * 1024`). The inline-versus-presigned split honors the cutoff at both ingest (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1131`) and load (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:924`). `ARTIFACT.md` is required and `SKILL.md` is enforced for skills in `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:149,191-196`, bundled resources are captured as opaque blobs in `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:214-246`, the size lint reads only on-disk `rec.Resources` so external resources are correctly exempt from the caps (`pkg/lint/size_rules.go:71-85`), and the `TypeProvider` SPI in `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go` implements extension-type registration with the unknown-type check wired into lint at `pkg/lint/lint.go:191`.

One finding stands out. The §4.1 claim that bundled resources can be binary blobs and are returned inline below the cutoff is broken on the server's load path: binary inline resources are emitted as raw JSON strings without the base64 flag the wire protocol defines, so non-UTF-8 bytes are corrupted.

### - [x] F-4.1.1 — Binary inline resources corrupted; server never sets `resources_base64` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 83322b4): `attachResources` now base64-encodes the whole inline resource set and sets `resources_base64` (`encodeBinaryInlineResources`) when any inline payload is not valid UTF-8, so a binary bundled resource at or below the cutoff round-trips instead of being mangled into U+FFFD by `encoding/json`. The Python and TypeScript SDKs gained `resources_base64` decoding on the single-load path (the Go sync and MCP consumers already decoded it). Covered by server unit tests, a no-object-store integration round-trip, Python/TS SDK unit tests, and a standalone-server e2e.

(bug) §4.1 lists "binary blobs" among the arbitrary bundled files a package may carry (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:11`) and states that below the inline cutoff "resource bytes are returned in the `load_artifact` response body" (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:76`). The `load_artifact` wire format carries a `resources_base64` boolean (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:478`) precisely so binary inline resources survive JSON transport, and the consumer side decodes it (`pkg/sync/server.go:106,149-167` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1438`). The server-side producer never sets it. `attachResources` writes every inline resource as `resp.Resources[ref.Path] = string(body)` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:942`) and no code path in `pkg/registry` ever assigns `ResourcesB64 = true` or base64-encodes the bytes; the only reference to the field across the whole `pkg/registry` tree is the struct declaration at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:478`. Because Go's `encoding/json` replaces invalid UTF-8 bytes in a string with the U+FFFD replacement character, any binary bundled resource at or below the 256 KB cutoff (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:924`) is silently corrupted in the `load_artifact` response, even though ingest preserved the bytes faithfully (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1101-1109`). A server-source consumer materializing that resource gets garbage. The blast radius is limited to the server-source path for binary resources under the cutoff (filesystem-source materialization reads bytes from disk directly), and the detailed wire contract lives in §7.2, so this is rated Medium. Suggested direction: in `attachResources`, detect non-UTF-8 inline payloads (or unconditionally base64-encode the inline set) and set `resp.ResourcesB64 = true` so the existing consumer decode path round-trips binary bundled resources without corruption.

## F-4.2 — 4.2 Registry Layout on Disk

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.2 against the implementation._

The subsection states the registry's authoring layout, the canonical-ID rule, the reference-suffix grammar, the discovery-rendering knobs, and the layer-rooting model. I traced each concrete claim into the filesystem-source walk (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go`), the server ingest walk (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go`), the reference-pin grammar (`pkg/version/version.go`), the discovery knobs (`pkg/registry/core/domain_load.go`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go`, `pkg/domain/domain.go`), and the layer source providers (`pkg/layer/source/git.go`, `pkg/layer/source/local.go`).

The canonical-ID invariant holds. The ID is computed as the forward-slash directory path under the layer root in `canonicalID` at `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:252-266`, and the shared `ValidateCanonicalID` at `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:283-296` rejects a root-level `ARTIFACT.md` (empty ID) and any path segment containing `@`, the delimiter reserved for the `@<semver>` and `@sha256:<hash>` suffixes. Both the filesystem-source walk (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:262`) and the server ingest walk (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:973`) call the same validator, so the canonical home is enforced identically on both paths. The authoring depth never changes the ID because `canonicalID` uses the full relative path regardless of nesting depth. Nested artifact-package boundaries are respected on both walks (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:225` and `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1014`), so a leaf directory's own files are not captured as a parent's bundled resources.

The reference-suffix grammar holds. `version.ParsePin` at `pkg/version/version.go:53-103` parses `1.2.3`, `1.2.x`, `1.x`, and `sha256:<hex>`, and the `@` split is taken at the first `@` via `splitRef` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1318-1323`) and `SplitArtifactRef` (`pkg/layer/composer.go:233`), consistent with the segment-level `@` ban. The discovery-rendering claim holds: `DefaultMaxDepth = 3` at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:447`, with `fold_below_artifacts` and `fold_passthrough_chains` resolved in `resolveKnobs` (`pkg/registry/core/domain_load.go:42-105`) and overridable per-subtree via `DOMAIN.md` (`pkg/registry/core/domain_load.go:65-87`). The layer-rooting claim holds: both a Git source (`pkg/layer/source/git.go:18-24`) and a local filesystem source (`pkg/layer/source/local.go:10-24`) provide the layer root whose directory hierarchy becomes the layer's domain contribution. The embedded diagram exists at `docs/assets/diagrams/registry-layout.svg`. I found no implementation gaps, inconsistencies, or bugs against the concrete claims in this subsection.

No findings.

## F-4.3 — 4.3 Artifact Manifest Schema (universal/caller-interpreted/type-specific/external resources, 4.3.4 SKILL.md, 4.3.5 hook events)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.3 against the implementation._

The manifest schema is implemented in `pkg/manifest` and validated at ingest by `pkg/lint`. The universal, caller-interpreted, type-specific, and external-resource fields in `spec/04-artifact-model.md:137-251` map cleanly to the `Artifact` struct in `pkg/manifest/types.go:98-158`, including the camelCase wire keys `mcpServers` and `requiresApproval` (`pkg/manifest/types.go:124-125`) and the `input: { $ref: ... }` mapping form handled by `SchemaRef.UnmarshalYAML` (`pkg/manifest/parse.go:90-107`). The §4.3.5 canonical hook-event taxonomy matches the spec table exactly, name for name and in table order (`pkg/manifest/hook_events.go:9-55`), and `ruleHookEventCanonical` rejects any non-canonical event at ingest (`pkg/lint/lint.go:319-338`). The §4.3.4 SKILL.md compliance rules are implemented in depth: the field-allocation split (`pkg/manifest/skill_fields.go:12-58`), the both-files-present and name/description checks (`pkg/lint/lint.go:245-273`), the agentskills.io name syntax (`pkg/manifest/parse.go:124-150`), the description ≤ 1024 and compatibility ≤ 500 caps (`pkg/lint/skill_rules.go:14-21,126-133`), the 5K-token / 500-line / 20K-token body thresholds (`pkg/lint/size_rules.go:20-29,144-166`), the empty-or-single-HTML-comment ARTIFACT.md body rule (`pkg/lint/body_rules.go:47-62`), and the compatibility derivation from `runtime_requirements` and `sandbox_profile` at materialization (`pkg/adapter/compatibility.go:22-69`). Lint errors block ingest per `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:530-535`. The findings below concern the `rule_mode` default not reaching the Cursor adapter, a missing enum check on `rule_mode`, and the §4.3.5 capability-gate cross-reference that only fires when `target_harnesses` is declared.

### - [x] F-4.3.1 — Cursor adapter does not honor the `rule_mode: always` default when the field is unset [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit ce66b15): `cursorRuleBody` now maps an empty `RuleMode` to `manifest.RuleModeAlways` before the switch (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go`), so an unset `rule_mode` materializes on Cursor as `alwaysApply: true` per the §4.3 default. Covered by `TestCursor_RuleModeUnsetDefaultsToAlways` (unit) and `TestRuleModes_AbsentModeCursorAlwaysApply` (e2e).

(inconsistency) The spec declares `rule_mode: always | glob | auto | explicit  # default: always` for `type: rule` (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:204`), and the `rule_mode` table states an `always` rule loads when the session starts (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:213`). The parser does not apply this default; `ParseArtifact` leaves `RuleMode` empty when the field is absent (`pkg/manifest/parse.go:56-67`), and no materialization step backfills it (no `RuleModeAlways` assignment exists outside the Cursor switch, confirmed in `pkg/adapter` and `pkg/materialize`). The Cursor adapter switches on `art.RuleMode` with no default case, so an unset value emits no native key (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go:93-110`): the produced `.mdc` carries empty frontmatter (`cursorMDC`, `pkg/adapter/builtins.go:115-122`). A Cursor `.mdc` rule without `alwaysApply: true`, `globs`, or `description` is not always-applied, so a rule that omits `rule_mode` materializes on Cursor as a non-always rule, contradicting the spec default. The Claude Code adapter is unaffected because it relies on an absent `paths:` loading like `CLAUDE.md` (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:149-169`). Suggested direction: apply the spec default by treating an empty `RuleMode` as `manifest.RuleModeAlways` in `cursorRuleBody` (or normalize the default in `ParseArtifact`) so an unset `rule_mode` emits `alwaysApply: true` on Cursor.

### - [x] F-4.3.2 — Ingest does not reject an out-of-enum `rule_mode` value [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit ce66b15): added `manifest.IsCanonicalRuleMode`/`CanonicalRuleModes` (`pkg/manifest/rule_modes.go`) and the `ruleRuleModeCanonical` lint rule (`pkg/lint/required_fields.go`, registered in `AllRulesWithClient`), which errors (`lint.unknown_rule_mode`) when a `type: rule` artifact's non-empty `rule_mode` is outside the four canonical values, mirroring `ruleHookEventCanonical`. An empty value is left to the §4.3 default. Covered by unit, integration (`TestPodiumLint_RuleModeOutOfEnumErrors`), and e2e (`TestRuleModes_LintRejectsOutOfEnumMode`) tests.

(gap) The spec constrains `rule_mode` to the enumeration `always | glob | auto | explicit` (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:204,211-216`). No lint rule validates the value against this set. `ruleTypeRequiredFields` only switches on the `glob` and `auto` cases to enforce their companion fields (`pkg/lint/required_fields.go:30-41`), and `ruleRuleModeHygiene` only handles `glob` and `auto` and the non-rule-type case (`pkg/lint/required_fields.go:79-90`); neither flags an unrecognized value such as `rule_mode: sometimes`. Such a value passes ingest and then falls through the Cursor adapter switch to produce no native key (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go:93-110`), the same degraded outcome as F-4.3.1. The spec presents the value as a closed enumeration but does not separately state "lint rejects an unknown `rule_mode`", so this is scoped Low. Suggested direction: add a lint rule that errors when `RuleMode` is non-empty and not one of the four canonical values, mirroring `ruleHookEventCanonical` for `hook_event`.

### - [x] F-4.3.3 — Capability ingest gate only fires when `target_harnesses` is declared [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (spec reword): the implementation behavior is correct and unchanged; the §4.3.5 cross-reference, the §6.7 ✗-cell paragraph, and the §6.7.1 legend were the source of the contradiction and now describe the two-tier enforcement explicitly. Enforcement is split: ingest lint is the opt-in tier, where `ruleHarnessCapability` evaluates an artifact's used capabilities only against a declared `target_harnesses` set (`pkg/lint/harness_capability.go:37`, `adapter.Evaluate`); materialization is the always-on per-harness tier, where `adapter.TranslationError(harnessID, art)` fails a `load_artifact` onto a harness with a ✗ cell for a used field (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1415`, `:1649`). An absent `target_harnesses` therefore keeps ingest portable while the actual incompatibility is caught at load against the harness the artifact materializes onto. A default-on ingest gate against `adapter.FirstClassHarnesses()` was rejected as incoherent: claude-desktop is ✗ for every type, field, rule_mode, and hook_event row, so a default-to-all gate rejects essentially every artifact, and any curated default subset that drops the always-✗ harnesses still over-rejects (for example `hook_event` is ✗ on opencode), which would auto-exclude exactly the harnesses the gate is meant to flag and leave it equivalent to the current opt-in behavior. The §4.3.5/§6.7/§6.7.1 prose conflated the opt-in ingest gate with the always-on §6.9 materialization guard; the reword separates them. The same default-on framing was replicated in the §11 verification items and in the authoring docs, so all of them were reconciled: spec/04-artifact-model.md (§4.3.5 "Coverage varies by harness"), spec/06-mcp-server.md (§6.7 ✗-cell paragraph, §6.7.1 capability-matrix legend), spec/11-verification.md (rule-mode adapter conformance, hook materialization), docs/authoring/rule-modes.md (matrix legend, "How each harness honors them" intro, capability-mismatch note), docs/authoring/hooks.md, and docs/authoring/artifact-types.md. No code change. The doc-derived conformance suite (`pkg/lint/harness_capability_test.go:TestHarnessCapability_NoTargetHarnessesSilent`, T-D-artifact-types-37/38, T-D-first-agent-2) continues to assert the opt-in behavior the reword now documents.

(inconsistency) Section 4.3.5 states that "lint rejects ingest at the unsupported (✗) intersection unless `target_harnesses:` excludes the unsupported harness" (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:328`), which reads as a default-to-all-harnesses gate that `target_harnesses` narrows. The implementation inverts the default: `ruleHarnessCapability` skips the check entirely for any artifact without `target_harnesses` (`pkg/lint/harness_capability.go:37` returns early on `len(art.TargetHarnesses) == 0`), so a `type: hook` declaring a canonical event unsupported by a default harness, or a `type: rule` using a field at a ✗ intersection, passes ingest with no `target_harnesses` declared. The capability matrix and the `Evaluate` entry point live in §6.7.1 territory (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:207`), and the §4.3.5 sentence is a cross-reference to that matrix, so the canonical owner of the matrix semantics is the §6.7.1 audit; this finding records that the §4.3.5 wording and the lint default disagree. Suggested direction: confirm the intended default with the §6.7.1 matrix owner, and if the spec wording is authoritative, evaluate every artifact against the full default harness set when `target_harnesses` is absent so an unsupported (✗) intersection rejects ingest unless the harness is excluded.

### - [ ] F-4.3.4 — `delegates_to` is not constrained to agent-type targets at ingest [Info] — DEFERRED

Deferred: the constraint is descriptive in the spec and the documented behavior is explicit non-enforcement. The spec annotates the constraint only as an inline YAML comment ("constrained to agent-type") and states no ingest error. The doc-derived conformance suite asserts the opposite of enforcement: `TestArtifactTypes_DelegatesToTypeNotEnforcedAtLint` (T-D-artifact-types-37) requires `podium lint` to exit 0 when an agent delegates to a skill, and `TestAgentTutorial_DelegatesEdgeIndexed`/`TestAgentTutorial_ImpactListsDependent` (T-D-first-agent-13/14, from your-first-agent.md) require an agent→skill `delegates_to` edge to ingest cleanly and be indexed. A prototype `ruleDelegatesToAgentType` (errors when a target resolves within the linted set to a non-agent) was implemented and reverted because it broke all three: it blocks ingest of the documented agent→skill delegation. Enforcing the constraint at filesystem lint contradicts the spec-conformant documented behavior; this needs a spec decision (the doc comment itself flags the type-combination check as "a server-ingest concern, not filesystem lint"). spec/ is read-only and unchanged.

(gap) The spec annotates `delegates_to` as "well-known delegation targets (constrained to agent-type)" for `type: agent` (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:198-200`). The field is parsed (`pkg/manifest/types.go:140`) and recorded as a dependency edge (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1167-1169`), but no lint or ingest check verifies that a delegation target resolves to a `type: agent` artifact. The constraint appears only as an inline comment inside a YAML example and the spec states no explicit ingest error for a non-agent target, so this is recorded as Info pending confirmation that the constraint is meant to be enforced rather than descriptive. Suggested direction: decide whether the agent-type constraint is enforceable at ingest (when the target resolves within the linted set) and, if so, add a lint rule; otherwise clarify in the spec that it is advisory.

## F-4.4 — 4.4 Bundled Resources (4.4.1 Execution Model Contract, 4.4.2 Content Provenance)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.4 against the implementation._

This review traced the §4.4 claims about bundled-resource discovery, content-addressed storage, atomic materialization, the ingest-time prose linter, the §4.4.1 execution-model contract (`runtime_requirements`, `sandbox_profile`), and the §4.4.2 content-provenance markers. Most of the surface is implemented and correct. Implicit discovery of bundled resources (every file under the artifact root except `ARTIFACT.md`, and `SKILL.md` for skills) is performed by `captureResources` in `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:214-244`, and there is no `resources:` frontmatter field on `manifest.Artifact` (`pkg/manifest/types.go:98-158`). Content-addressed storage keyed by SHA-256 with byte deduplication is in `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1121-1136`, and presigned-URL delivery is provided by the object stores (`pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:120-125`). Atomic materialization with `.tmp` + rename is implemented in `pkg/materialize/atomic.go:205-287`. The §4.4.1 contract is wired end to end: `runtime_requirements` and `sandbox_profile` parse into `manifest.RuntimeRequirements` and `manifest.SandboxProfile` (`pkg/manifest/types.go:126-127,186-190,49-57`), `materialize.ErrRuntimeUnavailable` carries the `materialize.runtime_unavailable` code (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:25-28`), the MCP server gates both runtime and sandbox at load time (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1302-1310,1717-1745`), and the seccomp-strict baseline ships embedded and materializes under the destination (`pkg/materialize/seccomp.go:16-72`). The §4.4.2 inline imported-block markers are rewritten into Claude `<untrusted-data>` regions and wired through the Claude adapter (`pkg/adapter/provenance.go:16-45`, `pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:48-102`).

The findings concern the ingest-time prose linter's missing "other artifacts" resolution branch (§4.4 line 348), the dropped document-level `source:` provenance declaration (§4.4.2 line 384), and a permissive URL-status acceptance range that diverges from the literal "200/3xx" wording (§4.4 line 347).

### - [x] F-4.4.1 — Prose linter never resolves references to other artifacts [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit b0b25da): `ruleProseReferenceResolution.Check` now builds the visible catalog from the linted record set (`artifactCatalog`) and `checkReference` resolves a non-bundled reference against it (stripping any §4.7.6 version pin) before erroring, so a reference naming another artifact resolves while an unknown ID stays an ingest error. The registry arg is nil at ingest, so the catalog is the record set (full registry walk for `podium lint`, the layer at single-layer ingest).

(gap) Spec §4.4 line 348 requires the ingest-time linter to validate that prose references resolve to one of three targets, the third being "Other artifacts (registry-side resolution against current visible catalog)", and line 350 states that unresolved references are an ingest error. The implementing rule `ruleProseReferenceResolution` in `pkg/lint/body_rules.go:112-146` handles only two of the three branches: absolute `http`/`https` URLs go through `checkURL` (`pkg/lint/body_rules.go:184-218`) and everything else goes through `checkBundled` (`pkg/lint/body_rules.go:155-182`). There is no branch that resolves a reference against the visible catalog of other artifacts. The `Check` method even discards the `*filesystem.Registry` argument (`pkg/lint/body_rules.go:112`, parameter named `_`), so no catalog lookup is possible, and no other lint rule performs this resolution (`pkg/lint/lint.go:100-122`). A prose reference written as a relative path that names another artifact rather than a bundled file is therefore reported as `prose reference %q does not match any bundled file` (`pkg/lint/body_rules.go:176-181`) instead of being resolved against the catalog, and a reference that the spec intends to be validated as an artifact target receives no registry-side check at all. Suggested direction: add an artifact-reference branch to `ruleProseReferenceResolution.Check` that, for references matching the artifact-ID form, resolves against the current visible catalog via the supplied `*filesystem.Registry` and emits an error only when the target is absent.

### - [x] F-4.4.2 — Document-level `source:` provenance declaration is parsed away and never propagated [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit b0b25da): added `Artifact.Source` (`yaml:"source,omitempty"`) so the field parses instead of being dropped, with default-for-unlisted child-wins merge handling. The Claude adapter reads the document-level source and, when it declares a non-authored default provenance (for example `imported`), wraps the manifest's authored prose in a single `<untrusted-data source="...">` region; `authored` and absent keep the prose trusted.

(gap) Spec §4.4.2 lines 382-385 show a manifest declaring its default provenance through a frontmatter `source:` field (`source: authored`), and line 394 states adapters propagate provenance markers to harnesses that support trust regions. The `manifest.Artifact` struct has no `source` field (`pkg/manifest/types.go:98-158`), and a search of the manifest package finds no `source` mapping or `Source` field (`pkg/manifest`). Because `ParseArtifact` uses a non-strict `yaml.Unmarshal` (`pkg/manifest/parse.go:62`), a `source:` key in frontmatter is silently dropped rather than rejected, so the value is neither stored nor available to adapters. The adapter provenance rewrite handles only the inline `<!-- begin imported ... -->` blocks (`pkg/adapter/provenance.go:16-45`) and has no path that reads a document-level `source:` declaration. As a result the document-level provenance signal described in §4.4.2 is unavailable to hosts applying differential trust. Suggested direction: add a `Source string` field with `yaml:"source,omitempty"` to `manifest.Artifact`, and have the Claude adapter consider the document-level `source` when deciding the default trust region for the authored prose.

### - [x] F-4.4.3 — URL reference linter accepts any 2xx status, not the spec's "200/3xx" [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit b0b25da): tightened the accepted range in `checkURL` to `resp.StatusCode == http.StatusOK || (resp.StatusCode >= 300 && resp.StatusCode < 400)`, so a HEAD returning 201/204/206 no longer passes while 200 and 3xx redirects still do.

(inconsistency) Spec §4.4 line 347 requires the URL branch of the prose linter to treat a reference as valid when "HTTP HEAD returns 200/3xx", meaning HTTP 200 or any 3xx redirect. The implementation in `pkg/lint/body_rules.go:209-211` accepts the full range `resp.StatusCode >= 200 && resp.StatusCode < 400`, which additionally treats 2xx codes such as 201, 204, and 206 as passing. A HEAD that returns 204 No Content for a reference that does not actually serve the named resource would pass the linter under the code while the literal spec wording ("200/3xx") would reject it. The divergence is narrow because HEAD on a fetchable resource normally returns 200 or a 3xx redirect, so the blast radius is small. Suggested direction: tighten the accepted range to `resp.StatusCode == 200 || (resp.StatusCode >= 300 && resp.StatusCode < 400)`, or amend the spec wording to "2xx/3xx" if the broader range is intended.

## F-4.5 — 4.5 Domain Organization (4.5.1 DOMAIN.md, 4.5.2 Imports/Globs, 4.5.3 Unlisted Folders, 4.5.4 Across Layers, 4.5.5 Discovery Rendering)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.5 against the implementation._

I traced the §4.5 claims through `pkg/domain` (DOMAIN.md merge, glob resolution, fallback description), `pkg/registry/core` (`LoadDomain`, `SearchDomains`, knob resolution, folding, notable selection, rendering note), `pkg/manifest` (the `Domain`/`DomainDiscovery` schema), `pkg/lint/domain_imports.go` (cycle, unresolved-import, broad-glob, and per-domain-override-disabled rules), `internal/serverboot` (tenant `discovery:` wiring), the registry HTTP handler, the MCP bridge, and both SDKs. Most concrete contracts hold. The glob matcher implements `*` as one segment, `**` as recursive, and `{a,b,c}` alternatives (`pkg/domain/resolve.go:86-108`, `pkg/domain/resolve.go:65-82`), with `exclude:` applied after `include:` (`pkg/domain/resolve.go:34-42`). The cross-layer merge applies last-layer-wins for description and body, additive include/exclude, most-restrictive unlisted, lowest-value `max_depth`/`notable_count`/`target_response_tokens`, highest `fold_below_artifacts`, and true-over-false `fold_passthrough_chains` (`pkg/domain/domain.go:31-83`). Unlisted propagation and the `domain.not_found` behavior for unlisted paths are correct (`pkg/registry/core/domain_load.go:166-173`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:492-494`), and `search_domains` excludes both DOMAIN.md-less and unlisted domains (`pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go:78-103`). Notable dedup with featured-wins tagging, the cap, the candidate pool, the rendering note format, and the depth-cap message all match (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:624-676`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:906-945`). Tenant `discovery:` defaults and the `allow_per_domain_overrides` gate are wired from `registry.yaml` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:711-713`, `1333-1347`).

The findings below cover behaviors §4.5 mandates that the implementation does not provide: the DOMAIN.md body-length lint warning, the audit recording of resolved depth and fold decisions, the client-side merge of a workspace-local DOMAIN.md for `load_domain`, and an SDK depth default that overrides the configured rendering default.

### - [x] F-4.5.1 — `domain.loaded` audit event omits resolved depth and fold decisions [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (be0c01f): `LoadDomain` now populates the `domain.loaded` audit `Context` with the resolved render depth, `depth_capped`, `folded_subdomains` (count of sparse subdomains collapsed by `fold_below_artifacts`), and `passthrough_collapsed` (read off the rendered tree before the budget pass trims it). The serverboot emitter already passes `Context` through to the audit log unchanged. Covered by core unit tests (default depth, cap, fold count, pass-through collapse) and an e2e test asserting the fields reach the audit log.

(gap) §4.5.5 line 540 states "Audit events (§8) record the resolved depth and fold decisions per call" (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:540`). The `domain.loaded` audit event constructed in `LoadDomain` populates only `Type`, `Caller`, `Target`, `ResolvedLayers`, and `ResultSize` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:463-474`); the `Context` map is never set and no depth or fold field is written, even though the call computes `renderDepth`, `depthCapped`, and the per-child fold outcomes (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:501-509`, `585-598`). `AuditEvent` has a `Context map[string]string` slot available (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:135`), and no downstream enrichment of `domain.loaded` exists in `pkg/audit` or `internal/serverboot`. A reviewer reading the audit trail cannot recover the resolved depth or whether folding occurred for a given call. Suggested direction: populate the `domain.loaded` event's `Context` with the resolved render depth and a fold summary (for example the count of folded subdomains and whether pass-through collapse fired) before emit.

### - [ ] F-4.5.2 — Workspace-local DOMAIN.md is not merged client-side for `load_domain` [Medium] — DEFERRED

DEFERRED (be0c01f): a faithful client-side merge per §4.5.4 requires the client to re-resolve a local `DOMAIN.md`'s `include:` globs over the registry's full artifact catalog (§4.5.2 "the merged view") and to re-run the §4.5.5 folding, notable selection, and budget rendering with the merged discovery knobs. The `/v1/load_domain` response is already rendered (capped notable list, depth-limited subtree per `pkg/registry/server/server.go:392`) and exposes neither the raw artifact-ID catalog nor the unrendered tree the client would need, so the merge cannot be completed from the current wire contract; a partial merge limited to description/keywords plus local artifacts would silently diverge from the spec on import resolution and folding. Closing it requires a new registry surface that exposes the per-domain artifact catalog (or a dedicated client-merge endpoint) plus parallel implementations in the MCP bridge and both SDKs, which is beyond one batch. The two e2e tests whose skip messages referenced this finding (`TestCoreConcept_DomainMDDescriptionKeywords`, `TestDomainModel_CLIShowSurfacesDomainMD`) were mis-attributed: they exercise server-side `DOMAIN.md` surfacing, which is implemented and verified by T-D-domains-4/5/8; both are now un-skipped and passing (be0c01f), and `podium domain show` now renders the requested domain's keywords.

(gap) §4.5.2 lines 453-455 require that "A local `DOMAIN.md`'s globs resolve over the merged view (layers org + team + user + local)" because the workspace local overlay is merged client-side, and §4.5.4 line 490 states "When a workspace-local-overlay `DOMAIN.md` is involved, the MCP server applies the merge client-side after the registry returns its result for the registry-side layers" (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:453-455`, `spec/04-artifact-model.md:490`). The MCP bridge dispatches `load_domain` straight to the registry with no overlay step (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068-1070`), in contrast to `load_artifact` and `search_artifacts`, which do consult the overlay (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1100-1109`, `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:42-54`). Both SDKs proxy `load_domain` directly with no overlay merge (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:507-513`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:497-501`) while applying overlay fusion to the other read meta-tools. The overlay provider itself only returns artifact records and surfaces no DOMAIN.md (`pkg/overlay/overlay.go:40-57`). A local DOMAIN.md therefore never participates in `load_domain` enumeration, description, or import resolution, so its globs resolve over the registry view only. Suggested direction: have the MCP bridge and the SDKs read the workspace-local DOMAIN.md set, merge it (per §4.5.4) onto the registry result, and re-resolve includes over the merged-plus-local artifact view before returning.

### - [x] F-4.5.3 — No lint warning for DOMAIN.md body exceeding 2000 tokens [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (12f682e): added `ruleDomainBodySize` (`pkg/lint/size_rules.go`), registered in `AllRulesWithClient`, which walks every DOMAIN.md and warns (`lint.domain_body_size`) when the prose body exceeds the new `DomainBodyWarnTokens = 2000` threshold, reusing `approxTokenCount`. Surfaced by `podium lint` over a filesystem-source registry. Covered by 2 unit tests (over-cap, boundary/empty) and 2 e2e `podium lint` tests.

(gap) §4.5.5 line 525 states "Body length is recommended ≤ 2000 tokens; lint warns above" (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:525`). The lint rule set registered in `AllRulesWithClient` includes no DOMAIN.md body-length rule (`pkg/lint/lint.go:100-122`), and the size rules in `pkg/lint/size_rules.go` measure only the SKILL.md body (§4.3.4) and the manifest token cap (§4.1), with no `Domain` reference. A repo-wide search for the `2000`/`2_000` threshold returns no match outside the §4.7 projection cap (`pkg/domain/embedding.go:12`, which is the unrelated 500-token projection truncation). An author can ship a DOMAIN.md whose prose body is well over 2000 tokens and receive no lint warning. Suggested direction: add an ingest-time lint rule that approximates the DOMAIN.md prose-body token count (reusing `approxTokenCount` in `pkg/lint/size_rules.go`) and emits a warning above 2000 tokens.

### - [x] F-4.5.4 — SDK `load_domain` hardcodes `depth=1`, overriding the configured default of 3 [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (be0c01f): both SDKs leave the `load_domain` depth unset by default (Python `depth: int | None = None`, TS `depth?: number`) and omit the `depth` query parameter unless the caller supplies one, so the registry's default-depth path applies the configured `max_depth` of 3. Covered by SDK unit tests in both languages (default omits `depth`; an explicit depth is forwarded).

(inconsistency) §4.5.5 line 500 sets `max_depth` Default 3, and the caller-override rules state depth "overrides the configured default" so an unspecified depth should fall back to the resolved ceiling (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:500`, `spec/04-artifact-model.md:544`; §5.1 reiterates that the `depth` arg "overrides the configured default" at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:7`). Both SDKs default the `depth` argument to `1` and always send it (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:507-513`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:497-501`), so a default SDK `load_domain` call renders a single level instead of the configured default of 3; the registry's default-depth path (`LoadDomainOptions.Depth == 0` using the resolved `max_depth`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:501-509`) is never reached from an SDK caller. The MCP bridge handles this correctly by passing `depth` through only when the host supplies it (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1070`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2164`). Suggested direction: default the SDK `depth` parameter to unset (omit the query parameter when the caller does not pass one) so the registry's configured default depth applies.

## F-4.6 — 4.6 Layers and Visibility

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.6 against the implementation._

I traced the §4.6 contracts for the layer list, source types, visibility evaluation, the config schema, collision handling, and the extends field-semantics table against `pkg/layer`, `pkg/manifest`, `pkg/registry/core`, `pkg/registry/ingest`, `pkg/registry/filesystem`, `pkg/registry/server`, and `internal/serverboot`. Most of the surface is implemented correctly. The visibility union evaluator honors `public`, `organization`, `groups`, and `users` with public-mode and filesystem-source short-circuits (`pkg/layer/composer.go:64`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1704`). The config schema field names match the spec exactly (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:147` through `:181`). The collision-at-ingest rule and the same-ID `extends:` overlay exception are enforced (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:620`, `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:64`). The full field-semantics merge table is implemented in `pkg/manifest/merge.go:28` (scalar child-wins, append-unique tags, append lists, most-restrictive sensitivity/sandbox/search_visibility, deep-merge mcpServers and runtime_requirements). Hidden-parent privacy is preserved: the server resolves and merges the parent bypassing visibility and strips `extends` from the served frontmatter, and `LoadArtifactResult` does not surface the parent ID (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1451`, `:1547`, `:1221`). The cross-type `extends:` rejection and the parent-version pinning fire in the server ingest path (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:608`, `:617`). The user-defined-layer implicit `users:[<registrant>]` visibility is set automatically and cannot be widened (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:536`, `:441`).

The findings below concern the runtime-registered layer class (the second of the three §4.6 layer classes), which is persisted but never composed into the read-path effective view in an authenticated deployment, the missing cross-type rejection on the filesystem-source materialization path, and the missing `license` change advisory.

### - [x] F-4.6.1 — Runtime-registered layers never enter the effective view in an authenticated deployment [High] — CLOSED

Resolution (b0033de): the core registry now resolves the per-request layer set from the store on every read (`Registry.resolveLayers`), composing admin-defined layers in config order below the caller's user-defined layers per the §4.6 composition order, instead of relying on the static boot-time slice. `visibleManifests`, `load_domain` (`mergedDomains`/`allowedLayers`), `search_domains`, the §3.5 scope preview, and the §4.7.2 admin diagnostic all use it; the boot-time slice remains the fallback only when the store carries no layer configs (the standalone filesystem path, which bypasses visibility in public mode). Covered by unit tests (`pkg/registry/core` owner-sees / others-hidden / composition-order) and an SQLite full-HTTP integration test.

(bug) §4.6 declares user-defined layers as a first-class class: "registered at runtime by individual users via the CLI/API (§7.3.1)" and states "Resolution of layers 1 and 2 happens at the registry on every `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` call" (spec/04-artifact-model.md:580, :589). The core registry holds a static admin layer list `layers []layer.Layer` set once at construction (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:55`, `:162`), and `visibleManifests` filters every read to manifests whose `m.Layer` is a member of that static list (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1707`-`:1717`). A layer registered at runtime via `POST /v1/layers` is persisted to the store as a `store.LayerConfig` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:643`) and its artifacts are ingested by the reingest runner under the layer's ID (`internal/serverboot/reingest.go:71`), but the registry's `r.layers` slice is never updated: `core.New` is invoked exactly twice, both with the boot-time layer list (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:297`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:710`), and the core package never reads `LayerConfig` rows from the store (no `ListLayerConfigs`/`GetLayerConfig` reference exists in `pkg/registry/core`). Consequently, in any deployment where the caller is authenticated rather than public (`IsAuthenticated: true`, `IsPublic` false, set at `internal/serverboot/identity_verify.go:39`) and at least one declared layer exists, `visibleManifests` drops every artifact contributed by a runtime-registered layer because that layer's ID is absent from `allowed`. The entire user-defined layer class, and any admin-defined layer registered via the API after boot, is invisible on the read path. The defect is masked in standalone/public mode only because `id.IsPublic` short-circuits layer filtering at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1704`. Suggested direction: have the registry resolve the per-request layer set (admin layers from config plus the caller's user-defined layers and any API-registered admin layers) from the store on each read, assigning user-defined layers precedence above admin layers in the user-controlled order, rather than relying on a static slice fixed at construction.

### - [x] F-4.6.2 — Filesystem-source extends resolution does not reject cross-type chains [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (b0033de): `mergeRecord` in `pkg/registry/filesystem/extends.go` now compares the child's `type:` against the resolved parent's and returns an `extends.type_mismatch` error before calling `MergeExtends`, mirroring the server ingest rejection. A cross-type chain therefore fails materialization rather than silently merging an incompatible parent. Covered by unit tests (different-ID and same-ID overlay), a `podium sync` integration test, and an e2e sync test, each asserting `extends.type_mismatch`.

(gap) §4.6 states "The child's `type:` must match the parent's; ingest rejects an `extends:` chain that crosses types" (spec/04-artifact-model.md:698). The server ingest path enforces this (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:608`: rejects with `ingest.invalid_artifact` when `parentType != rec.Artifact.Type`). The filesystem-source materialization path resolves and merges `extends:` chains through `resolveExtends`/`mergeRecord` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/extends.go:29`, `:75`) but performs no type comparison before calling `manifest.MergeExtends` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/extends.go:113`). Neither the lint rules nor the sync path supply a substitute check (no cross-type extends validation exists in `pkg/lint` or `pkg/sync`). A filesystem-source registry (§13.11) that declares a cross-type `extends:` chain therefore silently produces a merged artifact whose type is taken from the child while inheriting an incompatible parent's fields, instead of being rejected. Suggested direction: add a child-type-equals-parent-type check inside `mergeRecord` (or in `Walk` before `resolveExtends`) that returns an `extends.type_mismatch` error, mirroring the server ingest rejection at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:608`.

### - [x] F-4.6.3 — No lint warning when `license` changes across an extends chain [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (b0033de): `resolveExtendsPin` now also returns the resolved parent's license, and the ingest loop appends a `lint.license_changed_across_layers` warning advisory to `res.Advisories` when an extends child's license differs from the parent's (a child introducing a license over a parent with none is not flagged). The advisory is surfaced through the `/v1/layers/reingest` response and printed by `podium layer reingest` so the publisher sees the cross-layer change. Covered by ingest unit tests (changed / unchanged / introduced) and an SQLite two-layer reingest integration test.

(gap) The §4.6 field-semantics table specifies `license` as "Scalar; child wins (lint warning if changed across layers)" (spec/04-artifact-model.md:695). The merge applies child-wins correctly (`pkg/manifest/merge.go:43`), but no warning is emitted anywhere when the child's `license` differs from the parent's. The ingest advisory set is limited to description-quality rules (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:490`), and a repository search for a cross-layer license-change diagnostic in `pkg/manifest`, `pkg/registry/ingest`, `pkg/lint`, and `pkg/sync` returns nothing. The existing `license` lint in `pkg/lint/skill_rules.go:84` compares ARTIFACT.md against SKILL.md within a single artifact, not a parent against a child across layers. The parenthetical advisory the spec mandates is therefore absent. Suggested direction: emit an advisory (warning severity) during extends resolution when the resolved child `license` differs from the parent's, attaching it to the ingest `Advisories` set so the publisher sees the cross-layer change.

### - [x] F-4.6.4 — `users:` visibility matches on email in addition to OIDC subject [Info] — CLOSED

**Resolution (CLOSED):** Reconciled the spec wording with the shipped sub-or-email matching after the maintainer approved the spec edit. The §4.6 visibility table now reads "Listed user identifiers, matched against the caller's OIDC subject or email." (spec/04-artifact-model.md:609), matching the section's own config example and the evaluator at `pkg/layer/composer.go:94`. Also reconciled the `--user` flag help to "OIDC subject or email with visibility" (cmd/podium/layer.go), the visibility table and walkthrough in docs/getting-started/concepts.md, and the `identity-visibility-flow.svg` match label.
