The owner of user-defined layers stays canonical (OIDC subject) deliberately: `Owner` is the identity key for GDPR right-to-erasure (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:361`) and the per-owner layer cap (`:622`), where a single canonical identifier is required, so the sub-or-email widening is scoped to read-side visibility only. Behavior unchanged; pinned by `TestVisible_UsersMatchSubjectOrEmail`.

Deferred (b0033de): this is a spec self-contradiction, not a code defect. The §4.6 table says `users:` entries are "OIDC subject", but the same section's config example uses email-style identifiers (`users: [alice@acme.com]`); the evaluator follows the example by matching either the caller's `Sub` or `Email`, which is what makes the documented example functional. The finding's only remedy is to reconcile the table wording with the example, which is a read-only spec edit (ground rule A). No code change. The current dual-match behavior is pinned by a `pkg/layer` change-detector test (`TestVisible_UsersMatchSubjectOrEmail`) so a later subject-only narrowing, if the spec is reconciled that way, surfaces immediately.

(inconsistency) The §4.6 visibility table defines `users: [<user-id>, ...]` as "Listed user identifiers (OIDC subject)" (spec/04-artifact-model.md:609). The evaluator matches a configured user entry against either the caller's `Sub` or the caller's `Email` (`pkg/layer/composer.go:93`-`:97`). This broadens the table's stated "OIDC subject" matching to also accept email-style identifiers. The code comment justifies it by pointing at the spec's own config example, which uses email-style IDs (`users: [alice@acme.com]`, spec/04-artifact-model.md:665), so the example and the table text disagree and the implementation follows the example. This is an observation to confirm rather than a defect: matching email widens, not narrows, the grant, and the spec's example would not match a subject-only evaluator. Suggested direction: reconcile the §4.6 table wording with the config example so the matched identity attribute is stated unambiguously, then confirm the evaluator matches exactly that attribute.

## F-4.7 — 4.7 Registry as a Service (4.7.1 Tenancy/Residency, 4.7.2 Access Control, 4.7.3 Reverse Dep Index, 4.7.4 Classification/Lifecycle, 4.7.5 Audit, 4.7.6 Version Resolution, 4.7.7 Vuln Tracking out-of-scope, 4.7.8 Quotas, 4.7.9 Signing)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md §4.7 against the implementation._

I traced every concrete claim in §4.7 and its sub-subsections to the Go implementation. The bulk of the section is satisfied. The version-immutability invariant rejects a same-version re-ingest with a different content hash and emits `layer.history_rewritten` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:648-667`, `pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:123-135`). The §4.7.6 pinning grammar (`<id>`, `@<semver>`, `@<semver>.x`, `@sha256:<hash>`) parses correctly and `latest` orders by ingest time excluding deprecated versions (`pkg/version/version.go:53-103`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1390-1410`); session-consistent `latest` is recorded and reused per `session_id` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1382-1418`); the content hash is SHA-256 over the canonicalized manifest plus bundled resources in sorted-path order (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1138-1153`); `extends:` resolves to a hard pin at the child's ingest time (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:592-617`). The reverse-dependency index records `extends`, `delegates_to`, and `mcpServers` edges with `mcpServers` resolved via `server_identifier` (`pkg/dependency/graph.go:12-16`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1160-1233`) and feeds both impact analysis (`pkg/dependency/graph.go:63-86`) and search ranking (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1085-1096`). §4.7.4 classification and lifecycle surface sensitivity in search and load, exclude deprecated artifacts from default search, and attach a deprecation warning with the `replaced_by` upgrade target (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1037`, `1110-1113`, `1659-1668`; `pkg/registry/server/server.go:489-491`, `869`). §4.7.5 logs all four read calls with caller, resolved layer composition, and result size (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1000-1009`, `domain_search.go:57-65`, `core.go:460-473`), plus admin and break-glass events. §4.7.8 quotas define all four limit types (`pkg/store/store.go:70-82`), enforce storage at ingest and search-QPS/materialize-rate via token buckets (`pkg/registry/server/rate_limit.go`), and enforce the per-UTC-day audit-volume cap that refuses ingest writes with `quota.audit_volume_exceeded` (`pkg/registry/server/audit_volume.go`, `internal/serverboot/reingest.go:39-41`). §4.7.9 signing verifies signatures at materialization for sensitivity ≥ medium by default and aborts with `materialize.signature_invalid`, and exposes `podium sign`/`podium verify` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1298-1300`, `1690-1701`; `cmd/podium/sign.go`). §4.7.7 vulnerability tracking is correctly absent: the SBOM manifest field is opaque and no parsing, scoring, or `vulnerability.detected` emission exists (`pkg/manifest/types.go:192-197`).

The findings below concern §4.7.1's mandated Postgres isolation model, the §4.7.2 admin diagnostic-view capability, the §4.7.1 org-ID format, and the §4.7.3 `delegates_to` target-type constraint.

### - [ ] F-4.7.1 — Postgres isolation uses a tenant_id column rather than schema-per-org with row-level security [Medium] — DEFERRED

(inconsistency) §4.7.1 mandates a specific Postgres isolation model at `spec/04-artifact-model.md:778`: "Each org has its own schema; cross-org tables (e.g., shared infrastructure metadata) use row-level security with org_id checks. Schema-per-org gives clean drop-org semantics, isolates query patterns, and bounds the blast radius of SQL injection." The Postgres store instead creates a single set of shared tables keyed by a `tenant_id` or `org_id` text column and scopes every query with a `WHERE tenant_id = ...` clause (`pkg/store/postgres.go:78-174`, where `tenants`, `manifests`, `domains`, `dependencies`, and `admin_grants` are flat tables with `tenant_id`/`org_id` columns and composite primary keys). There is no `CREATE SCHEMA`, no `SET search_path`, no `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY`, and no `CREATE POLICY` anywhere in the store layer; a grep across `pkg/store/*.go` and `internal/serverboot/*.go` for those constructs returns nothing. The deployment runs a single fixed tenant (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:636` sets `tenantID = "default"`), so the practical blast radius is limited today, but the implementation diverges from the spec-mandated architecture, including the SQL-injection-containment property the spec calls out. Suggested direction: either implement schema-per-org provisioning plus row-level-security policies on shared tables in `pkg/store/postgres.go`, or amend §4.7.1 to describe the `tenant_id`-column isolation the code actually provides.

**Resolution (DEFERRED):** Spec amendment is off the table (read-only). A faithful fix is a large rearchitecture of the 875-line `pkg/store/postgres.go` (per-org `CREATE SCHEMA` + search-path management on every query, plus `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY`/`CREATE POLICY` with a non-owner role and per-request `SET LOCAL` session vars on the shared tables) whose correctness cannot be verified in this environment: no Postgres is reachable (`PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN` unset, `psql`/`pg_ctl` absent, docker daemon down, no cached image), and the storetest Postgres suite (`pkg/store/postgres_test.go`) skips without a DSN. `go build` does not validate SQL strings, so committing an unrunnable schema/RLS rewrite would violate ground rules D and E (never commit unverified code; tests must fail-without/pass-with). The `tenant_id`-column isolation is functionally correct for the single-tenant `default` deployment; the divergence is architectural and bounded today. Not unblocked by this batch (the blocker is the absent Postgres test environment).

### - [x] F-4.7.2 — Admin "view any layer's contents for diagnostic purposes" override is not implemented on the read path [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.7.2 lists as an admin capability at `spec/04-artifact-model.md:795`: "View any layer's contents for diagnostic purposes (override visibility; the override is itself audited)." No read path lets an admin see artifacts in a layer their own identity cannot otherwise see. `handleLoadArtifact` resolves the caller with `s.identity(r)` and passes it straight to `core.LoadArtifact` with no admin override parameter or header (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:818-827`); `handleSearchArtifacts` does the same (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:818` is the load path; the search path at `server.go:676-677` likewise uses the unmodified identity). The only admin-scoped diagnostic endpoint is `handleAdminShowEffective`, which returns the per-layer visibility configuration for a target user, not the layer contents (`pkg/registry/server/admin.go:80-112`). A grep for an admin visibility bypass across `pkg/layer/scope.go`, `pkg/layer/composer.go`, and `pkg/registry/core/effective_view.go` returns nothing, and `pkg/registry/core/admin.go` exposes only `AdminAuthorize`, `GrantAdmin`, and `RevokeAdmin`. Because the override does not exist, the spec's "the override is itself audited" requirement is also unmet. Suggested direction: add an admin-gated visibility-override option to the read handlers (for example an `?as_admin=1` parameter that requires `requireAdmin` and emits a dedicated audit event) so admins can diagnose layer contents and the override is recorded.

**Resolution (CLOSED, commit `870df1c`):** Added `AsAdmin` to `LoadArtifactOptions`/`SearchArtifactsOptions` and a `Registry.adminVisibleManifests` helper (`pkg/registry/core/core.go`) that re-checks `AdminAuthorize` (rejecting non-admin and public-mode callers with `ErrForbidden`), emits the new `admin.visibility_override` audit event (`pkg/audit/audit.go`), then returns the tenant's manifests bypassing per-layer visibility (OAuth read scopes still apply). `handleLoadArtifact`/`handleSearchArtifacts` parse `as_admin=1`, gate it with `requireAdmin` (403 `auth.forbidden`), and thread the flag; `writeCoreError` now maps `ErrForbidden` to 403. Tests: 8 core unit (`admin_override_test.go`), 1 integration (`admin_visibility_override_test.go`), 1 e2e (`admin_visibility_override_test.go`, injected-session-token admin over a bob-only declared layer). Fail-without-change verified at the core unit level.

### - [x] F-4.7.3 — Org IDs are not UUIDs [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.7.1 states at `spec/04-artifact-model.md:774`: "Org IDs are UUIDs; org names are human-readable aliases." The bootstrapped tenant ID is the literal string `"default"`, used as both the org ID and the org name (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:636-639`, where `const tenantID = "default"` is passed as the tenant `ID` and `Name`). Nothing validates or generates a UUID for the org ID, and the store treats `tenant_id`/`org_id` as an opaque text column (`pkg/store/postgres.go:79`, `133`). In the current single-tenant deployment this is cosmetic, but it diverges from the stated UUID-versus-alias distinction. Suggested direction: generate a UUID org ID at bootstrap and keep `"default"` as the human-readable name, or relax the §4.7.1 wording to allow opaque string org IDs.

**Resolution (CLOSED, commit `870df1c`):** Bootstrap now generates a UUID org ID while keeping `"default"` as the human-readable name. Added `internal/serverboot/orgid.go`: `orgIDForName` derives a name-based UUIDv5 (`uuid.NewSHA1(uuid.NameSpaceURL, "podium:org:"+name)`) so the ID is a UUID per §4.7.1 yet stable across restarts (a random UUID per boot would orphan persisted tenant-scoped rows), and `bootstrapDefaultTenant` creates the org with that ID and `Name: "default"`. `serverboot.go` replaces the inline `const tenantID = "default"` with this helper and threads the returned UUID as the org everywhere. Tests: 3 serverboot unit (`orgid_test.go`: UUID-and-name, stable-and-distinct, idempotent); the real-binary boot e2e (`TestAdminVisibilityOverride_E2E` with `PODIUM_BOOTSTRAP_ADMINS`, declared-layers boot) confirms bootstrap-admin and ingest wiring stays consistent under the UUID tenant.

### - [ ] F-4.7.4 — `delegates_to:` targets are not constrained to agent-type artifacts at ingest [Low] — DEFERRED

(gap) §4.7.3 describes the dependency edges at `spec/04-artifact-model.md:817`: "`delegates_to:` references (constrained to `agent`-type targets)." The edge builder records a `delegates_to` edge for every entry in `a.DelegatesTo` without checking that the resolved target is an `agent`-type artifact (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1167-1170`), in contrast to the sibling `mcpServers` handling, which only emits an edge when the reference resolves to an `mcp-server`-type artifact (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1179-1191`). No lint rule or ingest validation rejects a `delegates_to:` pointing at a non-agent target; a grep for `delegates` across `pkg/lint` and the ingest pipeline finds only the edge construction and an unrelated harness-capability comment. The spec phrasing is parenthetical and may be describing delegation semantics rather than mandating ingest-time rejection, so this is reported at Low. Suggested direction: confirm whether §4.7.3 intends an enforced constraint; if so, validate the resolved target type for `delegates_to` references at ingest (mirroring the `mcpServers` type check) and reject a cross-type delegation, otherwise leave the index as-is and note that the constraint is advisory.

**Resolution (DEFERRED):** The constraint is advisory; enforcing it at ingest contradicts the authored docs and the doc-derived conformance suite. `docs/authoring/your-first-agent.md` has an `agent` delegating to a `skill` (`conventional-commits`), and `TestAgentTutorial_DelegatesEdgeIndexed`/`TestAgentTutorial_ImpactListsDependent` (T-D-first-agent-13/14, real server ingest) require that agent→skill `delegates_to` edge to ingest **and** be surfaced by `/v1/dependents` and `podium impact`; `TestArtifactTypes_DelegatesToTypeNotEnforcedAtLint` (T-D-artifact-types-37) and `TestAgentTutorial_UnresolvedDelegateDoesNotBlockSync` (T-D-first-agent-25) require lint not to reject it. Both enforcement readings break these: rejecting at ingest fails the edge tests; filtering to agent-only targets (mirroring `mcpServers`) drops the edge so `/v1/dependents` returns nothing. This is a genuine spec-vs-docs contradiction (§4.7.3's parenthetical vs the authoring docs the conformance suite encodes), mirroring the already-deferred F-4.3.4. Per ground rule A, deferred pending a read-only spec decision; the current record-all-edges behavior is what the docs require. No code change. Not unblocked by this batch.

## F-5.0 — 5.0 Why Tools, Not Resources

_Reviewed spec/05-meta-tools.md §5.0 against the implementation._

Section 5.0 (`spec/05-meta-tools.md:18`) is short and makes one concrete, checkable contract on top of conceptual prose. The conceptual claim is that the meta-tools, rather than MCP resources, are the canonical interface because the catalog needs parameterized navigation and lazy materialization with side effects. The checkable claim at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:22` is that artifact bodies are also exposed as MCP resources, a read-only mirror of `load_artifact`, which ties back to the `resources` capability declared at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:14`. The implementation satisfies this. The MCP bridge advertises the `resources` capability in its `initialize` response at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:984-988`, routes `resources/list` and `resources/read` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1008-1013`, and implements both handlers in `cmd/podium-mcp/resources.go`. The read path returns the manifest content (`resp.Frontmatter + resp.ManifestBody`) at `cmd/podium-mcp/resources.go:98` and performs none of `load_artifact`'s filesystem materialization, which is the exact concatenation the `load_artifact` tool itself returns at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1896`, so the mirror is faithful. The list path enumerates the caller's effective view and filters out `mcp-server` artifacts at `cmd/podium-mcp/resources.go:53`, matching the bridge's tool-result behavior. The behavior is covered by tests in `cmd/podium-mcp/resources_test.go`.

The only deviation I can substantiate is a representation mismatch in the advertised capability value, recorded below as an informal-illustration discrepancy.

### - [x] F-5.0.1 — `resources` capability advertised as object, spec writes `true` [Info] — CLOSED

**Resolution (CLOSED):** Reconciled the spec illustration with the protocol-correct wire form after the maintainer approved the spec edit. `spec/05-meta-tools.md:14` now documents the `initialize` capability set as `{tools: {}, resources: {}, sessionCorrelation: true}`, matching what the bridge emits (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1125-1128`), with a note that `tools`/`resources` are MCP capability objects (`{}` = present with no optional sub-features like `listChanged`/`subscribe`) and `sessionCorrelation` is a Podium extension carried as a literal boolean. No code change; emitting `resources: true` to match the old wording would have violated the MCP schema. The mirror is pinned by `cmd/podium-mcp/load_artifact_test.go` and the e2e `artifact_response_test.go`.

(inconsistency) The capability declaration that §5.0 references writes the capability set as `{tools: true, resources: true, sessionCorrelation: true}` at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:14`, where the `resources` capability is the one that backs the §5.0 read-only mirror. The implementation emits this capability as an empty object rather than the boolean `true`: `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:984-988` builds `caps` with `"tools": map[string]any{}`, `"resources": map[string]any{}`, and `"sessionCorrelation": true`. The MCP protocol models capability values as objects, so `{}` is the protocol-correct representation while the spec's `true` is informal shorthand for "present"; the same shorthand applies to the `tools` entry, which the code also emits as `{}`. The mirror itself works, so this is a wire-representation difference in an informal spec illustration rather than a functional defect. Suggested direction: leave the code as the protocol-correct object form and adjust the spec line at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:14` to show the object representation (or note that `true` denotes capability presence) so the documented `initialize` response matches what the bridge emits.

DEFERRED: the code is already protocol-correct. MCP models `tools` and `resources` as capability objects, so the emitted `{}` is the standard representation and the spec's `true` is informal shorthand for "capability present" (the same line already emits the Podium-specific `sessionCorrelation` as a literal boolean, which the code matches). Emitting `resources: true` to match the spec literally would violate the MCP protocol. The resource mirror works (verified by `cmd/podium-mcp/resources_test.go` and the e2e mirror test). The only remediation is editing the spec illustration at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:14`, which is read-only under this batch's ground rules. No code defect.

## F-5.1 — 5.1 Meta-Tool Descriptions and Prompting Guidance

_Reviewed spec/05-meta-tools.md §5.1 against the implementation._

§5.1 states that the four meta-tool description strings are canonical and that hosts should emit them verbatim, names the optional arguments each tool accepts (`load_domain.depth`, `search_artifacts.top_k` with default 10 and max 50, etc.), specifies the response fields each tool surfaces (the `note` field, `total_matched`, the `search_domains` descriptor fields, and the `load_artifact` `materialized_at` paths), and gives an example system-prompt fragment. The canonical strings are carried verbatim in `cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go`: a byte-for-byte comparison of the four constants `descLoadDomain`, `descSearchDomains`, `descSearchArtifacts`, and `descLoadArtifact` (`cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:11`, `:14`, `:17`, `:20`) against the spec blockquotes at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:30`, `:34`, `:38`, and `:42` matches exactly, and the `systemPromptFragment` constant (`cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:26`) matches the spec example at `spec/05-meta-tools.md:47`. The descriptions are wired into the MCP `tools/list` result through `metaToolDescriptors()` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1004`) and the fragment is surfaced through the `initialize` result's `instructions` field (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:998`).

The advertised argument and response contracts hold end to end. `search_artifacts` returns `total_matched` and honors a `top_k` default of 10 (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:36`, `:182`), and the registry rejects `top_k > 50` with `ErrInvalidArgument` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1010`). `load_domain` accepts `depth` and emits the `note` field (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:609`, `:399`, `:618`). The `search_domains` descriptor carries the documented `path`, `name`, `description`, `keywords`, and `score` fields (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:407`). One defect surfaced in the `load_artifact` `materialized_at` contract.

### - [x] F-5.1.1 — `materialized_at` paths are not absolutized when the configured root is relative [Medium] — CLOSED

(bug) §5.1 states that `load_artifact` returns `materialized_at` paths and that "The returned `materialized_at` paths are absolute and ready to use" (`spec/05-meta-tools.md:42`). In the MCP bridge the materialization root is taken directly from the per-call `destination` argument or the `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` environment variable with no normalization: `destFromArgs` returns the raw argument string (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1277`), `materializeRoot` is set straight from `os.Getenv` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:232`) and from the config value (`cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:112`), and the returned paths are then built as `filepath.Join(root, filepath.FromSlash(f.Path))` against that unmodified `root` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1402` and the overlay path at `:1613`). No `filepath.Abs` is applied to `root` anywhere in `cmd/podium-mcp`. The on-disk write does absolutize internally (`materialize.Write` calls `filepath.Abs(destination)` at `pkg/materialize/atomic.go:209`), so the files land at the correct absolute location, but the `materialized_at` values reported to the host are whatever `filepath.Join` produces from the supplied root: relative when the root is relative. The sandbox-profile entry, by contrast, is always absolute because `WriteSandboxProfile` returns a path built from the absolutized destination (`pkg/materialize/seccomp.go:59`, `:71`), so a single response can mix relative file entries with an absolute sandbox-profile entry. A host that resolves the returned relative paths against its own working directory, which differs from the MCP server process working directory, will point at the wrong location, so the paths are not "ready to use" as the spec requires. Suggested direction: absolutize the materialization root once with `filepath.Abs` before computing the `materialized_at` entries (or absolutize each joined path), so every returned path is absolute regardless of whether the caller supplied a relative `destination` or `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT`.

Resolution (commit 0d95ffd): the bridge now absolutizes the materialization root via `absMaterializeRoot` (`filepath.Abs`) before computing `materialized_at` in both the registry-served (`deliverLoadArtifact`) and overlay (`loadArtifactFromOverlay`) paths (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`), so every returned file entry is absolute regardless of whether the caller supplied a relative `destination` or `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT`. Tests: 2 podium-mcp unit (relative-dest delivery returns absolute paths, `absMaterializeRoot` empty/relative/absolute cases).

## F-5.2 — 5.2 Command Materialization

_Reviewed spec/05-meta-tools.md §5.2 against the implementation._

Section 5.2 makes a small set of checkable claims about `type: command` artifacts. Commands are not projected through MCP, both `podium sync` and the MCP server materialize a command into the target harness's native command location and format (§6.7), Podium adds no argument layer of its own, and the `mcpServers:` declarations are stored by Podium and exposed via `load_artifact` for the host runtime to wire up. Each claim traces to code that satisfies it.

The "no MCP projection" claim holds. The MCP server advertises only `tools` (the meta-tools), `resources`, and `sessionCorrelation` capabilities and explicitly omits a `prompts` capability for commands (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:984` with the rationale comment at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:981`). The `tools/list` handler returns a fixed meta-tool set from `metaToolDescriptors()` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1004`, defined in `cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:45`), and the JSON-RPC method switch has no `prompts/list` or `prompts/get` case (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1000`-`1015`). The "both paths materialize commands into native locations" claim holds: the MCP server runs the artifact through the configured harness adapter at load time (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1378`), and `podium sync` runs the same adapter pipeline (`pkg/sync/sync.go:229`). The adapters route `type: command` to native command files, for example `.claude/commands/<name>.md` (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:82`-`87`), `.cursor/commands/<name>.md` (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go:62`-`63`), `.gemini/commands/<name>.toml` (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go:138`-`139`), and `.opencode/commands/<name>.md` (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go:167`-`168`). The "no argument layer" claim holds: the command body is written through verbatim, with only provenance rewriting for Claude (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:85`) and a passthrough of `art.Body` into the Gemini `prompt` TOML field with no Podium substitution (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:94`-`101`). The `mcpServers:` storage and exposure claim holds: the field is parsed and preserved on the manifest (`pkg/manifest/types.go:124`, `pkg/manifest/types.go:169`-`176`) and the full frontmatter that carries it is returned in the registry `load_artifact` response (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:469`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:863`) and consumed by the MCP bridge (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1551`). Codex returns no output for commands (`pkg/adapter/codex.go:34`-`35`), which matches the §6.7.1 capability matrix marking the codex cell unsupported for the `command` type (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:86`), so this is governed behavior rather than a §5.2 gap.

No findings.

## F-6.1 — 6.1 The Bridge

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.1 against the implementation._

Section 6.1 describes the Podium MCP server as a thin in-process bridge that exposes the meta-tools over MCP, forwards calls to the registry over HTTP, holds no per-session server-side state, keeps local state limited to a content-addressed disk cache, OS-keychain-stored credentials in `oauth-device-code` mode, an in-memory local-overlay index, and the materialized working set on disk, shares no state across processes, ships as a single Go binary configured via env vars, command-line flags, or a config file, and requires a server-source registry because it speaks HTTP and does not work against a filesystem-source registry. These are mostly architectural assertions; the concrete checkable contracts are the meta-tool exposure, the HTTP forwarding, the local-state inventory, the configuration surface, and the server-source requirement.

Every checkable claim holds in the current code. The bridge advertises the meta-tools through `tools/list` returning `metaToolDescriptors()` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1000-1004`) and forwards calls to the registry over HTTP through `newRegistryRequest`, which parses `s.cfg.registry + path` and issues an `http.NewRequestWithContext` with the credential, tenant, and session headers attached (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1903-1950`). The per-process `mcpServer` struct holds exactly the local state the spec enumerates: the disk content cache, the keychain `TokenStore`, the in-memory overlay records, and the materialized output paths (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:380-454`), and the keychain is consulted only in `oauth-device-code` mode through `deviceCodeToken` (`cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:35-77`). Configuration accepts env vars, command-line flags, and a config file with the documented `flag > config file > env > default` precedence (`cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:25-44`). The server-source requirement is enforced at startup: when `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is not an `http://` or `https://` URL, `synccfg.IsServerSource` returns false and `loadConfig` refuses to start with the `config.filesystem_registry_unsupported` error (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:303-304`, `pkg/sync/config.go:115-122`).

No findings.

## F-6.2 — 6.2 Configuration

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.2 against the implementation._

I checked every parameter in the §6.2 configuration table (spec/06-mcp-server.md:13-28) against the MCP bridge configuration loader and the registry-server boot path. The MCP bridge reads its parameters in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` `loadConfig` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:217-359), and applies flag and config-file overlays in `cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go` (cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:25-134). All ten env-var names in the table appear verbatim in non-test source. The documented defaults are correct: `PODIUM_HARNESS` defaults to `none` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:224), `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` to `always-revalidate` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:227), `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` to `oauth-device-code` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:241), `PODIUM_CACHE_DIR` to `~/.podium/cache` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:318-321), `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` to 3600 via `objectstore.DefaultPresignTTL` (pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:71, internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1636-1637), and the `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES` default resolves to `medium-and-above` when no env, flag, config, or sync.yaml value is present (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:311-316).

The `PODIUM_REGISTRY` unset behavior matches the table note: the loader falls back to `sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry` and otherwise fails with `config.no_registry` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:287-296). `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` unset disables the overlay (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:513-524). `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` is used as the default destination with the per-call destination taking precedence (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1341-1344). `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` distinguishes unset (registry-only) from set-but-empty or `default` (writes `~/.podium/audit.log`) using `LookupEnv` and `newAuditSink` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:269-271, 565-581; pkg/audit/file.go:33-39). The bridge accepts `--flag` and config-file equivalents for every bridge-side parameter through `applyConfigKV` (cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:97-134), and invalid values for `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE`, `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES`, `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`, and `PODIUM_HARNESS` are rejected at startup (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:330-357). One narrow deviation surfaced around the flag and config-file forms for `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS`.

### - [x] F-6.2.1 — `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` has no `--flag` or config-file form [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 2db2f42): `podium serve` now accepts `--presign-ttl-seconds`, which sets `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` (the value serverboot reads); the config-file form already exists as the registry.yaml `object_store.presign_ttl_seconds` key added under F-13.12.1, so the §6.2 "flag and config-file equivalents are accepted" claim now holds for this parameter on the registry server that reads it. Precedence is flag/env over the config file. Tests: 2 cmd/podium serve units (flag sets env; omitted flag preserves env); config-file form covered by the existing internal/serverboot registry_config_keys units.

(inconsistency) The §6.2 table header states that for every listed parameter "`--flag` and config-file equivalents are accepted" (spec/06-mcp-server.md:13), and `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` is one of the listed parameters (spec/06-mcp-server.md:25). In the implementation this parameter is read only from the environment by the registry-server boot path (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1631-1634), and the MCP bridge never consults it at all. There is no `--flag` parser entry or config-file key for it: the bridge's `applyConfigKV` does not recognize any `presign-ttl` key (cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:97-134), and a repository-wide search for `presign-ttl`, `presign_ttl`, or `PresignTTLSeconds` outside `serverboot.go`'s env read returns nothing. As a result the only configuration path for the presigned-URL TTL is the environment variable, which contradicts the table's blanket claim that flag and config-file forms exist. The deviation is narrow because presigning is a registry-server concern and the documented env-var default of 3600 is honored correctly. Suggested direction: either add a `--presign-ttl-seconds` flag and config-file key to the registry server, or amend the §6.2 table note to scope the flag and config-file equivalence claim to the bridge-side parameters and mark `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` as a registry-server, env-only override.

## F-6.3 — 6.3 Identity Providers (6.3.1 Claim Derivation, 6.3.2 injected-session-token Runtime Trust, 6.3.2.1 Token Rotation Contract)

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.3 against the implementation._

I reviewed the two built-in identity providers, the claim-derivation rules, the `injected-session-token` runtime trust model, and the token rotation contract. The bulk of the section is implemented. The `injected-session-token` verifier parses the JWT, looks up the runtime by `iss`, enforces a registered signing key with the registered algorithm, and rejects an unregistered issuer with `auth.untrusted_runtime` (`pkg/identity/runtime.go:150-182`). The required `exp`, `sub`, and `act` claims are enforced (`pkg/identity/runtime.go:160`, `pkg/identity/runtime.go:192-198`), and an `act` that does not name the verified runtime is rejected (`pkg/identity/runtime.go:230-255`). The server installs the per-request verifier and maps failures to the §6.10 envelope with `details.runtime_iss` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:906-911`, `pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:78-93`). The MCP bridge reads the token fresh on every call from the file then the env var (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2229-2249`), and the rotation watcher honors SIGHUP and a file change (`cmd/podium-mcp/token_watch.go:35-82`). The `oauth-device-code` flow, its options (`PODIUM_OAUTH_AUDIENCE`, `PODIUM_OAUTH_AUTHORIZATION_ENDPOINT`, `PODIUM_TOKEN_KEYCHAIN_NAME`), the OS-keychain cache, transparent refresh, the 10-minute login timeout, and `--no-browser` are all present (`pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go`, `cmd/podium/login.go:24,39`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:239-246`). The §6.3.1 `IdpGroupMapping` adapter and fine-grained scope claims are implemented and applied (`pkg/identity/group_mapping.go`, `pkg/identity/runtime.go:217-280`, `internal/serverboot/identity_verify.go:29-40`).

The findings concern the `aud` required claim, which is not enforced unless an audience is configured, plus the rotation watch mechanism, the missing `--json` device-code event, and the Windows browser-open command.

### - [x] F-6.3.1 — `aud` required claim not enforced when no audience configured [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §6.3.2 lists `aud` ("registry endpoint") among the "Required claims" the registry verifies on every `injected-session-token` call (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:56-62`). The verifier only adds the audience check when the configured audience string is non-empty: `if audience != "" { opts = append(opts, jwt.WithAudience(audience)) }` (`pkg/identity/runtime.go:162-164`), and it performs no independent presence check for `aud`. The audience is sourced from `PODIUM_OAUTH_AUDIENCE` with no default (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1452`), so a deployment that does not set that variable accepts a runtime-signed token regardless of its `aud` claim, including a token whose `aud` is absent or names a different registry endpoint. Because runtime signing keys are shared trust anchors, the unvalidated `aud` is a cross-registry token-confusion surface, and `aud` is the only one of the section's required claims (`iss`, `aud`, `sub`, `act`, `exp`) that the verifier leaves optional. Suggested direction: require the `aud` claim to be present on every injected token and validate it against the configured registry endpoint, failing closed (refuse to start, or reject the token) when the audience is unconfigured, so the spec's "Required claims" set is enforced as stated.

Resolution (commit 457f560): the `JWTVerifier` now fails closed when the audience is unconfigured, rejecting every token with `auth.untrusted_runtime` rather than skipping the `aud` check; with the audience set, `jwt.WithAudience` already requires `aud` to be present and to match (`pkg/identity/runtime.go`). A boot guard `injectedTokenAudienceGuard` refuses to start `injected-session-token` mode without `PODIUM_OAUTH_AUDIENCE`, exiting with `config.injected_token_audience_unset` (`internal/serverboot/identity_verify.go`, wired in `serverboot.go`). Tests: 2 identity unit, 1 serverboot guard unit, 1 integration (missing-`aud` 401), 2 e2e (missing-`aud` 401, boot refusal).

### - [x] F-6.3.2 — `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` watched by stat-poll instead of fsnotify [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §6.3.2.1 states that `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` "is watched via fsnotify and re-read on change" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:70`). The implementation watches the file with a one-second `time.Ticker` that stat-polls the modification time rather than with fsnotify: `const tokenWatchInterval = time.Second` and the `os.Stat` mtime comparison in `watchLoop` (`cmd/podium-mcp/token_watch.go:14`, `cmd/podium-mcp/token_watch.go:69-77`). The repository already depends on fsnotify and uses it elsewhere (`pkg/sync/watch_fsnotify.go:28`). The behavioral contract of re-reading after a change is met, with up to roughly one second of latency, but the named mechanism differs from the spec. Suggested direction: either switch the file watch to fsnotify to match §6.3.2.1, or update the spec text to describe the poll-based watch the implementation uses, consistent with the §6.4 note that already records this substitution.

Resolution (commit 457f560): the token watch now uses fsnotify rather than a stat-poll ticker (`cmd/podium-mcp/token_watch.go`). The watcher observes the token file's parent directory so an atomic rename-replace rotation is still seen; `watchLoop` acts only on events whose basename matches the watched file, alongside the unchanged SIGHUP forced re-read and per-call fresh read. If fsnotify cannot initialize, the file watch is skipped and SIGHUP plus the per-call read remain the rotation path. Tests: 4 podium-mcp unit (synthetic event, unrelated-file ignore, SIGHUP, real-fsnotify reload).

### - [x] F-6.3.3 — `--json` device-code prompt and `auth.device_code_pending` event absent [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) §6.3 states that for CLI commands the device-code "Output is suppressed under `--json`; the prompt is replaced with a structured `auth.device_code_pending` event emitted on stderr" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:38`). The only command that runs the interactive device-code flow is `podium login`, which prints the verification URL and user code to stderr unconditionally and exposes no `--json` flag (`cmd/podium/login.go:31-40`, `cmd/podium/login.go:98-106`). No code path emits an `auth.device_code_pending` event; the string appears only in a doc comment and the matrix fixture, never as an emitted stderr event (`pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:79`, `tools/matrix/matrices.go:84`). `podium sync` accepts `--json` but does not run the device flow; it relies on a pre-cached token from `podium login` (`cmd/podium/main.go:200`, `cmd/podium/main.go:314`). The structured machine-readable variant of the device-code prompt described by the spec is therefore unimplemented. Suggested direction: add a `--json` flag to `podium login` (and any future inline-auth CLI path) that suppresses the human prompt and emits an `auth.device_code_pending` event with the URL and code on stderr.

Resolution (commit 457f560): `podium login` gained a `--json` flag that suppresses the human prompt and success chatter and emits an `auth.device_code_pending` §6.10 envelope on stderr carrying `verification_uri`, `user_code`, and `verification_uri_complete` (`cmd/podium/login.go`). Tests: 1 podium unit (envelope shape and the omitted complete-URL case), 1 e2e (prompt suppressed and event present via the OIDC stub).

### - [x] F-6.3.4 — Windows browser open uses `rundll32` rather than `start` [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §6.3 says CLI commands "attempt to open the URL in the system browser (via `open` on macOS, `xdg-open` on Linux, `start` on Windows)" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:38`). The login command opens the URL on Windows with `exec.Command("rundll32", "url.dll,FileProtocolHandler", url)` rather than the spec-named `start` (`cmd/podium/login.go:221-222`); macOS uses `open` and Linux uses `xdg-open` as specified (`cmd/podium/login.go:219-224`). Both Windows mechanisms open the URL, so this is a naming divergence with no behavioral loss. Suggested direction: align the Windows path with the spec by invoking `start` (for example `cmd /c start <url>`), or update §6.3 to name the `rundll32` mechanism the code uses.

Resolution (commit 457f560): the Windows browser open now invokes the spec-named `start` builtin as `cmd /c start "" <url>` rather than `rundll32`; the empty title placeholder keeps a URL containing `&` or spaces from being read as the window title (`cmd/podium/login.go`, via the extracted `browserCommand(goos, url)`). Tests: 1 podium unit asserting the per-OS argv for darwin, linux, windows, and the empty-URL no-op.

## F-6.4 — 6.4 Workspace Local Overlay (6.4.1 Local Search Index)

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.4 against the implementation._

I traced the §6.4 path-resolution order, watch behavior, format and merge claims, and the §6.4.1 local-search-index contract through `pkg/overlay`, `cmd/podium-mcp`, `pkg/sync`, and the Python and TypeScript SDKs. Most of the concrete claims hold. The path-resolution order is implemented faithfully: the env var and the explicit `Client(overlay_path=...)` precedence appear in `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:64` and `sdks/podium-py/podium/_overlay.py:25`, the MCP server resolves `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` from the host's `roots/list` reply in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:877` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:912`, and `podium sync` and the SDKs apply the `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` fallback in `cmd/podium/main.go:309` and `sdks/podium-py/podium/_overlay.py:37`. The §6.4.1 BM25 index, the registry plus local fan-out, and the reciprocal-rank fusion are present and consistent with the registry's BM25 (`k1=1.5`, `b=0.75`) and RRF (`k=60`) constants: see `cmd/podium-mcp/local_search.go:165`, `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:67`, and `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:191` against `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1884` and `pkg/registry/core/rrf.go:20`. The default is BM25-only and the optional semantic stream degrades to BM25 on any backend error (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:61`, `cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go:149`). The SDK reads the overlay per call and caches it per `session_id` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:433`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:438`).

The findings below are: the MCP overlay watcher polls rather than using fsnotify as the spec names; the §6.4.1 semantic backend cannot be pointed at pgvector or the managed services the spec lists; overlay `DOMAIN.md` files are never read by any overlay consumer; and the SDK overlay search ignores the `scope` filter.

### - [x] F-6.4.1 — Overlay semantic backend cannot select pgvector or managed services [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit c808db3): extracted the built-in vector-backend switch into a shared `vector.OpenBuiltin(id, vector.BackendConfig, dim)` factory (`pkg/vector/builtin.go`), used by both `internal/serverboot.openVectorBackend` and the overlay path. `mcpOverlayVectorBackend` (`cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go`) now builds a `BackendConfig` from the same env vars the registry uses (`PODIUM_PGVECTOR_DSN`/`PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN`, `PODIUM_PINECONE_*`, `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_*`, `PODIUM_QDRANT_*`) and delegates to `OpenBuiltin`, so `pgvector`, `pinecone`, `weaviate-cloud`, and `qdrant-cloud` are reachable for the workspace overlay per §6.4.1 instead of returning `unsupported overlay vector backend`. Tests: 12 unit (`OpenBuiltin` dispatch + DSN-error naming in `pkg/vector`; `mcpOverlayVectorBackend` reaches every documented backend in `cmd/podium-mcp`). serverboot e2e (`TestVectorBackend*`) still green.

(gap) §6.4.1 states the operator can configure the overlay's `LocalSearchProvider` with a vector store whose backends "include `sqlite-vec` ..., a local pgvector instance, or a managed service (Pinecone, Weaviate Cloud, Qdrant Cloud)" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:97`). The MCP bridge reads the overlay vector backend from `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:236`) and resolves it in `mcpOverlayVectorBackend`, whose built-in switch handles only `memory` and `sqlite-vec` (`cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go:228`-`238`); any other id returns the error `"unsupported overlay vector backend: %s"`. The only other resolution path is `vector.Default.New` (`cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go:223`), and `vector.Default` is empty by default with no `init()` registrations (`pkg/vector/registry.go:44`-`45`), so `pgvector`, `pinecone`, `weaviate-cloud`, and `qdrant-cloud` are not reachable. Those backends exist as types (`pkg/vector/pgvector.go`, `pkg/vector/pinecone.go`, `pkg/vector/weaviate.go`, `pkg/vector/qdrant.go`) and are wired into the registry-side bootstrap (`internal/serverboot`), but not into the overlay path, so an operator who sets `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND=pgvector` for the bridge gets a startup error rather than the documented backend. Suggested direction: extend `mcpOverlayVectorBackend` to construct the pgvector, Pinecone, Weaviate, and Qdrant providers from their env-var configuration, reusing the serverboot factory logic, or narrow the spec's backend list to what the overlay path actually supports.

### - [ ] F-6.4.2 — Overlay `DOMAIN.md` files are never read by any overlay consumer [Medium] — DEFERRED

DEFERRED: this is the §6.4 framing of the already-deferred F-4.5.2 (§4.5.4 framing) and shares its root cause. §4.5.2 requires a workspace-local `DOMAIN.md`'s `include:` globs to "resolve over the merged view (layers org + team + user + local)", and §4.5.4 places the overlay `DOMAIN.md` merge client-side after the registry returns. The `/v1/load_domain` and `/v1/search_domains` responses are already rendered (capped notable lists, depth-limited subtree) and expose neither the per-domain artifact catalog nor the unrendered tree the client would need to re-resolve includes over the merged registry+overlay view, so a faithful merge cannot be completed from the current wire contract. A partial client-side merge (description/keywords plus overlay-only artifacts) would silently diverge from the spec on import resolution and folding, which the F-4.5.2 analysis explicitly rejected. Closing it requires a new registry surface exposing the per-domain catalog plus parallel MCP/Python/TS implementations, beyond this batch. No code changed for this finding; the tree stays green. Re-attempt alongside F-4.5.2 once the catalog-exposing registry surface lands.

(gap) §6.4 defines the workspace overlay as "a per-developer set of artifact packages (`ARTIFACT.md` for every type, plus `SKILL.md` for skills) and `DOMAIN.md` files that merge as the highest-precedence layer in the caller's effective view" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:76`). Every overlay consumer reads only `ARTIFACT.md` (and `SKILL.md` for skills) and ignores `DOMAIN.md`. The Go overlay provider resolves records via `filesystem.Walk`, whose `walkLayer` matches only `ARTIFACT.md` and explicitly skips `DOMAIN.md` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:135`-`151`); `overlay.Filesystem.Resolve` calls that `Walk` (`pkg/overlay/overlay.go:54`). The Python and TypeScript overlay parsers also key off `ARTIFACT.md` only (`sdks/podium-py/podium/_overlay.py:128`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/overlay.ts:132`). A repository-wide search confirms no overlay consumer references `DOMAIN.md` (the sole match is an unrelated comment in `pkg/sync/scope.go:33`). A `DOMAIN.md` placed in the workspace overlay therefore never merges into the effective view. Suggested direction: load overlay `DOMAIN.md` files and compose them at the overlay's precedence in the MCP server, `podium sync`, and the SDKs, or remove the `DOMAIN.md` claim from §6.4 if overlay domain composition is out of scope.

### - [x] F-6.4.3 — MCP server watches the overlay by polling rather than fsnotify [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit c808db3): the MCP overlay watcher now watches the resolved path via fsnotify, reusing the recursive watcher from `pkg/sync` (renamed/exported `sync.TreeWatcher` with `NewTreeWatcher`/`AddTree`/`Events`/`Errors`). `overlayWatchLoop` (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go`) re-targets the fsnotify watch when the resolved path changes (roots/list establishes it with no filesystem event) and re-indexes on each tree change, debounced to 200ms; newly created subdirectories are added to the watch. A content-fingerprint poll on the path-recheck interval remains the fallback when fsnotify cannot initialize, mirroring `pkg/sync/watch.go`. Matches §6.4 ("watches the resolved path via fsnotify and re-indexes on change"). Tests: 3 new unit (`UsesFsnotifyNotPolling` proves event-driven detection under a 5s interval; `WatchesNewSubdirectory`; `overlayContentWatch` retarget); existing watch + integration tests still green.

(inconsistency) §6.4 states "The MCP server watches the resolved path via fsnotify and re-indexes on change" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:85`). The MCP overlay watcher uses a 500ms poll loop over a content fingerprint and never opens an fsnotify watcher (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:18`, `cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:66`-`88`). The source comment claims "the project carries no fsnotify dependency" (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:15`), but `go.mod:8` pins `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify v1.10.1` and `pkg/sync/watch.go:97` does use fsnotify for `podium sync --watch`, so the dependency is present and used elsewhere. The behavioral contract "re-indexes on change" is met with up to one poll interval of latency, so the divergence is in the named mechanism rather than the observable result. Suggested direction: switch the MCP overlay watcher to fsnotify with the existing poll loop as the fallback, mirroring `pkg/sync/watch.go`, or relax the spec wording to describe change detection without naming fsnotify.

### - [x] F-6.4.4 — SDK overlay search ignores the `scope` filter [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit c808db3): both SDKs now thread `scope` into the overlay search the way the Go MCP server does (a prefix match on the artifact id). Python `LocalOverlay.search` gained a `scope` keyword and `Client._fuse_overlay`/`search_artifacts` forward it (`sdks/podium-py/podium/_overlay.py`, `client.py`); TypeScript `LocalOverlay.search` opts gained `scope` and `Client.fuseOverlay`/`searchArtifacts` forward it (`sdks/podium-ts/src/overlay.ts`, `index.ts`). A scoped query now excludes out-of-scope overlay artifacts, matching the registry stream and the effective-view semantics of §6.4. Tests: 2 Python + 2 TS (direct `LocalOverlay.search` scope filtering incl. browse mode, and `search_artifacts(scope=…)` excluding an out-of-scope overlay hit); verified to fail without the filter.

(inconsistency) §6.4 describes the overlay as merging "as the highest-precedence layer in the caller's effective view" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:76`), and the MCP server applies the `scope` prefix filter to overlay hits so an overlay artifact outside the requested scope is excluded (`cmd/podium-mcp/local_search.go:90`, called from `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:51`-`54`). The Python and TypeScript SDKs forward `scope` to the registry stream but never apply it to the overlay: `Client._fuse_overlay` calls `index.search(query, type_filter=type_filter, tags_filter=tags, top_k=top_k)` with no scope argument (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:606`-`608`), and `LocalOverlay.search` accepts no scope parameter (`sdks/podium-py/podium/_overlay.py:211`). The TypeScript path is identical: `fuseOverlay` passes only `type` and `tags` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:554`) and `LocalOverlay.search` has no scope option (`sdks/podium-ts/src/overlay.ts:235`). A scoped SDK search can therefore surface overlay artifacts outside the requested scope, diverging from both the Go behavior and the effective-view semantics. Suggested direction: thread the `scope` filter into the SDK overlay search the same way the Go path does (a prefix match on the artifact id), so a scoped query excludes out-of-scope overlay hits.

## F-6.5 — 6.5 Cache

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.5 against the implementation._

I reviewed the §6.5 Cache contract (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:99`–`114`) covering the disk-cache layout, the resolution and content cache layers, the resolution-cache TTL, the three cache modes selected via `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE`, the index DB, and the `podium cache prune` command. The implementation lives in `cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go` (resolution index over BoltDB), `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` (content cache, cache-mode dispatch, HEAD revalidation), and `cmd/podium/cache.go` (the `prune` CLI).

Most concrete claims hold. The disk layout `${PODIUM_CACHE_DIR}/<sha256>/` is honored by `sanitizeHash`, which strips the `sha256:` prefix and uses the bare digest as the bucket directory (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2313`). The content cache stores manifest bytes plus bundled resources and never overwrites destructively because the bucket is content-addressed (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2273`). The resolution cache maps `(id, "latest")` to the resolved semver and `(id, semver)` to the content hash, backed by an embedded BoltDB file, satisfying the "Index DB: BoltDB or SQLite" requirement (`cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:64`, `cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:145`). The TTL defaults to 30 seconds via `PODIUM_CACHE_RESOLUTION_TTL_SECONDS` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:231`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:374`). `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` defaults to `always-revalidate` and is validated against the three named modes at startup (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:227`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:330`). The always-revalidate path issues a HEAD and serves cached content only when the registry confirms the content hash is unchanged (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1135`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2043`). The `podium cache prune` command exists, is dispatched from the CLI, and skips the dot-prefixed resolution index (`cmd/podium/main.go:43`, `cmd/podium/cache.go:39`, `cmd/podium/cache.go:82`).

I found one behavioral deviation in the offline-first mode interaction with the resolution TTL, recorded below as an Info item because the spec text leaves the TTL-versus-mode precedence ambiguous.

### - [x] F-6.5.1 — Offline-first treats a stale-but-present `latest` resolution as a miss and calls the registry [Info] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The spec states for `offline-first`: "use cached resolution and content if present; only call the registry on miss" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:109`), while the resolution cache description lists "TTL 30s by default" under the resolution layer generally (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:103`). In `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1116`–`1129` the offline-first path calls `s.resolutions.Resolve(id, version, now, ttl, allowStale=false)` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1120`), and for a `latest` request `Resolve` returns a miss when the entry is older than the 30-second TTL (`cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:189`). The offline-first branch then falls through to the conditional registry fetch at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1161`. A `(id, "latest")` resolution that is present in the cache but older than 30 seconds therefore triggers a registry call in offline-first mode, which reads against the "only call the registry on miss" clause when the entry is in fact present. The spec does not say whether the resolution TTL is suppressed for offline-first, so the two clauses are in tension and a reader could justify either behavior; only `always-revalidate` is documented to revalidate. Suggested direction: clarify in §6.5 whether the resolution TTL applies in offline-first, and if a present-but-stale `latest` should be served without a registry call in offline-first, set `allowStale` true for offline-first in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1120` so it matches the documented "use cached resolution if present" contract.

Resolution (commit 0d95ffd): offline-first now resolves with `allowStale=true`, so a present-but-stale `(id, "latest")` resolution is served from cache without a registry call; only a genuine miss (no entry) falls through to the registry (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`). This follows the spec, which scopes TTL revalidation to `always-revalidate` ("Revalidated via HEAD on hit when PODIUM_CACHE_MODE=always-revalidate") and defines offline-first as "use cached resolution and content if present; only call the registry on miss." Tests: 2 podium-mcp unit (stale `latest` served with zero registry calls; true miss still fetches).

## F-6.6 — 6.6 Materialization

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.6 against the implementation._

I traced the five materialization steps the spec defines (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:118`) to the bridge pipeline in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`, the adapter and hook SPIs, and the atomic writer. The pipeline is implemented end to end in `deliverLoadArtifact` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1290`): step 1 fetch in `fetchLargeResources` / `fetchOneLargeResource` (`cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go:24`, `:55`), step 2 verify in `enforceSignaturePolicy` plus `verifyContentHash` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1298`, `:1474`), step 3 adapt via the configured `HarnessAdapter` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1378`), step 4 the `MaterializationHook` chain in `hook.Run` (`pkg/hook/hook.go:51`), and step 5 the atomic tree write in `materialize.Write` (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:205`).

Most concrete claims hold. The fetch retry contract (max 3 attempts, exponential backoff, fresh URL set on 403) is implemented exactly (`cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go:56-88`). The hook chain runs in declared order, each hook receives the previous hook's output, drops are honored, warnings concatenate, and an empty hook set is a no-op (`pkg/hook/hook.go:51-80`); the chain runs whether or not an adapter translated, since `PODIUM_HARNESS=none` still produces the canonical layout (`pkg/adapter/none.go:21`) and the hook step runs over that output (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1388`). The write is atomic with a tree-level all-or-nothing guarantee via `.tmp` staging plus rename (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:243-286`), and out-of-destination paths (including symlinked components) are rejected before any write (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:292-333`). The destination resolves from a per-call argument or `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT`, with the per-call value winning (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1341-1344`, `:1276-1283`). The env vars `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES`, `PODIUM_HARNESS`, and `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` are all wired (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:224`, `:232`, `:251`). The findings below concern the content-hash leg of step 2 and the manifest-body delivery channel described in the step-list preamble.

### - [x] F-6.6.1 — Content-hash match skipped for skills and extends-merged manifests [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Step 2 states that verification is "Signature verification (per `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES`) and content-hash match" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:121`), presenting the content-hash match as a step that always runs. The implementation's `verifyContentHash` returns `nil` without checking anything when `resp.Type == "skill"` or `resp.ManifestMerged` is set (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1475`). For those artifacts the served bytes cannot reproduce the stored hash by construction (the registry parses and discards the original `SKILL.md`, and an extends-merged manifest is a re-serialization), so the code relies on the signature gate instead. That gate is itself conditional: `EnforceVerification` returns `nil` when `needsVerification` is false (`pkg/sign/sign.go:99`, `:108-123`), which is the case for `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES=never` and for `medium-and-above` against a low-sensitivity artifact. Under those policies a skill or a merged manifest passes step 2 with neither a content-hash check nor a signature check, so a tampered registry response or a non-TLS hop that altered the bytes while keeping the `content_hash` field consistent would not be detected before the artifact is written to disk. The blast radius is bounded to skills and merged manifests under a permissive signature policy, but skills are a first-class type and `never` is a supported policy value, so the integrity guarantee step 2 mandates is absent on a common path. Suggested direction: deliver the skill's verbatim `SKILL.md` and the pre-merge parent bytes (or the canonical pre-merge artifact bytes) alongside the response so the bridge can reproduce the ingest canonicalization and run the content-hash match for these types instead of skipping it, falling back to the signature gate only when the source bytes are genuinely unavailable.

Resolution (commit 0d95ffd): the bridge's `verifyContentHash` no longer skips skills or merged manifests; it reproduces the §4.7.6 `contentHashOf` canonicalization for every type (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`). For a skill it hashes the verbatim `SKILL.md` (already shipped as `skill_raw`) in the SKILL.md slot; for an extends-merged manifest the registry now also delivers the leaf child's pre-merge ARTIFACT.md bytes in a new `raw_frontmatter` field (`pkg/registry/core/core.go`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go`), which the bridge hashes instead of the re-serialized merged frontmatter. A required dependency surfaced during the fix: the SQLite and Postgres stores persisted `frontmatter` and `body` but silently dropped `skill_raw`, so a SQL-backed registry returned `skill_raw=""` and would have made the new skill check false-reject every skill; both backends now persist and round-trip `skill_raw` (`pkg/store/sqlite.go`, `pkg/store/postgres.go`). Tests: 4 podium-mcp unit (skill verify/tamper, merged verify/tamper), 2 podium-mcp unit retained for non-skill/non-merged, 2 core unit (raw_frontmatter reproduces hash; unset for plain), 1 store conformance (SkillRaw round-trip, runs per backend), 3 integration (real-bridge skill verify/tamper, merged verify), 2 e2e (real registry: skill hash covers skill_raw, merged delivers raw_frontmatter reproducing the hash).

### - [ ] F-6.6.2 — Manifest body never delivered via presigned URL above the inline cutoff [Low] — DEFERRED

(gap) The step-list preamble states the registry "returns the canonical manifest body inline (or via presigned URL if above the inline cutoff)" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:118`), so a manifest body above the cutoff is described as travelling as a presigned reference the bridge fetches. The registry's `load_artifact` handler always populates `ManifestBody` inline from `res.ManifestBody` and only applies the inline cutoff to bundled resources via `attachResources` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:862`, `:873-879`, `:922-929`); there is no field or branch that presigns the body. The bridge's `loadArtifactResponse` correspondingly has only an inline `manifest_body` field and no manifest-body URL field (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1651`), so even if a registry emitted a presigned body the bridge could not fetch it. The body-via-presigned-URL channel is therefore not implemented end to end. No live failure results because the registry never emits a presigned body, so the gap is latent rather than a wrong result today. Suggested direction: either implement the presigned-body channel (a body URL field the registry sets above the cutoff and the bridge fetches in step 1) or narrow the spec preamble to state that the manifest body is always returned inline and only resources presign above the cutoff.

DEFERRED: the gap is latent (no wrong result today) and the two remediations are not cleanly available. The served `frontmatter` field is the full ARTIFACT.md (frontmatter plus body) and `manifest_body` is only the body, so the body is already delivered as a substring of the always-inline `frontmatter`; presigning `manifest_body` alone would not reduce the payload, and presigning `frontmatter` is not a behavior the spec describes. A faithful presigned-body channel therefore also requires uploading the body bytes to the §7.2 object store at serve time and extending the `/objects/{key}` visibility resolver (`ResolveResourceOwner`, keyed strictly on bundled-resource content hashes) to authorize a manifest-body hash, which is a new data-plane and authorization surface disproportionate to a Low latent gap and not unambiguously derivable from the spec. The alternative remediation (narrow the §6.6 preamble) edits `spec/`, which is read-only under this batch's ground rules. No consumer is broken because the registry never emits a presigned body.

## F-6.7 — 6.7 Harness Adapters (6.7.1 The Author Burden)

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.7 against the implementation._

I traced the §6.7 materialization matrix (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:162-180`), the §6.7 mechanisms (standalone file, bundled resources, inject, config-merge), the harness-neutral `type: context` bucket, the adapter sandbox contract, and the §6.7.1 capability matrix and author-burden mitigations against `pkg/adapter`, `pkg/materialize`, `pkg/lint`, and the MCP delivery path in `cmd/podium-mcp`. Most concrete contracts hold. Every harness in the table is registered (`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:153-170`), and the per-type native locations match the spec table cell for cell: claude-code skills at `.claude/skills/<n>/SKILL.md` (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:37-48`), codex skills at `.agents/skills/<n>` and agents at `.codex/agents/<n>.toml` (`pkg/adapter/codex.go:21-24`), gemini commands at `.gemini/commands/<n>.toml` (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go:139`), and the config-merge targets resolving to `.claude/settings.json`, `.cursor/hooks.json`, `.cursor/mcp.json`, `.codex/config.toml`, `.gemini/settings.json`, and root `opencode.json` (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:94-96`, `pkg/adapter/builtins.go:69-74,145-147,174`). The `type: context` bucket is `.podium/context/<artifact-id>/` and identical across adapters (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:41-50`). The capability matrix is transcribed verbatim from the spec rows (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:80-115`), the lint emits the spec's "field X is used but adapter cannot translate it" wording (`pkg/lint/harness_capability.go:43-45`), the §6.9 untranslatable guard runs before the write (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1363-1367`), per-call `harness:` override is honored (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1524-1529`), and the sandbox containment contract is enforced by lexical plus symlink-resolution checks (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:289-333`).

The findings concern the §6.7.1 capability matrix and the per-event hook coverage. The Codex hook event map omits a common event the matrix's ✓ grade requires, and the ingest lint never evaluates the matrix's `mcpServers` field row, so a non-portable `mcpServers` field on a Codex/Pi/Hermes agent passes lint silently. Two further observations cover the §6.7 versioning pin and the cowork rule cell.

### - [x] F-6.7.1 — Codex hook adapter omits `session_end` while matrix grades it ✓ [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Spec §6.7.1 defines the `hook_event` ✓ grade as config-merging all the common events: "the row marks ✓ when the adapter config-merges the common events (`session_start`, `session_end`, `pre_tool_use`, `post_tool_use`, `stop`, `pre_compact`) and ⚠ when only a subset translates" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:248`), and the matrix grades Codex `hook_event (any)` as ✓ (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:244`, encoded as the `N` in column 5 of `pkg/adapter/capability.go:114`). The Codex event map `codexHookEvents` lists `session_start`, `pre_tool_use`, `post_tool_use`, `stop`, and `pre_compact` but has no `session_end` entry (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:386-401`), whereas the Claude Code and Gemini maps both include `session_end` (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:330,410`). Because `codexHookTOML` returns `nil` for an unmapped event and `codexHookOut` then produces no files (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:249-260,231-240`), a hook artifact with `hook_event: session_end` targeting Codex materializes nothing, yet the matrix advertises Codex as ✓ so the lint raises no warning. Codex translates five of the six common events the ✓ grade requires, which is the spec's own definition of ⚠. Suggested direction: add `"session_end": "SessionEnd"` (or the correct Codex native event) to `codexHookEvents`, or regrade the Codex `hook_event` cell to ⚠ in `capabilityMatrix` if Codex genuinely has no session-end event.

Resolution (commit f7e0ec7): Added `"session_end": "SessionEnd"` to `codexHookEvents` (`pkg/adapter/layout.go`) so Codex config-merges every common event and genuinely meets its ✓ grade. Tests: adapter unit (`TestHookEvents_CodexCoversCommonEvents`, `TestHookEvents_CodexSessionEnd`), integration (`TestPodiumSync_CodexSessionEndHook`), e2e (`TestHarness_CodexSessionEndHookMaterializes`).

### - [x] F-6.7.2 — Capability lint never evaluates the graded `mcpServers` field row [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.7.1 includes `mcpServers` as a frontmatter-field fidelity row graded ✗ for Codex, Pi, and Hermes (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:229`), and mitigation 2 states the ingest lint surfaces such mismatches with "field `X` is used but adapter `cursor` cannot translate it" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:208`). The matrix encodes the row (`{Field: "mcpServers"}: row("NXNNXNNXX")` at `pkg/adapter/capability.go:93`), but `UsedCapabilities` never emits an `mcpServers` capability: it emits `delegates_to`, `requiresApproval`, and `sandbox_profile` when set but has no branch for `art.MCPServers` (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:178-186`). Both the lint (`pkg/lint/harness_capability.go:40`) and the §6.9 materialization guard (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:275`) iterate `UsedCapabilities`, so an agent that declares `mcpServers:` and targets Codex (where `type: agent` is ✓ but the `mcpServers` field is ✗) draws no diagnostic and materializes via `codexAgentTOML`, which silently drops the field (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:106-115`). The author receives no warning that the field is lost. Suggested direction: emit `Capability{Field: "mcpServers"}` from `UsedCapabilities` when `len(art.MCPServers) > 0` so the lint and the §6.9 guard evaluate the graded row.

Resolution (commit f7e0ec7): `UsedCapabilities` now emits `Capability{Field: "mcpServers"}` when `len(art.MCPServers) > 0` (`pkg/adapter/capability.go`), so the §6.7.1 lint errors and the §6.9 untranslatable guard evaluate the graded row instead of dropping the field silently. Tests: adapter unit (`TestCapability_UsedCapabilities`), 2 lint unit (`TestHarnessCapability_MCPServersTargetingCodexErrors`, `…ClaudeCodeClean`), integration (`TestPodiumLint_MCPServersUntranslatableErrors`), 2 e2e (`TestHarness_MCPServersTargeting{Codex,ClaudeCode}…`).

### - [x] F-6.7.3 — Adapter versioning pin and refuse-to-start are absent [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.7 "Versioning" states "Profile and harness combinations that need a newer adapter behavior pin a minimum MCP server version; older binaries refuse to start" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:199`). The sync configuration schema exposes no field to express a minimum MCP server version: `Defaults`, `Profile`, and `TargetEntry` carry only registry, harness, target, and profile selectors (`pkg/sync/config.go:30-62`), and no startup path checks a pinned version against the binary version (a repository-wide search for a min-version pin or a refuse-to-start check returned only the unrelated §6.9 unknown-harness guard at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:351`). A profile that needs newer adapter behavior cannot declare the requirement, and an older binary does not refuse to start. Suggested direction: add a minimum-server-version field to the profile or defaults schema and a startup check that fails when the binary version is below the declared minimum, or revise the spec if the pin mechanism is deferred.

Resolution (commit f7e0ec7): Added a `min_server_version` field to `Defaults` and `Profile` (`pkg/sync/config.go`, merged through `mergeDefaults`) plus `version.Compare`/`AtLeast` (`pkg/version/version.go`) and a `checkServerVersion` helper exposed on both `SyncConfig` and `MergedConfig`. The MCP bridge refuses to start (`cmd/podium-mcp`: `checkServerVersionFromSyncYAML` against every profile) and `podium sync` refuses (`cmd/podium/main.go`, scoped to the active profile) with `config.server_version_too_old` when the binary is below the highest applicable pin. Tests: 3 version unit, 5 sync-config unit, 3 integration, 3 e2e (CLI + bridge refuse/allow).

### - [x] F-6.7.4 — Cowork `rule` cell is ✗ in the path table but materialized as a skill [Info] — CLOSED

**Resolution (CLOSED):** Reconciled the §6.7 path table with the shipped skill fallback after the maintainer approved the spec edit. The `claude-cowork` × `rule` cell at `spec/06-mcp-server.md:169` now reads `skills/<n>/SKILL.md` (fallback) instead of `✗`, matching the §6.7.1 capability matrix (cowork `rule_mode` rows graded ⚠), the §6.7.1 prose ("Claude Cowork ships rules as skills"), the live enforcement matrix (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:107-110`, cowork rule graded `F`/fallback, so lint warns rather than errors), and the materialization code (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:449-462` synthesizes `SKILL.md`). The notation parallels the inject harnesses' `AGENTS.md` (inject) cells. No code change; behavior pinned byte-for-byte by `test/materialization/testdata/golden/claude-cowork.golden`.

(inconsistency) The §6.7 path table marks `rule` for `claude-cowork` as `✗` (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:169`), which by the table's own legend means the harness has no native location and produces no output. The §6.7.1 capability matrix instead grades cowork rule modes as ⚠ (fallback), and the surrounding prose states "Claude Cowork ships rules as skills, a fallback for every mode" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:240-243,246`). The implementation follows the capability matrix: `coworkPlugin` synthesizes a `SKILL.md` for a `type: rule` artifact and writes it under the plugin's `skills/` directory (`pkg/adapter/layout.go:442-458,480-496`). The code is internally consistent with the dominant §6.7.1 framing and benefits the author, so this is a spec-internal tension between the path-table `✗` and the capability-matrix ⚠ rather than a code defect. Suggested direction: reconcile the spec so the path-table cowork `rule` cell reflects the skill fallback (for example a `skills/<n>/SKILL.md (fallback)` note) instead of `✗`; no code change is required.

Deferred: spec-internal contradiction with no code defect. The §6.7 path-table `✗` and the §6.7.1 capability-matrix ⚠/prose disagree; the code follows the dominant §6.7.1 framing (cowork rules ship as skills), which is the author-beneficial reading. The only remedy is a read-only spec edit to reconcile the path-table cell, which ground rule A forbids. The current behavior is already pinned byte-for-byte by the golden suite (`test/materialization/testdata/golden/claude-cowork.golden`, e.g. `plugins/team/ts-glob/skills/ts-glob/SKILL.md` "Project rule shipped as a Claude Cowork skill."). Not unblocked by this batch (needs a spec decision).

## F-6.8 — 6.8 Process Model

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.8 against the implementation._

Section §6.8 (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:250`-`256`) describes the bridge as a stdio subprocess whose host owns the lifecycle (spawn, signal handling, and shutdown), with one subprocess per workspace for developer hosts and one subprocess per session for managed agent runtimes. The section states a deployment topology and a lifecycle-ownership contract rather than a wire format, so the checkable claims are limited to the stdio transport, host-owned shutdown, and the single-process-per-session model.

Every concrete claim holds. The bridge serves JSON-RPC over `os.Stdin` and `os.Stdout` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:130`), with line-delimited framing read in the serve loop (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:716`-`767`). Host-owned shutdown is satisfied: the serve loop terminates only when stdin reaches EOF (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:760`-`765`), which lets the deferred token-watch, overlay-watch, and metrics-listener cleanups run on a host-driven close. The bridge installs no `SIGINT` or `SIGTERM` handler; the only trapped signal is `SIGHUP`, used to force a §6.3.2.1 token re-read without affecting lifecycle (`cmd/podium-mcp/hangup_unix.go:12`, `cmd/podium-mcp/token_watch.go:35`-`46`), so signal-driven shutdown is left to the host. The binary spawns no subprocess and does not daemonize, consistent with one process per invocation, and it generates one `sessionID` per process that threads through every meta-tool call (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:498`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:628`-`636`), matching the one-subprocess-per-session model. The code prefixes `F-6.8.1` through `F-6.8.3` mark prior-audit items that are now remediated: notification frames are dropped without a spurious error response (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:783`-`794`), an oversized inbound frame fails only that request and keeps the process serving (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:742`-`754`), and shutdown is EOF-only (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:738`-`740`).

No findings.

## F-6.9 — 6.9 Failure Modes

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.9 against the implementation._

The §6.9 failure-mode table enumerates failure conditions with required behaviors, several of which name concrete error codes. I traced each row to code. The implementation covers almost the entire table. Registry-offline returns an explicit `offline` status for the discovery meta-tools: `proxyGet` emits `{"status":"offline"}` for `load_domain` and `search_domains` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2164`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2209`), and `searchArtifacts` emits the same with overlay matches (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:29`). A missing workspace overlay path is skipped with a single startup warning (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:513`) and the watcher warns once per transition (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:34`). The `oauth-device-code` expiry path refreshes silently then falls back to interactive reauth over MCP elicitation (`cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:47`, `cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:181`), and an `injected-session-token` expiry surfaces `auth.token_expired` (`pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:79`). An untrusted runtime is rejected with `auth.untrusted_runtime` carrying `details.runtime_iss` (`pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:86`). Visibility denial returns a generic not-found that does not leak the layer and emits a `visibility.denied` audit event (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1316`).

The materialization rows hold as well. The atomic writer stages to `.tmp` siblings and cleans up on any stage-phase failure so an unwritable destination leaves nothing partial (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:246`). Signature verification runs before any disk write and fails with `materialize.signature_invalid` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1298`). An unknown `PODIUM_HARNESS` value refuses to start during `loadConfig` and lists the registered adapter IDs (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:355`, `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:130`). An adapter that cannot translate a field fails with a structured error naming the field and suggesting `harness: none` (`pkg/adapter/capability.go:284`).
