MCP protocol negotiation agrees on the lower of the host request and the binary maximum, emitting `mcp.unsupported_version` only below the supported floor (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:88`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:971`). Quota exhaustion returns `quota.storage_exceeded` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:567`, `pkg/registry/server/error_envelope.go:42`), and an unsatisfiable runtime requirement fails with `materialize.runtime_unavailable` naming the requirement (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:104`). One row has no implementation, recorded below.

### - [x] F-6.9.1 — Binary version mismatch with host caller is not detected or refused [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 2db2f42): the `initialize` handler now reads `clientInfo.version` and refuses a host caller below a configured floor with an `mcp.client_too_old` initialize error so the host's CLI can prompt an update (`clientVersionRefusal`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`). The floor is the new `PODIUM_MIN_CLIENT_VERSION` (also a `min-client-version` flag/config key); the check is opt-in because host version strings are not portably comparable across MCP runtimes, so with no floor configured nothing is refused, and an absent or unparsable host version is not refused either (a mismatch cannot be established). Tests: 5 cmd/podium-mcp units (refusal, accept at/above floor, no-floor inert, unparsable not refused, the helper table) and 2 e2e (real-binary refusal + accept/inert).

(gap) The §6.9 row "Binary version mismatch with host caller" requires "Refuse to start; host's CLI prompts an update." (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:271`). The MCP `initialize` request carries a `clientInfo` object with a `version` field per the MCP spec, which the bridge could inspect to detect an incompatible host. The initialize handler parses only `protocolVersion` and `capabilities.roots` and ignores `clientInfo` entirely (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:959`), and a repository-wide search for any binary version handshake (`clientInfo`, a minimum-client check, or a refusal on version skew) finds only the unrelated artifact-version `X-Podium-Version` header (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:852`) and the MCP protocol-version negotiation. The bridge therefore never refuses to start on a binary version mismatch with the host caller. The "host's CLI prompts an update" half is the host's responsibility, so the missing piece is the Podium-side refusal. The spec does not define what counts as a mismatch, which error code to emit, or which versions are compared, so the contract is partly conceptual and the blast radius is limited. Suggested direction: read `clientInfo.version` from the `initialize` params and, when the host caller's version falls below a declared minimum the binary supports, return a structured initialize error (for example an `mcp.*` code) so the host can surface an update prompt, or tighten the spec row to clarify that this behavior is entirely the host's responsibility.

## F-6.10 — 6.10 Error Model

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.10 against the implementation._

Section 6.10 specifies a structured error envelope with the fields `code`, `message`, `details`, `retryable`, and `suggested_action`, requires error codes to be namespaced under the `auth.*`, `config.*`, `ingest.*`, `materialize.*`, `quota.*`, `mcp.*`, `network.*`, `registry.*`, and `domain.*` prefixes, and requires these errors to be mapped to MCP error payloads. The registry server implements the envelope correctly. The `ErrorResponse` struct at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:519-525` carries all five fields with the spec JSON names, and `writeErrorDetails` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:1153-1157` enriches every emission with `retryable` and `suggested_action` from the per-code registry in `pkg/registry/server/error_envelope.go:24-51`. The canonical `auth.untrusted_runtime` example is reproduced faithfully, including `details.runtime_iss` and the verbatim `suggested_action` remediation string, at `pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:85-92` and `pkg/registry/server/error_envelope.go:48-50`. All HTTP error paths route through the envelope writers; no handler bypasses them with a raw `http.Error`. The MCP bridge maps the registry envelope to the MCP error result while preserving all five fields at `cmd/podium-mcp/error_envelope.go:101-119`, and the namespaces `materialize.*`, `network.*`, `config.*`, and `mcp.*` are present in code as required.

Two deviations surfaced. The server emits one error code (`scope_preview_disabled`) with no namespace prefix, which contradicts the blanket §6.10 claim that codes are namespaced, although the code matches the explicit definition in §3. The two SDKs that consume the registry envelope discard the `details` and `suggested_action` fields.

### - [x] F-6.10.1 — SDK envelope drops `details` and `suggested_action` [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit bc61fce): both SDK `RegistryError` types now carry the full §6.10 envelope. The Python `RegistryError.__init__` accepts `details` and `suggested_action` (exposed as `.details`/`.suggested_action`), and `_registry_error_from_envelope` reads both from the envelope; the TypeScript `RegistryError` gains `details` and `suggestedAction` fields, and `registryErrorFromEnvelope` plus the `BatchResult` error type thread them through. Both default to an empty map and empty string when the registry omits them. Callers can now read `details` (for example `runtime_iss`) and the operator remediation hint on every parsed error, including batch-item errors.

(inconsistency) §6.10 defines the structured error envelope with the fields `code`, `message`, `details`, `retryable`, and `suggested_action` (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:280-288`). The registry server emits all five, but both SDKs that parse the envelope retain only `code`, `message`, and `retryable`. The Python `RegistryError` constructor accepts only those three fields at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:21-25`, and `_registry_error_from_envelope` reads only `code`, `message`, and `retryable` from the envelope at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:63-68`. The TypeScript `RegistryError` class is the same at `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:275-283`, and `registryErrorFromEnvelope` only declares `code`, `message`, and `retryable` in its parameter type at `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:302-309`. As a result an SDK caller cannot read the machine-readable `details` map (for example `runtime_iss`) or the operator remediation hint in `suggested_action`, both of which the registry populates. The human-readable summary still includes the code and message, so the blast radius is limited to programmatic access to the dropped fields. Suggested direction: extend the SDK `RegistryError` types and both envelope parsers to capture `details` and `suggested_action` so callers can read the full §6.10 envelope.

### - [x] F-6.10.2 — `scope_preview_disabled` error code is not namespaced [Info] — CLOSED

**Resolution (CLOSED):** Namespaced the code to `config.scope_preview_disabled` (Option B) after the maintainer chose taxonomic consistency over the prior bare literal. The §3.5 tenant gate now emits `403 config.scope_preview_disabled` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:48`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:811`), which satisfies the §6.10 namespacing rule (`config.*`) and is now recognized by the bridge's `splitNamespacedCode`. Reconciled in lockstep: the §3 mandate (`spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:66`), the HTTP-API reference (`docs/reference/http-api.md:313`), and all asserting tests (`pkg/registry/server`, `cmd/podium`, `cmd/podium-mcp`, `test/integration`, `test/e2e`). The CLI detector keys on the 403 status rather than the code string, so its behavior is unchanged. Full build, vet, and test suite green.

Deferred (spec self-contradiction, read-only): §3 (`spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:66`) mandates the bare `403 scope_preview_disabled`, while §6.10 generalizes that all codes are namespaced. The implementation correctly follows the specific §3 mandate (`handleScopePreview` emits `403 scope_preview_disabled`; the MCP bridge preserves the code), so there is no implementation defect. Reconciling §6.10's generalization with §3's explicit literal requires editing read-only spec text (Ground Rule A); renaming the code to satisfy §6.10 would directly violate §3. Not unblocked by code.

(inconsistency) §6.10 states that codes are namespaced under the listed prefixes (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:290`). The scope-preview handler emits the error code `scope_preview_disabled`, which has no namespace prefix, at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:790-792`, sourced from `core.ErrScopePreviewDisabled` at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:47`. This code is the one §3 explicitly mandates: `spec/03-disclosure-surface.md:66` requires the endpoint to return `403 scope_preview_disabled`. The implementation therefore matches §3 while contradicting the §6.10 generalization. The bridge's `splitNamespacedCode` does not treat it as a namespaced code either, so it falls back to a bare `{"error": msg}` MCP result at `cmd/podium-mcp/error_envelope.go:69-73` and `cmd/podium-mcp/error_envelope.go:154-177`. This is a spec-internal contradiction with no clear implementation defect, because the code follows §3. Suggested direction: reconcile the spec so that §6.10 either carves out the §3 code as an exception or §3 adopts a namespaced code such as `config.scope_preview_disabled`, then align the constant and the bridge namespacing accordingly.

## F-6.11 — 6.11 Host Configuration Recipes

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md §6.11 against the implementation._

Section 6.11 documents host MCP config recipes for spawning the Podium stdio bridge alongside other MCP servers. The checkable contracts are the bridge binary name (`podium-mcp`), reuse of the §6.2 env-var contract across all recipes, the harness identifiers each recipe sets in `PODIUM_HARNESS`, the canonical-layout behavior of `PODIUM_HARNESS=none`, and the standalone resolution path where the registry is read from `~/.podium/sync.yaml` `defaults.registry` when the env var is omitted. The recipes themselves are host-side JSON files the user edits manually, so the only implementation surface is the bridge's handling of the env vars and harness IDs they set.

Every concrete claim holds. The bridge binary is built as `bin/podium-mcp` (`Makefile:173`), matching `"command": "podium-mcp"` in each recipe. The bridge reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, `PODIUM_HARNESS`, and `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` from the environment (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:223`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:224`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:235`), with `PODIUM_HARNESS` defaulting to `none`. Each harness identifier named in a recipe is a registered adapter: `claude-desktop`, `claude-code`, `cursor`, `opencode`, `pi`, `hermes`, and `none` all appear in `DefaultRegistry()` (`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:156`-`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:165`). The `none` adapter writes the canonical layout as-is (`pkg/adapter/none.go:21`-`pkg/adapter/none.go:43`), satisfying the closing claim that `PODIUM_HARNESS=none` writes the canonical layout. An unknown `PODIUM_HARNESS` value is rejected at startup with the registered IDs enumerated (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:355`-`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:357`). The standalone recipe resolves the registry from `sync.yaml` when no env var, flag, or config-file value supplies one: the bridge falls back to `registryFromSyncYAML()` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:287`-`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:289`), which consults the workspace `.podium/sync.yaml` and then the home-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (`cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:143`-`cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:166`, where `ConfigPath` resolves to `<workspace>/.podium/sync.yaml` per `pkg/sync/config.go:66`). The `${WORKSPACE}` token in the Claude Code recipe is a host-side substitution that the host resolves before spawning the process; the bridge performs no expansion of `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH`, which is correct for the documented usage.

No findings.

## F-7.1 — 7.1 The Registry: Podium Server or Local Filesystem (latency SLOs)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.1 against the implementation._

I reviewed §7.1 (`spec/07-external-integration.md:3`-`spec/07-external-integration.md:22`), which states that the registry is reachable as a Podium server over HTTP/JSON or as a local filesystem directory, that the dispatch between them is governed by `defaults.registry` in the merged `sync.yaml` (a URL routes to a server, a filesystem path routes to local filesystem), that both modes apply layer composition, that the MCP server, the language SDKs, and identity-based visibility filtering require a Podium server, and that the latency SLO targets are named per operation (`load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts` p99 < 200 ms; `load_artifact` manifest only p99 < 500 ms; `load_artifact` manifest plus resources p99 < 2 s).

The checkable claims hold. The URL-versus-path dispatch is implemented in `pkg/sync/config.go:115` (`isServerSource` treats `http://` and `https://` as a server and every other value as a filesystem source) and is applied consistently at the sync dispatch (`pkg/sync/sync.go:383`) and in the CLI (`cmd/podium/main.go:278`, `cmd/podium/main.go:318`). Both modes apply layer composition: the filesystem source resolves `extends:` and effective-view assembly in `pkg/registry/filesystem/extends.go:10` and `pkg/sync/sync.go:445`, while the server source composes through `pkg/registry/core`. The SDKs are HTTP-only (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:127`, `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:718`), the filesystem source carries no per-caller identity filtering (it reads only layer-config visibility metadata at `pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:155`), and the four SLO-budgeted operations map to their spec names in `pkg/registry/server/latency.go:44`, wired as the outermost middleware in `pkg/registry/server/server.go:359` and installed by the boot layer (`internal/serverboot/access_log.go:30`, `internal/serverboot/metrics_wiring.go:26`). The single item below is an observation with no defect.

### - [x] F-7.1.1 — load_artifact latency observer collapses the two SLO budgets into one key [Info] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §7.1 defines two distinct `load_artifact` SLO targets: manifest only at p99 < 500 ms and manifest plus resources from a cache miss at p99 < 2 s (`spec/07-external-integration.md:19`-`spec/07-external-integration.md:20`). The latency observer maps the `/v1/load_artifact` route to a single operation key `load_artifact` (`pkg/registry/server/latency.go:52`-`pkg/registry/server/latency.go:53`), and the metrics observer records duration under that one key (`internal/serverboot/metrics_wiring.go:27`-`internal/serverboot/metrics_wiring.go:28`). A deployment that buckets observed latency by operation name therefore cannot separate the manifest-only path from the manifest-plus-resources path, so it cannot compare against the two budgets independently. This is an observation rather than a defect: §7.1 states the budgets as operator-facing SLO targets ("Server deployments that miss these should investigate." at `spec/07-external-integration.md:22`) and mandates no wire field or label that the implementation must expose to distinguish the two. Suggested direction: leave as-is unless operators need per-budget tracking, in which case add a label (for example whether resources were inlined or fetched) to the `load_artifact` observation so the two budgets can be measured separately.

Resolution (commit 542ab69): no defect. §7.1 states the two `load_artifact`
budgets as operator-facing SLO targets and mandates no wire field or label to
distinguish the manifest-only path from the manifest-plus-resources path, so the
single `load_artifact` operation key conforms. Adding a discriminating label
would introduce observability surface the spec does not define; left unchanged.
The single-key mapping stays locked by `TestOperationName` (`pkg/registry/server`).

## F-7.2 — 7.2 Control Plane / Data Plane Split

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.2 against the implementation._

I reviewed §7.2 (`spec/07-external-integration.md:24`), which defines two surfaces. The control plane is the HTTP API that returns metadata synchronously, audited, carrying the host's OAuth identity, and visibility-filtered. The data plane is object storage that holds bundled resources. The checkable contracts are the 256 KB inline cutoff, the rule that the control plane never streams bytes for resources above the cutoff, the use of presigned URLs that the MCP server fetches from object storage for resources above the cutoff, and the inline return of resources below the cutoff.

Most of these contracts hold. The cutoff constant is `InlineCutoff = 256 * 1024` (`pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:41`), matching "256 KB". The serving split decides per resource on `ref.Size > objectstore.InlineCutoff`, presigning the large set and returning the small set inline (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:922`). The presigned link is emitted under the `presigned_url` JSON key as the spec describes (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:508`). The ingest path records `Size` as the exact byte length and drops the inline copy for resources above the cutoff so the control plane does not carry their bytes (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1106`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1131`). Control-plane calls are identity-verified for every `/v1/` route through the wrapping middleware (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:359`, `pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:62`), `load_artifact` emits an audit event (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1284`), and the data-plane `/objects/` route is exempt from caller-identity verification because access is via presigned URLs while still re-checking visibility on each fetch (`pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:68`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:1020`). One behavioral inconsistency surfaces in the standalone deployment that runs without an object store.

### - [x] F-7.2.1 — Large resources unserveable when the object store is disabled [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 83322b4): `attachResources` presigns a resource above the inline cutoff only when an object store is configured; in the standalone-without-storage mode (where ingest keeps every resource inline regardless of size) it now serves the inline bytes (base64-encoded when binary) instead of calling `presignResource` and returning HTTP 500 `registry.unavailable`. Covered by a server unit test, a no-object-store integration round-trip, and a standalone-server e2e.

(inconsistency) §7.2 states that resources above the inline cutoff are returned as presigned URLs that the MCP server fetches directly from object storage, while resources below the cutoff are returned inline (`spec/07-external-integration.md:30`). The implementation supports a standalone deployment where no object store is configured: when `openObjectStoreOrNil` returns nil (the store is disabled or fails to open), `resourcePut` is left nil and ingest keeps every resource's bytes inline regardless of size (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:657`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:1121`). At serve time, however, `attachResources` routes any resource with `ref.Size > objectstore.InlineCutoff` to `presignResource` purely on its recorded size, ignoring that the bytes are still held inline on the record (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:924`). `presignResource` then returns an error because `s.objectStore == nil` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:950`), and `handleLoadArtifact` maps that to an HTTP 500 `registry.unavailable` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:876`). The result is that a bundled resource larger than 256 KB is accepted at ingest but can never be served in the no-object-store mode, so `load_artifact` fails for that artifact even though its inline bytes are present on the record. Suggested direction: in `attachResources`, when a large resource still carries `ref.Inline` bytes and no object store is configured, return those bytes inline (or otherwise serve them) rather than calling `presignResource`, so the standalone-without-store mode can serve large resources it deliberately kept inline at ingest.

## F-7.3 — 7.3 Host Integration (7.3.1 Authoring and Ingestion, 7.3.2 Outbound Webhooks)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.3 against the implementation._

I traced the §7.3.1 author flow, ingestion triggers, ingest cases, layer CLI, and error codes, plus the §7.3.2 outbound webhook event set, schema, and receiver configuration. Most concrete claims hold. The layer CLI subcommands match the spec invocations (`cmd/podium/layer.go:44`), `podium layer register` for a git source returns the webhook URL and a freshly generated HMAC secret (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:633`, `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:652`), and the inbound Git-provider webhook trigger verifies the delivery signature in constant time and rejects a bad signature with `ingest.webhook_invalid` (401) before any content reaches the store (`pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:72`, `pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go:116`). The ingest cases for a new pair, an identical-hash no-op, lint failure, freeze window, and source-unreachable map to the spec error codes (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:651`, `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:941`). Force-push handling emits `layer.history_rewritten` in tolerant mode and rejects with `ingest.history_rewritten` under `force_push_policy: strict` (`pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:113`), and `last_ingested_at` is stamped and exposed (`pkg/store/store.go:286`). The §7.3.2 outbound worker marshals exactly the `{event, trace_id, timestamp, actor, data}` schema and HMAC-signs the body with `X-Podium-Signature: sha256=<hex>` (`pkg/webhook/webhook.go:159`, `pkg/webhook/webhook.go:254`); all five event types are emitted through `PublishEvent` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:728`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:736`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:459`, `pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:123`, `pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:164`); and the per-org receiver CRUD masks the HMAC secret on every read (`pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go:29`).

Two findings stand out. The inbound git webhook HMAC secret is returned verbatim in every `GET /v1/layers` list response, contradicting the one-time-credential framing the spec gives the secret and the masking the same codebase applies to outbound receivers. The `ingest.immutable_violation` rejection the spec names for a same-version content conflict is never surfaced with that error code; the conflict is reported only as an opaque count with HTTP 200.

### - [x] F-7.3.1 — `GET /v1/layers` leaks the inbound webhook HMAC secret [High] — CLOSED

Resolution: tagged `store.LayerConfig.WebhookSecret` with `json:"-"` so it is redacted from every marshaled `LayerConfig` (the non-admin-gated `GET /v1/layers` and the `?deleted=true` listing); the secret reaches the caller only through the dedicated `webhook_secret` field on the one-time register and rotate-secret responses, mirroring the outbound-receiver masking. The SQL backends persist it via explicit columns, so storage is unaffected. Tests: a `pkg/registry/server` redaction unit test (register/list/deleted-list plus a store-persistence assertion) and the hardened `TestHTTPAPI_ListLayers` e2e. Fixed in 429fed5.

(bug) The spec frames the git webhook HMAC secret as a credential returned once at registration: "`podium layer register` returns the webhook URL and HMAC secret to register on the source repo" (`spec/07-external-integration.md:93`). The register handler generates a 32-byte secret and stores it on `store.LayerConfig.WebhookSecret` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:633`), but that field carries no `json:"-"` tag (`pkg/store/store.go:263`) and the list handler marshals the raw `LayerConfig` rows directly (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:678`). A registered run of `GET /v1/layers` therefore returns `"WebhookSecret": "<hex>"` in the body; I confirmed this against `pkg/store.Memory` by registering a git layer and observing the secret in the list response. The list handler is not admin-gated (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:663` has no `authAdmin` call), so any caller who can list layers can read every layer's inbound HMAC secret and forge signed webhook deliveries that pass `webhook.Default.Verify` and trigger ingest. The outbound-receiver CRUD already masks its secret with `Secret = "***"` on List, Get, and Put (`pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go:29`, `pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go:103`, `pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go:150`), so the inbound path is the inconsistent one. Suggested direction: tag `WebhookSecret` with `json:"-"` (or give `LayerConfig` a `MarshalJSON` that redacts it) so the secret only appears in the one-time register and rotate-secret responses, mirroring the outbound-receiver masking.

### - [x] F-7.3.2 — Same-version content conflict is not surfaced as `ingest.immutable_violation` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution: `runIngestAndRespond` now reports each same-version content conflict as a per-artifact object carrying the `ingest.immutable_violation` code and the conflicting `(artifact_id, version, old_hash, new_hash)`, replacing the opaque count. A pure-conflict snapshot (nothing accepted or idempotent) returns HTTP 409 `ingest.immutable_violation`, mirroring the pipeline's lint hard-error rule; a mixed snapshot stays 200 with the conflicts reported per-artifact. Added the code to the §6.10 envelope registry and surfaced conflicts in the `podium layer reingest` CLI. Tests: three `pkg/registry/server` reingest unit tests (pure 409, mixed 200, empty list) and the now-unblocked `TestPluginSPI_IngestImmutableViolation` (T-D-extending-44) e2e. Fixed in 429fed5.

(inconsistency) The §7.3.1 ingest-cases table states "Same version, different content_hash | Rejected as `ingest.immutable_violation`" and the Errors paragraph lists `ingest.immutable_violation` among the §7.3.1 error codes (`spec/07-external-integration.md:75`, `spec/07-external-integration.md:97`). The pipeline does reject the conflicting artifact (it appends a `ConflictReport` and `continue`s without storing, so the immutability invariant itself holds) at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:656` and `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:701`, but the conflict never reaches the caller as the named error code. `runIngestAndRespond` returns HTTP 200 and exposes only an opaque `"conflicts": len(res.Conflicts)` count, discarding the per-artifact `ArtifactID`, `Version`, and hashes the `ConflictReport` carries (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:927`). A `grep` for `ingest.immutable_violation` across `pkg/registry/server` and `internal/serverboot` returns no HTTP-layer emission, and `writeReingestError` has no case for `store.ErrImmutableViolation` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:941`). An author whose reingest hit a version collision receives a 200 with a bare count instead of the `ingest.immutable_violation` envelope the spec promises, and cannot tell which artifact collided. Suggested direction: include the per-artifact conflicts in the reingest response with the `ingest.immutable_violation` code and the conflicting `(artifact_id, version)` so a caller can act on the rejection the spec describes.

### - [ ] F-7.3.3 — `podium layer reorder` annotation says user-defined only, code allows admin-defined [Info] — DEFERRED

Deferred: the code already conforms to the normative §4.6/§4.7.2 grant that admins may "Add, remove, and reorder admin-defined layers" — the reorder handler requires admin authorization for any admin-defined layer in the set rather than refusing it (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go` reorder, verified). The only remediation is editing the conflicting inline annotation "# user-defined layers only" in the §7.3.1 layer-CLI block, and the spec is read-only (Ground Rule A). This is a spec-internal self-contradiction between the §7.3.1 annotation and the normative §4.6 grant, not a code defect, so no code change is warranted.

(inconsistency) The §7.3.1 layer-CLI block annotates `podium layer reorder <id> [<id> ...]` with "# user-defined layers only" (`spec/07-external-integration.md:87`). The reorder handler does not restrict the operation to user-defined layers: it iterates the requested order and, for any admin-defined layer in the set, requires admin authorization rather than refusing it (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:815`), then re-sequences whatever the caller passed. The code aligns with `spec/04-artifact-model.md:792`, which grants admins the ability to "Add, remove, and reorder admin-defined layers", so the implementation is correct against §4.6 and the §7.3.1 inline annotation is the narrower, conflicting text. Reported per the spec-is-reference rule, but the defect is in the §7.3.1 annotation rather than the code. Suggested direction: drop or relax the "# user-defined layers only" annotation in §7.3.1 so it matches the §4.6 admin-reorder grant the code implements.

## F-7.4 — 7.4 Degraded Network

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.4 against the implementation._

Section 7.4 defines the degraded-network fallback driven by `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` across three consumers: the MCP server, `podium sync`, and the language SDKs. The spec mandates three modes. `always-revalidate` returns `{status: "offline", served_from_cache: true}` alongside cached results, and surfaces the structured error `network.registry_unreachable` when there is no cache. `offline-first` serves cached results silently with no error. `offline-only` never contacts the registry and returns a structured error on a cache miss. The MCP server implements all three modes for `load_artifact` faithfully: the always-revalidate fallback merges `status: "offline"` and `served_from_cache: true` onto a cached delivery and otherwise returns `network.registry_unreachable` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1188`-`1210`), the offline-first cache hit serves silently (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1116`-`1124`), and offline-only short-circuits to `errOfflineCacheMiss` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1126`-`1127`). The bridge produces a structured `network.registry_unreachable` envelope with `code`, `retryable`, and `suggested_action` (`cmd/podium-mcp/error_envelope.go:69`-`76`, `cmd/podium-mcp/error_envelope.go:125`-`128`). `podium sync` validates the env var and threads the mode into `sync.Run`, handling offline-only and offline-first (`pkg/sync/sync.go:184`-`203`). Both SDKs validate the mode and short-circuit offline-only before any request (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:412`-`424`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:418`-`424`).

The findings concern the `always-revalidate` no-cache error code on the consumers that keep no content cache (`podium sync` and the SDKs), and a literal deviation from the offline-first "silent" contract in the MCP discovery and search paths. The MCP `load_artifact` path itself is conformant.

### - [x] F-7.4.1 — Python SDK leaks raw transport error instead of `network.registry_unreachable` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit bc61fce): a new `Client._unreachable_error` maps a transport-level `urllib.error.URLError` (connection refused, DNS failure, connect timeout — the non-`HTTPError` subclass) to the structured `RegistryError("network.registry_unreachable", …)`, mirroring the MCP bridge's retryable flag and remediation hint. It is applied at all three urlopen sites: `_get`, the `load_artifacts` batch path, and the `subscribe` event stream. Because the SDK keeps no content cache, an unreachable registry in both always-revalidate and offline-first is a no-cache miss; offline-only still short-circuits earlier in `_guard_offline`. A reachable server's structured error (an `HTTPError` with an envelope) is unaffected.

(inconsistency) The spec states that in `always-revalidate` mode, "if no cache, structured error `network.registry_unreachable`" (`spec/07-external-integration.md:127`), and that "`podium sync` and the SDKs apply the same cache modes" (`spec/07-external-integration.md:133`). The Python SDK keeps no content cache, so every always-revalidate (and offline-first) call against an unreachable registry hits the no-cache branch and should surface the structured `network.registry_unreachable` error. The SDK's request helper catches only `urllib.error.HTTPError` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:793`-`795`); a transport-level failure (connection refused, DNS failure, timeout) raises the parent `urllib.error.URLError`, which is not caught and propagates as a raw exception rather than a `RegistryError("network.registry_unreachable", ...)`. The same omission applies to the batch path (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:714`-`718`) and the event stream (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:773`). Suggested direction: wrap the `urlopen` calls so a `urllib.error.URLError` that is not an `HTTPError` is converted to `RegistryError("network.registry_unreachable", ...)`, matching the MCP bridge's code and the always-revalidate no-cache contract.

### - [x] F-7.4.2 — TypeScript SDK leaks raw fetch rejection instead of `network.registry_unreachable` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit bc61fce): a new `Client.unreachableError` maps a rejected `fetch` promise (the `TypeError` raised for connection refused or DNS failure before any `Response` exists) to the structured `RegistryError("network.registry_unreachable", …)` with the retryable flag and remediation hint. It wraps the `fetcher` call in `get`, `loadArtifacts`, and `subscribe`. As with the Python SDK, both always-revalidate and offline-first surface the no-cache miss; offline-only short-circuits in `guardOffline`. A reachable non-2xx response still maps through `registryErrorFromEnvelope`, preserving the server's code.

(inconsistency) The spec's `always-revalidate` mode requires the structured error `network.registry_unreachable` when there is no cache (`spec/07-external-integration.md:127`), and the SDKs "apply the same cache modes" (`spec/07-external-integration.md:133`). The TypeScript SDK keeps no content cache, so an always-revalidate call against an unreachable registry should produce that structured error. The `get` helper inspects `resp.ok` and maps a non-2xx response to a `RegistryError` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:733`-`748`), but a transport-level failure rejects the `fetch` promise (a `TypeError` for connection refused or DNS failure) before any `resp` exists; that rejection is not caught and propagates raw rather than as a `RegistryError("network.registry_unreachable", ...)`. The batch path has the same gap (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:648`-`667`). Suggested direction: wrap the `fetcher` calls in `get` and `loadArtifacts` so a rejected fetch becomes a `RegistryError("network.registry_unreachable", ...)`, matching the bridge's envelope code.

### - [x] F-7.4.3 — `podium sync` returns raw transport error in always-revalidate mode instead of `network.registry_unreachable` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit ece18d6): `Run` now classifies a `serverUnreachableError` before falling through. offline-first stays the silent no-op; every other mode (always-revalidate and the default empty value) returns the new `ErrRegistryUnreachable` sentinel (`network.registry_unreachable: …`, mirroring `ErrOfflineCacheMiss`'s namespaced form), so the CLI prints the structured §6.10 code rather than the raw dial error. A reachable 5xx rejection is unaffected, and a filesystem source never produces the transport error. Covered by `TestRun_AlwaysRevalidateServerUnreachable`, `TestRun_AlwaysRevalidateStructuredErrorNotUnreachable`, `TestRun_AlwaysRevalidateFilesystemSourceMaterializes`, and the `TestSyncServerSource_AlwaysRevalidateUnreachable` e2e.

(inconsistency) The spec states that `always-revalidate` returns the structured error `network.registry_unreachable` when there is no cache (`spec/07-external-integration.md:127`) and that `podium sync` applies the same cache modes (`spec/07-external-integration.md:133`). `podium sync` keeps no offline content cache, so an always-revalidate sync against an unreachable server-source registry hits the no-cache branch. `Run` handles only the offline-first case for an unreachable server (`pkg/sync/sync.go:200`-`201`); every other mode, including always-revalidate, falls through to `return nil, err` (`pkg/sync/sync.go:203`), returning the `serverUnreachableError` whose `Error()` is the raw transport message (`pkg/sync/server.go:28`-`30`, `pkg/sync/server.go:187`). The CLI then prints `sync failed: <raw dial error>` (`cmd/podium/main.go:336`-`338`) rather than the structured `network.registry_unreachable` code. The offline-only sync miss does carry a `network.*` code (`pkg/sync/sync.go:43`, `pkg/sync/sync.go:188`), so only the always-revalidate path diverges. Suggested direction: in `Run`, when a `serverUnreachableError` surfaces in always-revalidate mode, return a `network.registry_unreachable` error mirroring `ErrOfflineCacheMiss`'s namespaced form.

### - [x] F-7.4.4 — MCP discovery and search emit `status: "offline"` in offline-first mode despite the "silently" contract [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 2db2f42): a new `offlineEnvelope` helper omits the `status: "offline"` field in offline-first mode and keeps it for always-revalidate, honoring the §7.4 per-mode distinction ("offline-first: no error; serve cached results silently"). It is used by the discovery path (`proxyGet`) and `offlineSearchArtifacts` (`cmd/podium-mcp`). load_artifact keeps its own §12 status semantics (out of this finding's scope). Tests: 3 cmd/podium-mcp units (offline-first silent for discovery + search, always-revalidate keeps status) and 2 e2e (real-binary offline-first silent + always-revalidate status).

(inconsistency) The spec defines `offline-first` as "no error; serve cached results silently" (`spec/07-external-integration.md:128`), which distinguishes it from `always-revalidate`, which surfaces an explicit offline status (`spec/07-external-integration.md:127`). For `search_artifacts`, the bridge routes an unreachable registry through `offlineSearchArtifacts`, which always sets `status: "offline"` regardless of mode (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:29`-`30`, `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:108`-`139`), with the in-code comment stating "always-revalidate and offline-first both report the offline status" (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:25`-`28`). The discovery meta-tools behave the same way through `proxyGet`, returning `offlineResult(offline)` with `status: "offline"` for both modes (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2185`-`2186`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2209`-`2215`). An offline-first caller therefore receives the same explicit offline status as an always-revalidate caller, blurring the spec's "silent" distinction for these tools. These tools keep no content cache, so the practical impact is limited to the presence of the status field. Suggested direction: either omit the `status: "offline"` field for these tools in offline-first mode, or reconcile the spec text if the host-facing status signal is intentional for cacheless tools.

## F-7.5 — 7.5 podium sync (7.5.1 Scope Filters, 7.5.2 sync.yaml, 7.5.3 sync.lock, 7.5.4 Watch/Toggle, 7.5.5 override, 7.5.6 save-as, 7.5.7 profile edit)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.5 against the implementation._

I traced the `podium sync` command family (`sync`, `sync override`, `sync save-as`, `profile edit`) from the CLI in `cmd/podium/main.go` into `pkg/sync` (`config.go`, `resolve.go`, `scope.go`, `lockfile.go`, `sync.go`, `watch.go`, `watch_server.go`, `override.go`, `profile_edit.go`) and `pkg/materialize/atomic.go`. Most concrete claims hold. The scope filters implement the §4.5.2 glob syntax including `*`, `**`, and brace expansion (`pkg/sync/scope.go:117`-`195`), with visibility enforced before scope because the server source reads `GET /v1/sync/manifest` (the effective view) at `pkg/sync/server.go:79`-`82` and the filesystem source walks the composed registry at `pkg/sync/sync.go:445`-`473`. The `--json` envelope matches `{profile, target, harness, scope, artifacts: [{id, version, type, layer}]}` at `cmd/podium/main.go:1410`-`1448`. The §7.5.2 precedence chain (CLI flags, `PODIUM_*`, then the three config scopes, then built-in defaults) is resolved in `pkg/sync/resolve.go:199`-`245`, with whole-profile collision overwrite and the targeted collision warning at `resolve.go:130`-`148` and `resolve.go:220`-`224`. Workspace discovery walks up to `.podium/` at `resolve.go:55`-`68`. The lock-file schema and atomic write match §7.5.3 (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go`), manual sync clears toggles while watch/override preserve them (`pkg/sync/sync.go:206`-`215`, `watch.go:61`-`66`, `override.go:124`-`150`), `last_synced_by` carries `full | watch | override`, and the server watcher subscribes to `artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, and `layer.config_changed` (`watch_server.go:82`). The target directory and `<target>/.podium/` are created (`materialize/atomic.go:225`, `lockfile.go:96`-`98`). Findings below are deviations of limited blast radius.

### - [ ] F-7.5.1 — TUI mode for `sync override` and `profile edit` is absent [Medium] — DEFERRED

Deferred: implementing the full interactive checklist/tree TUIs requires either a new heavy TUI dependency (against the reuse-first rule) or a hand-rolled raw-terminal input loop, for which the codebase has no existing pattern (no `golang.org/x/term` raw-mode use, no stdin prompts anywhere). Such an interactive loop cannot be exercised or verified under the no-interactive-command constraint of this environment, so it cannot meet the batch's test bar. The batch-flag forms cover every underlying operation, and the project already codifies the TUI-deferral contract in a committed e2e test (`TestSync_InteractiveTUIDeferral`). Not unblocked by any other finding in this batch.

(gap) §7.5.5 specifies that `podium sync override` with no flags "launches a checklist over the resolved set + everything else the caller can see" and renders "the caller's effective view as an expandable tree (domains as nodes, artifacts as leaf checkboxes)" (spec/07-external-integration.md:341-342, 356), and §7.5.7 specifies that `podium profile edit` / `podium profile edit finance-team` opens a "TUI for the active or named profile" (spec/07-external-integration.md:393-395). The implementation does not provide either interactive form. `cmd/podium/main.go:507`-`510` prints `interactive override (TUI) is not available; use --add <id>, --remove <id>, or --reset` and returns exit code 2, and `cmd/podium/main.go:660`-`663` prints `interactive profile editing (TUI) is not available` and returns 2. The batch flag forms (`--add`/`--remove`/`--reset`, `--add-include`/`--remove-include`/`--add-exclude`/`--remove-exclude`) cover the underlying operations, so a workaround exists. Suggested direction: implement the checklist and tree TUIs described in §7.5.5 and §7.5.7, or amend the spec to mark the interactive modes as deferred so the contract matches the shipped behavior.

### - [x] F-7.5.2 — `save-as` omits the empty `defaults:` block on a fresh `sync.yaml` [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 3bbc66e): `SaveAs` now detects a freshly created `sync.yaml` and writes it through `writeConfig`/`marshalConfig` with `ensureDefaults`, which prepends an empty `defaults:` mapping ahead of `profiles:`, matching the layout `podium profile edit` produces. Covered by `TestSaveAs_FreshFileEmitsDefaultsBlock`, `TestSaveAs_ExistingFileNoSpuriousDefaults`, and the `TestSyncSaveAs_FreshFileDefaultsAndActivation` e2e.

(inconsistency) §7.5.6 states that when `.podium/sync.yaml` does not exist yet, `save-as` "creates it with the new profile and an empty `defaults:` block" (spec/07-external-integration.md:386). `SaveAs` builds the config via `EnsureConfig`, which returns `&SyncConfig{Profiles: map[string]Profile{}}` with a zero-value `Defaults` (`pkg/sync/config.go:164`-`176`), then writes it with `WriteConfig` (`pkg/sync/override.go:237`-`238`). Because `SyncConfig.Defaults` carries `yaml:"defaults,omitempty"` (`pkg/sync/config.go:25`) and the struct is zero-valued, `yaml.Marshal` emits no `defaults:` key at all; I confirmed the rendered output is `profiles:` only with no `defaults:` line. The sibling command `profile edit` does insert the empty block on a fresh file (`pkg/sync/profile_edit.go:30`-`34`), so the two creation paths diverge. Suggested direction: have `save-as` materialize an empty `defaults:` mapping on a fresh file the way `editProfileYAML` does, so both creation paths produce the structure §7.5.6 and §7.5.7 describe.

### - [x] F-7.5.3 — Redundant `override --add` records a toggle and emits no warning [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 3bbc66e): `Override` now treats an `--add` whose ID is already materialized (present in the lock's `artifacts:` and not pending removal) or already in `toggles.add` as a no-op, skipping the stray toggle and returning an advisory warning that the CLI prints to stderr (§7.5.5). Re-adding an artifact that is pending removal stays a real operation. Covered by `TestOverride_RedundantAddWarnsAndNoOps`, `TestOverride_NonRedundantAddRecordsToggle`, `TestOverride_ReaddPendingRemoveIsRealOp`, and the `TestSyncOverride_RedundantAddWarns` e2e.

(inconsistency) §7.5.5 states that for batch override, "running `--add` on something already materialized is a no-op with a warning" (spec/07-external-integration.md:358). The implementation does not warn, and adding an artifact that the active profile already materializes is not a no-op: `Override` only checks `alreadyAdded(lock.Toggles.Add, id)` (`pkg/sync/override.go:92`-`99`), so an `--add` for an ID that is in the profile's resolved scope but not yet in `toggles.add` appends a fresh `toggles.add` entry and sets `changed = true`. The CLI prints `(no change)` only when `res.Changed` is false (`cmd/podium/main.go:532`-`534`) and never prints a warning for a redundant add. The redundant `toggles.add` entry then survives into a later `save-as`, which turns it into an extra pinned `include:` entry (`pkg/sync/override.go:227`-`229`). Suggested direction: in `Override`, treat an `--add` whose ID is already in the resolved profile set as a no-op and emit a stderr warning, matching the §7.5.5 wording.

### - [x] F-7.5.4 — Lock file omits `profile:` instead of writing `profile: null` when no profile is active [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 3bbc66e): `LockFile.Profile` is now a `nullProfile` type whose `MarshalYAML` emits the YAML null literal for the empty name and the plain name otherwise, and the field dropped `omitempty`, so a profile-less sync records the explicit `profile: null` the §7.5.3 schema documents. The default decoder reads both `profile: null` and a named profile back into the string. Covered by `TestLock_NoProfileSerializesNull`, `TestLock_ProfileSerializesNameAndRoundTrips`, `TestLock_NullProfileReadsBackEmpty`, and the `TestSync_NoProfileLockRendersNull` e2e.

(inconsistency) The §7.5.3 lock schema shows `profile: finance-team` annotated "null when no profile was used" (spec/07-external-integration.md:286). The `LockFile.Profile` field carries `yaml:"profile,omitempty"` (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:16`), so a sync with no active profile omits the `profile:` key entirely rather than serializing `profile: null`; I confirmed the rendered lock contains no `profile:` line in that case. The schema annotation is informal and YAML readers treat an absent key and an explicit `null` equivalently, so the impact is cosmetic. Suggested direction: either serialize `profile: null` without `omitempty` to match the documented schema, or relax the spec annotation to say the key is omitted when no profile is used.

## F-7.6 — 7.6 Language SDKs (7.6.1 Read CLI, 7.6.2 Bulk Fetch)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.6 against the implementation._

I reviewed the §7.6 SDK surface, the §7.6.1 Read CLI, and the §7.6.2 Bulk Fetch endpoint against the Go CLI in `cmd/podium`, the registry handlers in `pkg/registry/server`, the core resolution in `pkg/registry/core`, the MCP prefetch in `cmd/podium-mcp`, and the two SDKs under `sdks/podium-py` and `sdks/podium-ts`. Most concrete claims hold. The batch endpoint is registered at `POST /v1/artifacts:batchLoad` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:331`), the request and per-item envelope field names match the §7.6.2 wire example (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:19-58`), and the 50-ID hard cap is enforced server-side with `registry.invalid_argument` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:15,80-83`). Both SDKs split larger sets into 50-ID chunks transparently (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:697-720`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:635-671`). Visibility denial and not-found both collapse to `visibility.denied` so no existence leak occurs (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:148-155`, backed by `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1311-1323`), partial failure keeps HTTP 200 with per-item status (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:90,99-104`), session-consistent `latest` freezing is honored through the shared core path (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1379-1418`), and explicit `version_pins` bypass the session pin correctly. The MCP server warms its cache through the same endpoint when `prefetch` is configured (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2085-2135`). The Read CLI exposes `podium search`, `podium domain search`, `podium domain show`, and `podium artifact show` with the documented flags (`cmd/podium/main.go:776-994`), the human renderer prints the `Showing N of M results` prefix (`cmd/podium/main.go:1277`), and `podium artifact show` prints only the manifest body and frontmatter without materializing resources (`cmd/podium/main.go:988-993`).

The findings concern the documented `--json` schemas in the §7.6.1 table and one batch resource-delivery edge case. The CLI emits each read endpoint's raw response under `--json`, and three of the documented schemas name keys that the wire response does not use or deliberately omits. One additional finding covers batch resource delivery when no object store is configured.

### - [x] F-7.6.1 — `podium domain search --json` emits `domains`, spec documents `results` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 05bf46f): `podium domain search --json` now emits the §7.6.1 envelope, keying the ranked domains under `results` instead of the wire `domains` key. The CLI maps the raw `/v1/search_domains` response into the documented schema in `emitDomainSearchJSON` (`cmd/podium/read_cli_json.go`) rather than echoing the wire body. Covered by a CLI unit test and the `TestCLI_DomainSearchJSON` e2e.

(inconsistency) The §7.6.1 `--json` schema for `podium domain search <query>` documents the ranked domains under a `results` key: `{ "query": "...", "total_matched": 8, "results": [ { "path": "...", "name": "...", ... } ] }` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:498-503`). The CLI echoes the raw `/v1/search_domains` response under `--json` (`cmd/podium/main.go:926-929`), and that handler serializes the domain entries under the JSON key `domains`, not `results` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:650-657`, with `SearchResponse.Domains` tagged `json:"domains"` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:456`). The human renderer also reads `domains` (`cmd/podium/main.go:1382-1386`), confirming the wire key. A `jq` pipeline written against the documented schema reads `.results[]` and gets nothing for domain search, while the same key works for `podium search`. Suggested direction: either rename the `domain search` wire key to `results` (or add a `results` alias) so it matches the documented schema and the artifact-search envelope, or correct the §7.6.1 example to `domains`.

### - [x] F-7.6.2 — `podium artifact show --json` emits `manifest_body`, spec documents `body` [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 05bf46f): `podium artifact show --json` now emits the §7.6.1 envelope `{id, version, content_hash, frontmatter, body}`. `emitArtifactShowJSON` (`cmd/podium/read_cli_json.go`) keys the manifest text `body` (the wire calls it `manifest_body`) and parses the raw frontmatter string into an object. Covered by CLI unit tests and the `TestCLI_ArtifactShow` / `TestCLI_ArtifactShowJSON` e2e cases.

(inconsistency) The §7.6.1 `--json` schema for `podium artifact show <id>` documents `{ "id": "...", "version": "...", "content_hash": "...", "frontmatter": { ... }, "body": "..." }` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:515-517`). The CLI prints the raw `/v1/load_artifact` response verbatim under `--json` (`cmd/podium/main.go:987-991`), and that response carries the manifest text under `manifest_body`, with no `body` key (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:463-469`, where `ManifestBody` is tagged `json:"manifest_body"`). A `jq` consumer reading `.body` per the spec finds nothing. The same example shows `frontmatter` as a nested object `{ ... }`, but the wire delivers it as a JSON string (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:469`); this part is a representational illustration rather than a field-name break. Suggested direction: align the §7.6.1 example to the wire key `manifest_body` (and note that `frontmatter` is a string), or have the CLI re-map the response to the documented `body` key before emitting `--json`.

### - [x] F-7.6.3 — `podium search --json` never includes the documented `frontmatter` result field [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 05bf46f): search descriptors now carry the artifact frontmatter block per §7.6.1. The stored manifest bytes are the full ARTIFACT.md source, so the core `descriptorOf` splits off and delivers only the `---`fenced`---` frontmatter (the prose body stays at the registry until `load_artifact`, per §5), and the registry handler no longer blanks it. `podium search --json` emits it as a parsed object, and both SDKs surface it on search results (the §7.6.1 1:1 CLI/SDK mapping). The MCP bridge strips frontmatter from the agent-facing results so the §5 meta-tool surface stays lean and uniform with overlay descriptors. Covered by core, server, CLI, MCP, and SDK unit tests plus the read-CLI e2e.

(inconsistency) The §7.6.1 `--json` schema for `podium search` documents each result as `{ "id": "...", "type": "...", "version": "...", "score": 0.83, "frontmatter": { ... } }` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:495-496`). The search handler deliberately clears the frontmatter on every result before serializing (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:688-689`: `d.Frontmatter = ""`), and `Frontmatter` carries `omitempty` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:444`), so the key is absent from the `--json` output the CLI echoes (`cmd/podium/main.go:810-814`). The Python SDK likewise does not read `frontmatter` from search results (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:560-570`). The omission follows §3.2/§5 (search returns descriptors only and the body stays at the registry until `load_artifact`), so the §7.6.1 schema text is the likely defect, but the documented `--json` contract and the implementation disagree. Suggested direction: remove `frontmatter` from the §7.6.1 `podium search --json` example to match §3.2/§5 and the implemented descriptor surface, or reconcile the spec on whether search descriptors carry frontmatter.

### - [x] F-7.6.4 — Batch path drops inline resources when no object store is configured [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 83322b4): `loadOneForBatch` delivers inline resources when no object store is configured (new `inline`/`inline_base64` fields on `BatchResource`) instead of dropping them, mirroring the single-load path; with an object store it still presigns. The Python and TypeScript batch `materialize` helpers consume the inline fields. Covered by a server unit test, a no-object-store integration round-trip, SDK unit tests, and a standalone-server e2e.

(inconsistency) §7.6.2 states that bundled resources travel via presigned URLs so the response body stays small (`spec/07-external-integration.md:580`), and the wire example shows every batch resource as `{path, presigned_url, content_hash}` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:562-564`). The batch handler attaches resources only when an object store is configured: `if s.objectStore != nil` guards the entire resource loop and otherwise omits the references (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:122-138`). The single-artifact `load_artifact` path instead returns small resources inline directly from the bytes ingest stored on the record, even with no object store, because `inlineBytes` returns `ref.Inline` before consulting the store (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:935-942,968-971`). A deployment with no object store but inline-stored bundled resources therefore delivers those resources through `load_artifact` but silently drops them from `batchLoad`, so a batch consumer materializes a package missing files that the single-load path would have written. Suggested direction: in the no-object-store branch of `loadOneForBatch`, deliver small resources inline (mirroring `attachResources`) instead of omitting them, or document that batch loading requires a configured data plane and surface a per-item error rather than silently returning an incomplete artifact.

## F-7.7 — 7.7 Onboarding: podium init, config show, login

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md §7.7 against the implementation._

I reviewed the onboarding commands `podium init`, `podium config show`, `podium login`, and `podium logout` against `spec/07-external-integration.md` lines 584-662. The three commands are wired in `cmd/podium/main.go:41-70` and implemented in `cmd/podium/main.go:996` (`initCmd`), `cmd/podium/config.go:36` (`configShow`) with `cmd/podium/clientconfig.go` (provenance resolution), and `cmd/podium/login.go:30` (`loginCmd`) with `cmd/podium/login.go:300` (`logoutCmd`).

Most concrete claims hold. `podium init` writes a `defaults` block to `sync.yaml`, honors `--global` and `--local` scope targeting, refuses to overwrite without `--force`, and resolves the standalone shortcut to `http://127.0.0.1:8080` (`cmd/podium/main.go:1014-1019`, `1084-1098`). Workspace mode walks up to an existing `.podium/` via `sync.DiscoverWorkspace` (`cmd/podium/main.go:1070-1075`, `pkg/sync/resolve.go:55`), adds `.podium/sync.local.yaml` and `.podium/overlay/` to `.gitignore` (`cmd/podium/main.go:1105-1110`), and prints next-step hints (`cmd/podium/main.go:1115-1121`). `podium login` resolves the registry from `--registry`, `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, then the merged `sync.yaml` (`cmd/podium/login.go:145-160`), no-ops for filesystem and standalone registries (`cmd/podium/login.go:55-58`, `165-170`), bounds the flow to a 10-minute deadline (`cmd/podium/login.go:24`, `90`), caches access and refresh tokens in the keychain keyed by registry URL (`cmd/podium/login.go:233-243`, `pkg/identity/keychain.go:30-48`), prints the verification URL and user code to stderr (`cmd/podium/login.go:98-99`), honors `--no-browser` and `PODIUM_NO_BROWSER` truthy values `1`/`true`/`yes`/`on` (`cmd/podium/login.go:202-208`), and prints `sub`, `email`, and OIDC groups on success (`cmd/podium/login.go:248-291`). `podium logout` clears both the access and refresh entries (`cmd/podium/login.go:314-318`).

The findings are limited to cosmetic and additive deviations in `config show` output formatting, plus one ambiguity in the documented login exit conditions. No correctness, auth, or data-integrity defects were found.

### - [x] F-7.7.1 — config show profile output omits per-field provenance [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 58d4a6c): the human `config show` view now prints each profile field with the scope it resolved from (`include: [...]   (from <ws>/.podium/sync.yaml)`), matching the §7.7 example. The profile header stands alone; a profile with no printable fields keeps its source on the header so provenance is never dropped (whole-profile overwrite per §7.5.2 means every field shares the winning scope). Covered by `TestConfigClientShow_ProfileFieldProvenance` and `TestConfigClientShow_EmptyProfileHeaderProvenance`.

(inconsistency) The §7.7 `config show` example at `spec/07-external-integration.md:634-639` renders each profile field with its own provenance annotation (`include:           ["finance/**", "shared/policies/*"]   (from <ws>/.podium/sync.yaml)`) and a `(defined in <ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml)` annotation on the profile header line. The implementation in `cmd/podium/clientconfig.go:172-175` prints a single `profiles.<name>:   (from <winner>)` header and then the field lines from `profileLines` (`cmd/podium/clientconfig.go:228-246`) with no per-field provenance. The merged result and the winning scope are reported, but the per-field source attribution shown in the spec example is absent. Suggested direction: either annotate each rendered profile field with the scope it resolved from, or treat the spec example as illustrative and relax its per-field provenance text.

### - [x] F-7.7.2 — config show appends server settings table to the client view by default [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 58d4a6c): bare `podium config show` now prints only the merged client sync.yaml with per-key provenance, matching the §7.7 example. The resolved server settings table (and the JSON `settings` key) are isolated behind `--server`, where the §13.10/§13.12 knobs already lived. `configEffectiveShow` and its dead `clientPayloadAt` helper were removed. The doc-accuracy e2e tests that verify server settings (identity_provider, backend selectors, read_only probe, public_mode, scope_preview, embedding, layer_path) were migrated to `config show --server`; the two tests asserting client values (quickstart table, deployment registry) are unchanged. Covered by `TestConfigShow_BareOmitsServerSettings` and `TestConfigShow_BareJSONHasNoSettings`.

(inconsistency) §7.7 at `spec/07-external-integration.md:625-642` describes `podium config show` as printing the merged `sync.yaml` with per-key provenance, and the example output contains only the client merged config. The default path in `cmd/podium/config.go:63-82` (`configEffectiveShow`) prints the client merged config and then also appends a server settings table from `serverboot.LoadConfig().Settings()` (`cmd/podium/config.go:80-81`), and in JSON mode injects a `settings` key into the payload (`cmd/podium/config.go:73`). The server settings belong to §13.10/§13.12, and `config show --server` already isolates them (`cmd/podium/config.go:46-47`, `88-96`); emitting them unconditionally in the bare `config show` diverges from the §7.7 example, which shows client config only. Suggested direction: print only the client merged config for bare `config show`, and keep the server settings behind `--server`, or document the combined output in §7.7.

### - [x] F-7.7.3 — login exit on auth.untrusted_runtime is unreachable in the device-code flow [Info] — CLOSED

**Resolution (CLOSED):** Removed the unreachable exit condition from §7.7 after the maintainer approved the spec edit. `spec/07-external-integration.md:657` now reads "Exits non-zero on timeout or denial." `podium login` runs the device-code flow only (`cmd/podium/login.go`, `flow.Poll`), whose surfaced errors are timeout (`context.DeadlineExceeded`/`ErrExpiredToken`) and denial (`ErrAccessDenied`); both return 1. `auth.untrusted_runtime` is produced exclusively by the injected-session-token server-side request verifier (`pkg/identity/runtime.go`, §6.3.2) and is structurally unreachable from interactive login, so the §7.7 sentence had conflated the runtime-token path with the login path. No code change; the code already handled every reachable outcome.

Deferred: §6.3.2 and §6.10 bind `auth.untrusted_runtime` exclusively to the `injected-session-token` provider's server-side request verification (`pkg/identity/runtime.go`). The `podium login` device-code flow (§7.7: "Explicit OAuth device-code flow") never injects a session token and never triggers runtime-key verification, so the exit condition is unreachable by design — the device-code token endpoint yields only `access_denied` (denial) and `expired_token`/timeout, both already handled. The finding itself rates this Info and reads it as a spec-side conflation. The only resolution is removing `auth.untrusted_runtime` from the §7.7 login exit list, a `spec/` edit forbidden by ground rule A. No code defect; no code change. Not unblocked by F-7.7.1/F-7.7.2 (unrelated `config show` surface).

(gap) §7.7 at `spec/07-external-integration.md:657` states that `podium login` "Exits non-zero on timeout, denial, or `auth.untrusted_runtime`." The implementation handles timeout (`cmd/podium/login.go:116-117`, returns 1) and denial (`ErrAccessDenied` propagates from `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:214-215` through `Poll` at `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:316-317` and `loginCmd` returns 1 at `cmd/podium/login.go:121`), but `auth.untrusted_runtime` is produced only by injected-session-token verification in `pkg/identity/runtime.go:24-48` (§6.3.2), which the device-code login path never invokes. The login command therefore cannot reach an `untrusted_runtime` outcome, so the documented third exit condition has no corresponding code path. This reads as a spec-side conflation of the runtime-token path with the interactive login path rather than a missing implementation branch. Suggested direction: confirm whether §7.7 should list `auth.untrusted_runtime` for `podium login` at all; if not, remove it from the login exit conditions in the spec.

## F-8.1 — 8.1 What Gets Logged

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md §8.1 against the implementation._

The section defines the registry audit event catalog, the trace-ID requirement, the two-stream model (registry-owned events plus an optional MCP `LocalAuditSink`), and the caller-identity contract for read events. The event catalog is complete: every event named in the §8.1 table at `spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:9-26` has a constant in `pkg/audit/audit.go:31-48` and an emission site. Read events emit from `pkg/registry/core/core.go:463` (`domain.loaded`), `pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go:60` (`domains.searched`), `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1004` (`artifacts.searched`), and `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1285` (`artifact.loaded`); ingest and orchestration emit `artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, `artifact.signed`, `domain.published`, `layer.ingested`, `layer.history_rewritten`, and `freeze.break_glass` at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:728-762` and `pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:123-176`; `layer.config_changed` and `layer.user_registered` emit from `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:148-158`; `admin.granted` from `pkg/registry/server/admin.go:56`; `visibility.denied` from `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1318`; `user.erased` from `pkg/audit/retention.go:227`; and `registry.read_only_entered`/`exited` from `internal/serverboot/readonly_audit.go:18-34`.

The §8.1 caller-identity contract for registry read events holds. The identity middleware captures the trace id, the structured caller identity (email and groups), and public-mode network attributes at the HTTP boundary in `pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:59-72`, and the core emit adapter recovers them and attaches them to the persisted event in `internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:43-52`. Public-mode and anonymous callers render `caller = "system:public"` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1606-1614`), and the public-mode source IP and `X-Forwarded-User` header are recorded in the network attributes (`pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:68-69`). The findings below concern the trace-id sharing between the two streams and the wire-key naming relative to the spec's dotted prose.

### - [x] F-8.1.1 — MCP local audit events carry no trace ID, so the two streams do not share one [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 2db2f42): a new `traceID` helper extracts the in-flight call's span trace id from `s.activeCtx` (the same span the otelhttp transport injects as the W3C `traceparent` header the registry derives its stream's trace id from), and `auditMeta`, `auditSearch`, and the new `auditLoadArtifact` stamp it on the local `audit.Event`. With tracing off (no recording span) no id is written, matching the registry path. Both §8.1 streams now share one trace id per call. Tests: 3 cmd/podium-mcp units (auditMeta/auditSearch stamp it, none when tracing off) and 1 integration (real binary: the local event's trace_id equals the traceparent injected to the registry stub).

(bug) §8.1 states the registry and the MCP local audit form two streams and that "Both streams share trace IDs" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:28`). The registry stream derives its trace id from the W3C `traceparent` header the bridge injects (`pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:79-86`), so the registry-side read event for a given meta-tool call carries a trace id. The MCP local sink, however, builds its events with `context.Background()` and never sets `TraceID`: `auditMeta` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:597-602` and `auditSearch` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:613-619` both append an `audit.Event` with no `TraceID` field. The trace context for the in-flight call is available on `s.activeCtx` (set in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1035-1037`) and is injected into the outbound registry request through the otelhttp transport, but it is not extracted into the local audit event. The result is that the registry stream records a trace id while the MCP local stream records an empty trace id for the same call, so the two streams cannot be correlated by trace id as §8.1 requires. Suggested direction: extract the active span's trace id from `s.activeCtx` (the same value the otelhttp transport propagates) and set it on the `audit.Event` in both `auditMeta` and `auditSearch` so the local stream shares the trace id with the registry stream.

### - [x] F-8.1.2 — Audit wire keys use `caller`/`caller_network`/`caller_public_mode` rather than the spec's dotted `caller.*` names [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 9b83b84): the JSON-Lines wire form now nests the caller-identity attributes under a single `caller` object whose keys are the dotted names §8.1 illustrates: `caller.identity` (the sub-claim or `system:public`), `caller.email`, `caller.groups`, `caller.network` (`source_ip` / `forwarded_user`), and `caller.public_mode`. A SIEM consumer keying on the dotted path `caller.public_mode` resolves the nested field directly; the flat `caller_email` / `caller_groups` / `caller_network` / `caller_public_mode` keys are gone. The hash-chain canonical body is unchanged (it never reaches a consumer), so tamper-evidence and existing chains are preserved. Covered by `pkg/audit` round-trip and typed-decode units, server/serverboot emission tests, and the `TestHTTPAPI_PublicModeAudit` e2e.

(inconsistency) §8.1 describes the caller-identity attributes using dotted names: `caller.identity = "<sub-claim>"`, `caller.network`, and `caller.public_mode: true` (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:30`). The JSON-Lines wire format serializes the identity string under `caller` (not `caller.identity`), the network attributes under `caller_network`, and the public-mode flag under `caller_public_mode` (`pkg/audit/file.go:165-185`). The dotted names in the spec are informal prose rather than a normative wire-format block, and the underlying attributes are all present and tamper-evident (`pkg/audit/audit.go:136-141`), so this is a naming-only deviation. A SIEM consumer keying on the literal field names `caller.identity` or `caller.public_mode` would not find them. Suggested direction: either align the spec prose with the flat snake_case wire keys the implementation already emits, or document the mapping (for example `caller.public_mode` maps to the JSON key `caller_public_mode`) so downstream consumers parse the correct field names.

## F-8.2 — 8.2 PII Redaction

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md §8.2 against the implementation._

I reviewed both redaction surfaces §8.2 names: manifest-declared field redaction and default-on query-text scrubbing. The query-text surface is fully implemented and wired. `pkg/audit/redact.go:82` defines `NewPIIScrubber` with default patterns for SSN, credit-card, email, and phone, matching the spec's named cases; I confirmed by execution that all four patterns match representative inputs. The registry emits `artifacts.searched` and `domains.searched` events with the free-text query in `Context["query"]` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1006`, `pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go:62`), and the audit emitter applies `scrubber.ScrubEvent` before `sink.Append` (`internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:42`). The MCP server applies the same scrub on its local sink (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:618`). The `PIIRedactionConfig` surface exists with the tri-state `Enabled` field that is default-on when absent (`pkg/audit/redact.go:36`), supports appended custom patterns (`pkg/audit/redact.go:42`), is loaded from `registry.yaml` `pii_redaction` and `PODIUM_PII_REDACTION` with env winning the toggle (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:324`), and is surfaced in config output (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1418`).

The manifest-declared surface is wired but functionally limited. The manifest field `audit_redact` is parsed (`pkg/manifest/types.go:115`), merged (`pkg/manifest/merge.go:117`), carried as `RedactKeys` on read events (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1355`), and passed to `audit.RedactFields` on publish/deprecate/sign events (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:750`). `RedactFields` correctly replaces matching keys with `[redacted]` (`pkg/audit/redact.go:145`). The findings below concern the gap between the spec's illustrated directive fields and the keys that actually reach the audit context.

### - [x] F-8.2.1 — Manifest-declared redaction cannot redact the example fields it names [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 826bd1a): the registry now surfaces the author-named sensitive frontmatter fields into the audit context so the `audit_redact` directive has a concrete target, then masks them to `[redacted]` before any event reaches a sink. A new `manifest.FrontmatterFields` extracts the named scalar fields from the stored frontmatter; the ingest publish/deprecated/signed events and the `artifact.loaded` read event merge them in and redact. The read path derives the `audit_redact` key set from the persisted frontmatter (the SQL backends do not store `AuditRedact` as its own column), so redaction now works uniformly across the memory, SQLite, and Postgres stores. Covered by a `pkg/manifest` unit test, `pkg/registry/core` read-event and `pkg/registry/ingest` publish-event unit tests, and an e2e that forwards the audit stream to a recorder and asserts the field is `[redacted]` while the raw value never leaks.

(inconsistency) The spec states "Artifact manifests can specify fields that should be redacted in audit logs (e.g., `bank_account`, `ssn`). The registry honors redaction directives" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:36`). The implementation only ever writes a fixed structural set of keys into every audit event's context: `version`, `content_hash`, and `layer` for read and publish events (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1350`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:750`), plus `query`, `scope`, and `type` for search events (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1006`). No artifact-author-supplied manifest field value ever flows into the audit context. `RedactFields` only replaces keys that are present in the context map (`pkg/audit/redact.go:154`), so an `audit_redact` directive listing `bank_account` or `ssn` matches nothing and redacts nothing. The mechanism functions only for the structural keys (`version`, `content_hash`, `layer`), which an author is unlikely to name in `audit_redact`. The spec's example is informal, which is why this is rated Low, but the directive as illustrated has no effect because the named fields are never emitted to audit. Suggested direction: either emit the manifest fields named in `audit_redact` into the audit context (so redaction has a target) or revise the spec example to reflect that redaction applies to the structural read-event context keys rather than arbitrary artifact content fields.

### - [x] F-8.2.2 — MCP local sink writes no manifest fields, so "applies the same directives" is inert [Info] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 2db2f42): the MCP server now applies the manifest `audit_redact` directive to its local sink. The new `auditLoadArtifact` parses the resolved frontmatter, surfaces the author-named sensitive fields into the local `artifact.loaded` event context via `manifest.FrontmatterFields`, and masks them with `audit.RedactFields` before the event reaches the sink, mirroring the registry-side F-8.2.1 path. The event is emitted from the load paths (`deliverLoadArtifact` and `loadArtifactFromOverlay`) where the frontmatter is available, replacing the bare dispatch-time `auditMeta` for load_artifact. Tests: 2 cmd/podium-mcp units (directive redacts the named field; no directive yields no redaction) and 1 e2e (real binary, real server: the local sink's artifact.loaded masks bank_account and never leaks the raw value).

(inconsistency) The spec states "the MCP server applies the same directives before writing to its local audit sink" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:36`). The MCP server's `load_artifact` audit path calls `auditMeta`, which writes only the artifact ID as `Target` and a fixed `Context: {"source": "mcp"}` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:597`, dispatched at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1078`). The MCP server never constructs `RedactKeys`, never calls `audit.RedactFields`, and never writes any manifest field into its local sink context (confirmed by the absence of `RedactFields`/`AuditRedact`/`RedactKeys` in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`). The local sink therefore has no redactable manifest fields, so applying the directives is moot rather than violated. This is rated Info because no PII is leaked; the MCP server simply does not carry the data the directive would mask. Suggested direction: confirm the intended local-sink content; if manifest fields are never meant to reach the local sink, adjust the spec wording so it does not assert that the MCP server applies manifest-declared field redaction there.

## F-8.3 — 8.3 Audit Sinks

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md §8.3 against the implementation._

Section 8.3 describes the two audit sinks: the registry's own sink for catalogue events and the MCP server's local file log. The concrete, checkable claims are the enablement env var `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK`, the interface name `LocalAuditSink` the MCP server writes through, the default path `~/.podium/audit.log` (user-wide, one file across all workspaces), the workspace-override path example, and the claim that both sinks can be redirected to external SIEM or log aggregation independently.

Most of these hold. `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` distinguishes unset (registry-only) from set-but-empty/`default` (local file) via `os.LookupEnv` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:269`, and `newAuditSink` routes the value to a file sink or an HTTP endpoint sink at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:565-581`. The local sink default resolves to `~/.podium/audit.log` under the user home directory at `pkg/audit/file.go:34-40`, satisfying the user-wide one-file invariant. A workspace override is honored because the env value is passed through verbatim to `NewFileSink`. The MCP server records meta-tool events through the sink at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1069` and `1078`. The local sink's external-SIEM redirect is implemented by `audit.EndpointSink`, which POSTs each hash-chained event to an `http(s)` URL (`pkg/audit/endpoint.go:42-87`), selected when the value carries an `http://` or `https://` prefix (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:585-587`).

Two findings remain: the implementation interface is named `audit.Sink` rather than the spec's `LocalAuditSink`, and the registry sink cannot be redirected to an external endpoint the way the local sink can, leaving the "independently" redirection claim only half-met in code.

### - [x] F-8.3.1 — Registry sink has no external-endpoint redirect path [Medium] — CLOSED
