Resolution (6080642): `openAuditSink` now builds an `audit.EndpointSink` when `PODIUM_AUDIT_LOG_PATH` is an http(s) URL, mirroring the local sink, so the registry sink can be redirected to a SIEM independently (§8.3). Catalogue, HTTP-boundary, read-only-transition, and outbox events flow through the `audit.Sink` interface; the file-only anchor/verify/retention and §8.5 erasure paths run against the `*FileSink` (nil when redirected). Covered by openAuditSink units, an e2e boot-to-SIEM test, and an integration endpoint-redirect erase test.

(gap) §8.3 states "Both the registry and local sinks can be redirected to external SIEM / log aggregation independently" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:41`). The local sink supports this: `newAuditSink` builds an `audit.EndpointSink` when `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` is an `http(s)` URL (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:577-578`, `pkg/audit/endpoint.go:42-87`). The registry sink has no equivalent. The standalone registry constructs its sink only through `openAuditSink`, which always calls `audit.NewFileSink` and never `audit.NewEndpointSink` (`internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:26-38`); the registry path config `PODIUM_AUDIT_LOG_PATH` is consumed solely as a filesystem path (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1507`, `internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:106-115`). A repo-wide search shows `NewEndpointSink` is referenced in non-test code only at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:578`, so the registry cannot push to a SIEM endpoint. External shipping of the registry log is possible only by tailing the JSON-Lines file out of band, which is not an in-process redirect comparable to the local sink. Suggested direction: teach `openAuditSink` to recognize an `http(s)` value of `PODIUM_AUDIT_LOG_PATH` (or a dedicated endpoint key) and construct an `audit.EndpointSink`, mirroring the local sink, so both sinks can be redirected independently as the spec claims.

### - [x] F-8.3.2 — Local sink interface is named `Sink`, not `LocalAuditSink` [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (6080642): added `audit.LocalAuditSink` and `audit.RegistryAuditSink` type aliases for `audit.Sink` so the §9.1 SPI-table names exist as Go types (§9.1 itself states "the `audit.Sink` interface is the seam"). The MCP server's local-sink field and `newAuditSink` return are now typed `audit.LocalAuditSink`, making the alias load-bearing for the §8.3 local log. Covered by a unit test asserting the aliases are interchangeable with `Sink`.

(inconsistency) §8.3 says the local file log "is written by the MCP server through the `LocalAuditSink` interface" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:41`), and §9 lists `LocalAuditSink` as the canonical SPI name (`spec/09-extensibility.md:22`). The implementation exposes the interface as `audit.Sink` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:150-154`), and `LocalAuditSink` exists nowhere as a Go type or interface; it appears only in code comments and test names (for example `pkg/audit/file.go:16`, `pkg/audit/endpoint.go:18`, `test/e2e/plugin_spi_test.go:1273`). The MCP server stores and writes through a field typed `audit.Sink` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:565`, `593-600`). This matches the package-qualified naming the codebase uses for its other §9 SPIs (`identity.Provider`, `overlay.Provider`), so the divergence is cosmetic, but the exact interface name the spec references does not exist in code. Suggested direction: either rename or alias the interface to `LocalAuditSink` to match the spec's SPI table, or update §8.3 and §9 to use the package-qualified `audit.Sink` name the implementation already exposes.

## F-8.4 — 8.4 Retention

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md §8.4 against the implementation._

The subsection lists four retention defaults that are configurable per deployment: audit-event metadata at 1 year, query text at 30 days with placeholder redaction after 7 days, deprecated artifact versions at 90 days after the deprecation flag is set, and owner-unregistered layers at 30 days with soft-delete recoverable via admin. It also describes optional per-event-type sampling of high-volume low-sensitivity events, citing `domain.loaded` at a 10% sample. Most of these contracts are implemented. The audit-event metadata window is enforced by a scheduler that defaults to enabled with a 1-year (365-day) max age (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1517-1518`, `internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:27`). The query-text window is implemented with placeholder-at-7-days and drop-at-30-days defaults (`pkg/audit/retention.go:46-52`, `pkg/audit/retention.go:58-79`) and is driven from the same pass (`internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:57`); search events store the redacted field under the `query` context key the retention logic targets (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1006`, `pkg/audit/retention.go:24`). Sampling is wired with the documented env var and consulted before an event enters the hash chain (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1520`, `internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:25-27`, `pkg/audit/sampler.go:42-54`). The deprecated-version and layer-recovery purges have correct default windows of 90 and 30 days and correct store implementations across memory, SQLite, and Postgres (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1523-1524`, `pkg/store/sqlite.go:452-462`, `pkg/store/postgres.go:775-801`), with `deprecated_at` anchored on ingest (`pkg/store/store.go:301-310`) and recovery exposed through `podium layer restore` and `/v1/layers/restore` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:327-349`).

One material gap concerns enforcement of the store-level windows: the scheduler that applies the 90-day and 30-day defaults is disabled out of the box, so two of the four spec-listed retention defaults never take effect unless an operator opts in. Two further observations about the deprecation anchor timestamp and the set of event types covered by the default audit policy are recorded as Info.

### - [x] F-8.4.1 — Store retention (deprecated versions, layer purge) disabled by default [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (6080642): `PODIUM_STORE_RETENTION_INTERVAL_SECONDS` now defaults to `86400` (one day, matching the audit-retention scheduler) so the §8.4 90-day deprecated-version and 30-day owner-unregistered-layer windows are enforced out of the box; `0` remains the explicit disable value. Covered by `LoadConfig` default-on / explicit-disable / env-override unit tests (the default-on test fails on the prior `0` default).

(gap) §8.4 lists the deprecated-artifact-version window (`90 days after the deprecation flag is set`) and the owner-unregistered-layer window (`30 days`) under the heading `Defaults, configurable per deployment:` (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:45,51,52`), which states these are enforced defaults. The store-retention scheduler that applies both windows is started only when `cfg.storeRetentionInterval > 0` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1088-1090`), and that interval is sourced from `envInt("PODIUM_STORE_RETENTION_INTERVAL_SECONDS", 0)`, defaulting to `0` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1522`). When the interval is non-positive the scheduler returns immediately without registering any sweep (`internal/serverboot/store_retention.go:25-28`), and the only callers of `PurgeDeprecatedManifests` and `PurgeExpiredLayerDeletions` are inside that scheduler (`internal/serverboot/store_retention.go:47,56`). As a result, deprecated artifact versions are never purged after 90 days and soft-deleted layers are never hard-deleted after 30 days in a default deployment, even though the window values default correctly to 90 and 30. This asymmetry contrasts with the audit-event retention scheduler, which defaults to enabled with `PODIUM_AUDIT_RETENTION_INTERVAL_SECONDS` at `86400` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1517`). Suggested direction: default `PODIUM_STORE_RETENTION_INTERVAL_SECONDS` to a positive cadence (for example one day, matching the audit retention default) so the §8.4 90-day and 30-day defaults are enforced out of the box, and keep `0` as the explicit disable value.

### - [x] F-8.4.2 — Deprecated-version window anchored to ingest time, not flag-set time [Info] — CLOSED

Resolution (6080642): confirmed deprecation is only ever set at ingest. `deprecated` is a per-version manifest frontmatter field, so deprecating an artifact ingests a distinct record (new content hash) with its own `IngestedAt`; there is no in-place toggle that flips an already-stored version. Anchoring `DeprecatedAt` to that version's `IngestedAt` therefore equals "90 days after the deprecation flag is set" (§8.4). Documented the invariant on `stampDeprecation` and added a unit test asserting a born-deprecated version and a later deprecation flip each anchor to their own ingest time, not an earlier version's. No behavior change.

(inconsistency) §8.4 specifies the deprecated-artifact-version window as `90 days after the deprecation flag is set` (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:51`). The store anchors the window to `IngestedAt` rather than to the moment the deprecation flag transitions: `stampDeprecation` sets `DeprecatedAt` from `IngestedAt` (falling back to now) whenever a manifest is deprecated and the timestamp is unset (`pkg/store/store.go:301-310`), and the purge compares `deprecated_at < before` (`pkg/store/sqlite.go:455`, `pkg/store/postgres.go:460`, `pkg/store/memory.go:191`). In this implementation a version's deprecated state is fixed at ingest time and the flag is treated as set when the deprecated version is stored, which the code comment documents (`pkg/store/store.go:296-300`). This matches the spec under the reading that deprecation is an authoring-time manifest field set at ingest, so a separate flag-flip timestamp does not exist; the divergence only matters if deprecation could later be toggled on an already-stored fresh version. Suggested direction: confirm that deprecation is only ever set at ingest, and if a post-ingest deprecation path is added, stamp `DeprecatedAt` at that transition instead of inheriting `IngestedAt`.

### - [x] F-8.4.3 — Default audit retention policy omits integrity and erasure event types [Info] — CLOSED

Resolution (6080642): every audit event type is now explicitly classified. `operationalEventTypes` (including the previously-omitted `admin.visibility_override`) carry the §8.4 1-year metadata default; `retainedIndefinitelyEventTypes` (the §8.6 anchor/gap/retention-marker integrity events and the §8.5 `user.erased` GDPR-accountability record) carry no default policy and are documented as deliberately kept indefinitely so an external anchor of a superseded head can still be reconciled and the erasure record persists (§8.4 frames the windows as configurable defaults). Added `audit.AllEventTypes` and a completeness-guard test that fails if any type is unclassified, plus a test asserting the integrity/erasure types carry no policy.

(inconsistency) §8.4 lists `Audit events (metadata)` with a 1-year default and frames it as a blanket retention for audit events (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:49`). The default policy table built at boot, `defaultRetentionPolicies`, enumerates the §8.1 operational event types but omits `EventUserErased`, `EventAuditAnchored`, `EventAuditAnchorFailed`, `EventAuditGapDetected`, and `EventRetentionEnforced` (`internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:75-99`, compare the full type set at `pkg/audit/audit.go:31-65`). Because `Enforce` drops an event only when its type has a matching policy (`pkg/audit/retention.go:116`), those omitted types are retained indefinitely rather than at the 1-year default. The omission is conservative for integrity and GDPR-accountability records (anchoring, gap, retention markers, and erasure), so it preserves more than the spec default rather than less, and §8.4 frames the windows as configurable defaults. Suggested direction: if the 1-year default is meant to be exhaustive, document the intentional retain-forever treatment of integrity and erasure event types, or add them to the default policy with a longer explicit window.

## F-8.5 — 8.5 Erasure

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md §8.5 against the implementation._

The §8.5 block defines the `podium admin erase <user_id>` command and four checkable behaviors: it unregisters and purges the user's owned user-defined layers and the artifacts ingested from them, redacts the user identity in audit records by replacing it with `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>`, preserves audit event sequencing for integrity, and logs the erasure as a `user.erased` event. The command and both execution forms exist. The CLI dispatches `erase` to `adminEraseCmd` (`cmd/podium/admin.go:43`), which calls the registry endpoint `POST /v1/admin/erase` (`cmd/podium/admin.go:268`) or, with `--local`/`--audit-path`, the local-log form `audit.EraseUser` (`cmd/podium/admin.go:253`). The registry endpoint is mounted at `/v1/admin/erase` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:965`) and purges every user-defined layer owned by `user_id` plus its ingested artifacts via `DeleteLayerConfig` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:307-326`, `pkg/store/memory.go:363-379`), then redacts the audit stream and appends the `user.erased` event (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:327-340`). The tombstone format `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>` is computed with no delimiter between `user_id` and `salt`, matching the spec literal (`pkg/audit/retention.go:245-248`). Event sequencing is preserved because `EraseUser` reads all events in order, redacts in place, appends `user.erased`, and rewrites the whole hash chain in the original order under the sink mutex (`pkg/audit/retention.go:191-239`, `pkg/audit/retention.go:276-305`). The `user.erased` event type is defined and emitted (`pkg/audit/audit.go:46`, `pkg/audit/retention.go:226-232`).

One High-severity gap surfaced: the redaction pass leaves the user's directly-identifying email and group membership in the persisted audit records, so the user identity is not actually removed. A secondary ambiguity around which identity field `user_id` is matched against is recorded as Info.

### - [x] F-8.5.1 — Erasure leaves caller_email and caller_groups unredacted [High] — CLOSED

Resolution (d98e639): `EraseUser` now redacts the full caller identity for a matched event — the sub-claim, the attached `CallerEmail` (replaced with the same `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>` tombstone), and `CallerGroups` (cleared) — so the persisted record no longer carries the erased user's PII. `CallerNetwork` is left intact as public-mode request metadata. Unit, registry-handler, integration, and CLI e2e tests assert the on-disk email and group membership are gone after erasure.

(gap) §8.5 requires that erasure "Redacts the user identity in audit records (replaces with `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>`)" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:63`), and §8.1 states that read events record the caller's identity "from the OAuth token: typically `caller.identity = \"<sub-claim>\"`, with email and groups attached" (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:30`). The persisted audit record therefore carries the user identity in three fields: `Caller` (the sub-claim), `CallerEmail`, and `CallerGroups` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:83-89`), all serialized to disk as `caller`, `caller_email`, and `caller_groups` (`pkg/audit/file.go:169`, `pkg/audit/file.go:193`). The `EraseUser` redaction loop replaces only `ev.Caller` and `ev.Context[k]` when they equal `userID`; it never touches `ev.CallerEmail` or `ev.CallerGroups` (`pkg/audit/retention.go:197-213`). Both the registry read-event emitter (`internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:49-50`) and the HTTP-boundary write emitter (`pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:180-181`) populate `CallerEmail` from `m.Email` and `CallerGroups` from `m.Groups` for every authenticated, non-public call, so each `domain.loaded`, `artifacts.searched`, `artifact.loaded`, and `layer.user_registered` event the erased user produced retains their email address after erasure. The email is directly identifying PII, so the GDPR right-to-erasure flow that §8.5 advertises does not remove the user identity it claims to redact. No erase test asserts redaction of these fields (`pkg/audit/retention_test.go`, `pkg/registry/server/erase_test.go`). Suggested direction: extend the `EraseUser` loop in `pkg/audit/retention.go` to redact `CallerEmail` and `CallerGroups` for events whose `Caller`, `CallerEmail`, or any context value matches `userID`, replacing the email with the same tombstone and clearing or tombstoning group membership, and add coverage asserting the on-disk `caller_email` no longer contains the original address.

### - [x] F-8.5.2 — user_id matched only against the sub-claim, not the email [Info] — CLOSED

Resolution (d98e639): `EraseUser` runs an alias-discovery pass that collects both identity fields (sub-claim and email) from every event matching the passed `user_id` on either field, then redacts against the full alias set. Passing the email (the value a GDPR request supplies) now also erases the sub-claim recorded elsewhere, including the sub-claim stored in the layer-owner context, and passing the sub-claim erases the email. The spec is left unchanged (Rule A); §8.5's single `<user_id>` argument is honored by accepting either identifier. CLI e2e plus unit coverage exercise email-input and context-only-match cases.

(inconsistency) §8.5 takes a single `<user_id>` argument (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:59`) without defining which identity field it matches, while §8.1 records the read-event identity as the sub-claim with the email attached separately (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:30`). The identity resolver populates `Sub` from the JWT `sub` claim and `Email` from the `email` claim as distinct values (`pkg/identity/runtime.go:200-206`), and the audit `Caller` is set to `id.Sub` via `callerOf`/`callerIdentityString` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1606-1614`, `pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:137-142`). `EraseUser` only matches `ev.Caller == userID` and `ev.Context[k] == userID` (`pkg/audit/retention.go:200-208`). An operator who passes the user's email address (the value a human knows for a GDPR request) will not match the `Caller` sub-claim and the layer-owner context, so nothing is redacted, while passing the sub-claim leaves the email unredacted per F-8.5.1. The combination means there is no single `user_id` value that fully erases the identity today. Suggested direction: define in the spec which identifier `user_id` denotes, and have `EraseUser` match and redact against both the sub-claim and the email so either input erases the full identity.

## F-8.6 — 8.6 Audit Integrity

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md §8.6 against the implementation._

I reviewed §8.6 (`spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:68`), which states three checkable contracts: every audit event carries a hash chain computed as `event_hash = sha256(event_body || prev_event_hash)`, detection of chain gaps is automated and alerted, and periodic anchoring of the chain head to a public transparency log is recommended for high-assurance deployments.

The hash-chain formula is implemented consistently across every sink. `pkg/audit/audit.go:174` computes `sha256(canonicalBody() || lastHash)` in `Memory.Append`, `pkg/audit/file.go:88` does the same in `FileSink.Append`, and `pkg/audit/endpoint.go:62` does the same in `EndpointSink.Append` before forwarding to an external aggregator. The canonical body is a deterministic, sorted serialization of every event field (`pkg/audit/audit.go:112`), so the implementation is a faithful realization of the `sha256(event_body || prev_event_hash)` contract. Every audit event flows through one of these chained sinks: the registry HTTP boundary appends via `pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:183`, registry core events via the `auditEmitterFor` adapter at `internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:53`, ingest events via `internal/serverboot/reingest.go:144`, and the MCP-side local sink via `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:597`, all reaching `audit.FileSink` or `audit.EndpointSink`.

Gap detection is automated and alerted. `VerifyScheduler` (`pkg/audit/scheduler.go:83`) re-verifies the chain on a cadence, records an `audit.gap_detected` event on a break, and invokes `OnGap`. It is wired in production at `internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:84` with an alert log line, enabled by default with a one-hour interval (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1513` and `serverboot.go:1071`). Periodic anchoring is implemented in `pkg/audit/anchor.go:27` and scheduled by `pkg/audit/scheduler.go:33`, which satisfies the recommended (non-mandatory) anchoring clause. All concrete claims in §8.6 hold against the current code.

No findings.

## F-9.1 — 9.1 Pluggable Interfaces

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md §9.1 against the implementation._

The §9.1 table catalogs the registry's Service Provider Interfaces with their defaults and purposes. I extracted every checkable claim: the SPI seams, the default backend per deployment mode, the environment-variable selectors, the built-in backend id strings, and the behavioral rules embedded in the `RegistrySearchProvider`, `EmbeddingProvider`, `LocalSearchProvider`, and `MaterializationHook` rows. Most of the catalog is implemented faithfully. The vector backend ids match (`pgvector`, `sqlite-vec`, `pinecone`, `weaviate-cloud`, `qdrant-cloud`) at `pkg/vector/pgvector.go:86`, `pkg/vector/sqlitevec.go:126`, `pkg/vector/pinecone.go:70`, `pkg/vector/weaviate.go:66`, and `pkg/vector/qdrant.go:66`, and the embedding provider ids match (`openai`, `voyage`, `cohere`, `ollama`) at `pkg/embedding/openai.go:29`, `pkg/embedding/voyage.go:27`, `pkg/embedding/cohere.go:27`, and `pkg/embedding/ollama.go:31`. The per-mode defaults resolve correctly in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1581-1593` (standard → `pgvector` + `openai`, standalone → `sqlite-vec` + `ollama`). The `self_embedding` capability is exposed via `SelfEmbeds()` on Pinecone, Weaviate, and Qdrant at `pkg/vector/pinecone.go:76`, `pkg/vector/weaviate.go:72`, and `pkg/vector/qdrant.go:72`. The audit seam matches the spec: `audit.Sink` at `pkg/audit/audit.go:151`, `audit.FileSink` at `pkg/audit/file.go:21`, wired from `PODIUM_AUDIT_LOG_PATH` in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1507` with the `~/.podium/audit.log` default in `internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:114`. The identity providers `oauth-device-code` and `injected-session-token` are registered at `pkg/identity/registry.go:63-67`, the Git providers GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket at `pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go:46-100`, the `HarnessAdapter` default `none` at `pkg/adapter/none.go:15`, the `LocalOverlayProvider` `.podium/overlay/` default at `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:71`, and the `MaterializationHook` chain runner between adapter and atomic write at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1378-1396`.

Three findings stand against the behavioral rules in the table. The `EmbeddingProvider` row claims the provider is an "optional override when the backend self-embeds", but the boot wiring discards any configured provider when the backend self-embeds, so the override never reaches the registry. The `LocalSearchProvider` row names "a local pgvector instance" and "any managed vector service" as supported local-overlay backends, but the local-overlay backend switch only handles `memory` and `sqlite-vec`. A storage-only backend with a stray cloud inference-model env var skips the embedding-provider key check in the pre-flight validation.

### - [x] F-9.1.1 — EmbeddingProvider override ignored when the backend self-embeds [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit `1899821`): `openVectorAndEmbedder` now builds the embedder and opens the backend at the embedder's dimension when an `EmbeddingProvider` is explicitly configured (`PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` set, or registry.yaml `embedding.type`) even though the backend self-embeds, passing it through `WithVectorSearch` so the core's existing override path (`queryVector`/`upsertVector` prefer a present embedder) embeds locally. Config now tracks `embeddingProviderExplicit` so a defaulted provider, or an explicit `none`/empty, leaves the backend self-embedding. The pre-flight `missingBackendValues` requires the override provider's API key in this case.

(inconsistency) §9.1 states the `EmbeddingProvider` is an "optional override when the backend self-embeds" (`spec/09-extensibility.md:12`), and the cross-referenced contract in `spec/04-artifact-model.md:743` states that "an `EmbeddingProvider` can be **explicitly configured** to override the backend's hosted model." The registry core honors this override: `queryVector` uses the local embedder whenever one is present, gating the self-embedding path on `r.embedder == nil && vector.SelfEmbeds(r.vector)` at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:231`. The boot wiring defeats it. `openVectorAndEmbedder` short-circuits when `c.vectorSelfEmbeds()` is true and returns a `nil` embedder without ever calling `openEmbedder` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1846-1851`), and `Run` then calls `registry.WithVectorSearch(v, nil)` at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:737`. An operator who configures both a self-embedding backend and `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` gets the backend's hosted model with the configured provider silently dropped, so the documented override to pin an existing corpus's model or use a model the backend does not host is unreachable. Suggested direction: construct the embedder when `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` is explicitly set even though the backend self-embeds, and pass it through `WithVectorSearch` so the core's existing override path activates, opening the backend with the embedder's dimension rather than 0.

### - [x] F-9.1.2 — LocalSearchProvider cannot use a local pgvector or managed backend [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (already resolved by commit `730fa0a`, batch fix-6.4-overlay / F-6.4.1): `mcpOverlayVectorBackend` no longer falls through to a `memory`/`sqlite-vec`-only switch. It now delegates to the shared `vector.OpenBuiltin` factory (`cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go:262`), so the workspace overlay reaches `pgvector`, `pinecone`, `weaviate-cloud`, and `qdrant-cloud` via the same env vars the registry uses. Verified by `TestMCPOverlayVectorBackend_ReachesAllDocumentedBackends` (`cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic_test.go:129`). No further change needed this batch.

(gap) §9.1 states that `LocalSearchProvider` "backends include `sqlite-vec`, a local pgvector instance, or any managed vector service" (`spec/09-extensibility.md:13`). The local-overlay backend selector `mcpOverlayVectorBackend` consults the custom-plugin registry first, then falls through to a built-in switch that handles only `memory` and `sqlite-vec`; any other id, including `pgvector`, `pinecone`, `weaviate-cloud`, and `qdrant-cloud`, returns `fmt.Errorf("unsupported overlay vector backend: %s", id)` at `cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go:228-238`. The custom registry seam at `cmd/podium-mcp/local_semantic.go:223` does not cover this because `pgvector` and the managed services are built-ins that are never registered into `vector.Default` (the registry is empty unless a source build imports a plugin, per `pkg/vector/registry.go:45`). An operator who sets `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND=pgvector` for the workspace overlay fails to build the semantic index even though the spec names a local pgvector instance as a supported backend. Suggested direction: extend the local-overlay switch to construct the built-in `pgvector` and managed backends the same way `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1939-1984` does for the registry side, or narrow the spec row to the backends the overlay actually supports.

### - [x] F-9.1.3 — Storage-only backend with a stray inference-model env var skips the embedding-key pre-flight [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit `1899821`): the pre-flight embedding-key gate in `missingBackendValues` now keys on `!c.vectorSelfEmbeds() || c.embeddingProviderExplicit` rather than `c.vectorInferenceModel == ""`. A storage-only backend (`pgvector`, `sqlite-vec`) cannot self-embed even with a stray `*_INFERENCE_MODEL` set, so its embedding-provider key stays required and the startup error names the missing key. The override term keeps the F-9.1.1 explicit-override key required on a self-embedding backend.

(inconsistency) §9.1 states that "storage-only backends (`pgvector`, `sqlite-vec`, plain `qdrant`, plain `weaviate`) require" an `EmbeddingProvider` (`spec/09-extensibility.md:11`). The pre-flight `missingBackendValues` gates the embedding-provider API-key requirement on `c.vectorInferenceModel == ""` without checking whether the selected backend can actually self-embed (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1719-1728`). The companion `vectorSelfEmbeds` correctly returns false for `pgvector` and `sqlite-vec` regardless of the inference model (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1794-1803`), so the two predicates disagree. When an operator selects `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND=pgvector` while a leftover `PODIUM_PINECONE_INFERENCE_MODEL` is set, `vectorInferenceModel` is non-empty and the pre-flight skips the `OPENAI_API_KEY` requirement, so the startup error does not name the missing key even though the spec says §13.12's "refuses to start ... naming the missing keys" applies. Runtime correctness is preserved because `openEmbedder` still errors with `OPENAI_API_KEY required for openai embedder` at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1886-1888`, so the only effect is a less precise pre-flight message. Suggested direction: gate the line-1719 skip on `c.vectorSelfEmbeds()` rather than on `c.vectorInferenceModel == ""` so the embedding-key requirement is dropped only for backends that genuinely self-embed.

## F-9.2 — 9.2 Plugin Distribution

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md §9.2 against the implementation._

Section 9.2 (`spec/09-extensibility.md:28-32`) makes a small number of checkable claims. Plugins ship as Go modules importable into a registry build, a deployment that needs a custom `IdentityProvider` or `GitProvider` builds a registry binary from source with the plugin imported, and a community plugin registry is hosted at the project's public URL. The community-registry sentence is a documentation statement with no code contract, mirrored in `docs/deployment/extending.md:51`, so it produces no implementation finding.

Both SPIs named by example in §9.2 expose a process-global, compile-time registration seam that an imported package can populate from `init()`, and the server consults that seam at startup. `IdentityProvider` registers through `identity.Default.Register` in `pkg/identity/registry.go:74-88`, with the registry declared as a package-level `var Default = newDefault()` at `pkg/identity/registry.go:59` and seeded with the built-in `oauth-device-code` and `injected-session-token` providers at `pkg/identity/registry.go:63-68`. The server selects the provider by its `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` id at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:901-905`, reading the id from the environment at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1451` and resolving it against `identity.Default` in `internal/serverboot/identity_verify.go:103-110`. `GitProvider` registers through `webhook.Default.Register` in `pkg/layer/webhook/registry.go:47-62`, with `var Default = newDefault()` at `pkg/layer/webhook/registry.go:35` seeded with the built-in `github`, `gitlab`, and `bitbucket` providers at `pkg/layer/webhook/registry.go:39-41`, and the inbound webhook path selects the provider by id and verifies the signature at `pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:62-72`. Both seams are the build-path consumers that make "import a custom provider into a source build change behavior," which is the only concrete mechanism §9.2 mandates.

I also confirmed the more general "plugins ship as Go modules" claim against the other SPIs that §9.1 says register as Go-module plugins: `RegistrySearchProvider` and `EmbeddingProvider` carry the same `Default` registration seams at `pkg/vector/registry.go:45-49` and `pkg/embedding/registry.go:42-46`. The §9.2 claims are satisfied by the implementation.

No findings.

## F-9.3 — 9.3 Forward Compatibility for Out-of-Process Plugins

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md §9.3 against the implementation._

Section 9.3 is a forward-compatibility commitment for a potential out-of-process plugin protocol. The spec explicitly states it does not commit Podium to ship such a protocol or transport (`spec/09-extensibility.md:50`). Most of the section is conceptual. The concrete, present-day-checkable claims are the per-SPI constraints in `spec/09-extensibility.md:40-46` (cancellable context-first methods, no func or channel types, no shared in-process state, structured errors with codes namespaced per §6.10, restartable long-lived operations, idempotent retries, bounded payloads) and the assertion that the built-in `RegistryStore`, `HarnessAdapter`, and `LayerSourceProvider` implementations conform today (`spec/09-extensibility.md:48`).

The context-first ("Cancellable") constraint holds for the named built-ins and for the broader §9.1 SPI surface. `store.Store` takes `context.Context` first on every working method (`pkg/store/store.go:314-376`), `adapter.HarnessAdapter.Adapt` is context-first (`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:100`), and `source.Provider.Snapshot` is context-first with zero-parameter accessors `ID()` and `Trigger()` exempt (`pkg/layer/source/source.go:45-53`). The same holds for `sign.Provider` (`pkg/sign/sign.go:58-70`), `audit.Sink` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:151-154`), `notification.Provider` (`pkg/notification/notification.go:52-55`), `identity.Provider` (`pkg/identity/identity.go:43-49`), `embedding.Provider` (`pkg/embedding/embedding.go:35-48`), `vector.Provider` (`pkg/vector/vector.go:54-76`), `hook.Hook` (`pkg/hook/hook.go:40-46`), `lint.Rule` (`pkg/lint/lint.go:81-86`), and `typeprovider.Provider` (`pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:39-43`). A static guard verifies the no-func and no-channel parameter rules plus context-first for a subset of these packages and passes (`test/conformance/spi_signatures_test.go:32-92`). The §6.10 code-namespacing tie-in holds: built-in SPI sentinel errors carry namespaced mappings (`pkg/store/store.go:42`, `pkg/hook/hook.go:20-21`, `pkg/layer/source/source.go:86-88`, `pkg/sign/sign.go:18-19`). The "Bounded payloads" constraint is honored on the inbound webhook path with a 1 MiB cap (`pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:12-15`).

The findings below are low-impact. One concerns the "Structured errors" constraint, where the built-in SPIs return plain Go error chains rather than the `{code, message, retryable, details}` envelope the constraint describes; the envelope is constructed only at the §6.10 HTTP boundary. The other concerns the static signature guard's package list, which omits the two SPI packages §9.3 names as canonical conforming built-ins.

### - [x] F-9.3.1 — Built-in SPIs return Go error chains, not the structured envelope §9.3 claims they conform to [Info] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 8463e10): introduced `pkg/spi.Error` carrying `{code, message, retryable, details}` and converted the built-in SPI sentinels (`store.ErrNotFound`/`ErrImmutableViolation`/`ErrTenantNotFound`, `source.ErrSourceUnreachable`/`ErrInvalidConfig`, `sign.ErrSignatureInvalid`/`ErrSignatureMissing`/`ErrSigstoreUnavailable`/`ErrRegistryManagedUnavailable`, `hook.ErrSandboxViolation`) plus the adapter's `Registry.Get` and `TranslationError` to return it, each stamped with its §6.10 code. `.Error()` text and `errors.Is` pointer identity are preserved, so the §6.10 wire boundary and all consumers are unchanged. Guarded by the new `TestSPIStructuredErrors` conformance test plus `pkg/spi`, adapter, and integration coverage.

(inconsistency) The "Structured errors" constraint states that failures "use a structured envelope (`{code, message, retryable, details}`) rather than opaque Go error chains" and that the default `RegistryStore`, `HarnessAdapter`, and `LayerSourceProvider` implementations "conform to these constraints today" (`spec/09-extensibility.md:43`, `spec/09-extensibility.md:48`). The built-in SPIs return plain Go `error` values: `store.Store` returns sentinels such as `ErrImmutableViolation` and `fmt.Errorf` chains (`pkg/store/store.go:37-47`, `pkg/store/store.go:320`), `source.Provider` returns `ErrSourceUnreachable` and `ErrInvalidConfig` (`pkg/layer/source/source.go:84-92`), `adapter.HarnessAdapter.Adapt` returns a bare `error` (`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:100`), and `sign.Provider`, `hook.Hook`, and the others do likewise. The `{code, message, retryable, details}` envelope is materialized only at the §6.10 HTTP edge by `ErrorResponse` and `enrichEnvelope` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:519-523`, `pkg/registry/server/error_envelope.go:53-72`); no SPI package defines or returns a structured error type with `code`, `message`, `retryable`, and `details`. The constraint's namespaced-code intent is preserved through sentinel-to-code mapping comments, but the in-process return type is an opaque Go error chain, which is what the constraint says built-ins do not do. This is rated Info because §9.3 frames the whole section as forward-looking and states the option is not committed (`spec/09-extensibility.md:50`); an out-of-process transport would map Go errors to the envelope at the boundary, which the registry already does at §6.10. Suggested direction: either soften the §9.3 wording so the present-day claim describes the boundary envelope plus namespaced sentinels rather than asserting the SPI return type is already the envelope, or introduce a shared structured error type that the built-in SPIs return so the conformance claim is literally true.

### - [x] F-9.3.2 — SPI signature guard omits the `store` and `layer/source` packages §9.3 names as conforming built-ins [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 8463e10): added `pkg/store` (RegistryStore) and `pkg/layer/source` (LayerSourceProvider) to the `spiPkgs` list in `test/conformance/spi_signatures_test.go`, so both §9.3-named built-ins are now walked by the wire-compatibility guard. Their interfaces already conform (context-first, no func/channel params). Refactored `checkMethod` into the testable `methodViolations` and added `TestMethodViolations`, which proves the guard flags a missing-context, func-param, or channel-param method; a temporary violating interface in `pkg/layer/source` was confirmed to fail the guard before removal.

(gap) Section 9.3 names `RegistryStore`, `HarnessAdapter`, and `LayerSourceProvider` as the built-in implementations that "conform to these constraints today" (`spec/09-extensibility.md:48`), where the constraints include the cancellable context-first rule and the no-func and no-channel parameter rules (`spec/09-extensibility.md:40-41`). The static guard that enforces these rules checks only `pkg/adapter`, `pkg/sign`, `pkg/hook`, `pkg/lint`, and `pkg/typeprovider` (`test/conformance/spi_signatures_test.go:34-40`). It omits `pkg/store` (the `RegistryStore` SPI) and `pkg/layer/source` (the `LayerSourceProvider` SPI), so two of the three SPIs §9.3 highlights have no regression guard for their wire-compatibility constraints. The implementations conform today (`pkg/store/store.go:314-376`, `pkg/layer/source/source.go:45-53`), so this is a coverage gap rather than a live violation, and the guard's contract is rooted in §11 verification rather than §9.3 itself. Suggested direction: add `pkg/store` and `pkg/layer/source` to the `spiPkgs` list in `test/conformance/spi_signatures_test.go` so the two §9.3-named built-ins are guarded against future context-first or func-parameter regressions.

## F-9.4 — 9.4 Building on Podium from outside the registry

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md §9.4 against the implementation._

Section 9.4 describes composition patterns for building team-specific tooling on top of the registry HTTP API, the SDKs, the CLI, and the outbound webhook stream. The prose is mostly conceptual, but it names several concrete contracts: the SDK and read-CLI discovery operations, a worked `podium sync --include` example, and the CLI commands `podium lint` and `podium layer reingest <id>`. Every checkable claim resolves to working code.

The discovery operations the section names (`load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, `load_artifact`, and `dependents_of()`) are present in the Python SDK (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:507`, `:515`, `:534`, `:633`, `:722`) and the TypeScript SDK (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:497`, `:503`, `:517`, `:586`, `:676`). The worked example calls `Client.from_env()`, `search_artifacts(query, type=, top_k=)`, reads `r.id` and `r.score` from each result, and passes the chosen ids to `podium sync` with repeated `--include` flags. `Client.from_env()` exists at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:384`; `search_artifacts` accepts `type` and `top_k` and returns `ArtifactDescriptor` records carrying `id` and `score` (`client.py:534`, `:71`). The same four read operations are exposed through the read CLI per §7.6.1 at `cmd/podium/main.go:810`, `:889`, `:926`, and `:987`.

The `podium sync` flags in the example all exist: `--harness`, `--target`, and the repeatable `--include` glob over canonical IDs are registered at `cmd/podium/main.go:193`, `:197`, and `:208`, and an exact id is a valid glob that matches itself. `podium lint` is dispatched at `cmd/podium/main.go:49` and implemented at `:720`. `podium layer reingest <id>` is dispatched at `cmd/podium/layer.go:55` and implemented at `:353`, POSTing to `/v1/layers/reingest`. The outbound-webhook event names the section cites illustratively (`artifact.deprecated`, `artifact.published`, `layer.history_rewritten`) are defined as constants at `pkg/audit/audit.go:35`, `:36`, and `:40` and are delivered through the webhook path (`pkg/webhook/webhook.go`). No defects found.

No findings.

## F-10.0 — 10 MVP Build Sequence

_Reviewed spec/10-mvp-build-sequence.md §10.0 against the implementation._

Section 10 is a build-sequence roadmap. It names the deliverables of each phase: CLI commands and flags, deployment modes, file and directory paths, HTTP API endpoints, harness adapters, artifact types, and supporting components such as lint, signing, the SDK, and the MCP bridge. Each phase entry states a checkable contract about what the codebase must contain. I extracted those concrete artifacts and traced every one of them to real code.

The named CLI surface resolves to actual dispatch cases in `cmd/podium/main.go:39-81` (`serve`, `config`, `cache`, `import`, `sync`, `lint`, `search`, `domain`, `artifact`, `init`, `profile`, `layer`, `impact`, `admin`, `login`, `sign`, `verify`, `quota`). The Phase 3 sync flags all exist on the flag set in `cmd/podium/main.go:198-209` (`--dry-run`, `--watch`, `--profile`, `--type`, `--include`, `--exclude`), the per-target lock file path matches `.podium/sync.lock` at `pkg/sync/lockfile.go:66`, and `podium init` carries the workspace, `--global`, and `--local` modes at `cmd/podium/main.go:996` and below. The Phase 2 HTTP endpoints `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` are registered at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:327-330`. The Phase 0/3 core adapters return the expected IDs (`pkg/adapter/none.go:15`, `pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:26`, `pkg/adapter/codex.go:15`), and the Phase 13 remaining built-ins (`claude-desktop`, `claude-cowork`, `cursor`, `gemini`, `opencode`, `pi`, `hermes`) all exist in `pkg/adapter/builtins.go:24-211`. The multi-type catalog types (`skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`, `mcp-server`) are defined at `pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25`, agentskills.io lint compliance is implemented in `pkg/lint/skill_rules.go`, signing lives in `pkg/sign/`, the Python SDK at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py`, and the MCP bridge under `cmd/podium-mcp/`. The standalone deployment defaults to embedded SQLite plus sqlite-vec with no auth, confirmed at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:10` and `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1585`, and ingests the filesystem registry at boot via `bootstrapLayerPath` at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:333`.

Every concrete deliverable named across §10's phase tables traces to present, working code. The section states no wire format, status code, error envelope, or default value that the implementation contradicts. I found no defects in scope.

No findings.

## F-11.0 — 11 Verification

_Reviewed spec/11-verification.md §11.0 against the implementation._

Section 11 is a verification catalog: each bullet names a test and, in passing, asserts concrete contracts (error codes, environment variables, CLI commands and flags, lock-file structure, file names, and dispatch rules). I traced the checkable contracts embedded in those bullets to the implementation rather than auditing for the presence of test files. The error codes referenced across the section are present and wired: `auth.untrusted_runtime` (`pkg/identity/identity.go:17`, `pkg/registry/server/error_envelope.go:48`), `registry.invalid_argument` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:37`), `materialize.signature_invalid`, `ingest.immutable_violation` (`pkg/store` via `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:701`), `layer.history_rewritten` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:40`, `pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:123`), and `config.layer_path_ambiguous` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:29`).

The `top_k > 50` rejection is enforced server-side at the registry (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1010`, `pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go:66`) and client-side in both SDKs (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:35`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:322`), and `total_matched` is captured before truncation (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1052`). The `--layer-path` dispatch (single-layer vs multi-layer, `layer_order:` then alphabetical, and the top-level-manifest refusal) is implemented in `pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:112-273` and surfaced at startup through `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:337`. The sync lock-file structure (`.podium/sync.lock` with `profile`, `scope`, `artifacts`, and `toggles`) matches §7.5.3 in `pkg/sync/lockfile.go`, manual sync clears toggles by leaving `PreserveToggles` false (`pkg/sync/sync.go:210`), `override --reset` clears toggles (`pkg/sync/override.go:85`), and `profile edit` preserves untouched formatting via a `yaml.Node` tree (`pkg/sync/profile_edit.go:16-83`). Break-glass dual-signoff requires two distinct approvers (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:92`), and the rule-mode and hook-event capability lint enforces ✓/⚠/✗ against `target_harnesses` (`pkg/lint/harness_capability.go:33-54`, `pkg/adapter/capability.go:105-114`).

One inconsistency surfaced: `podium sync save-as` does not make the saved profile the active one, contradicting the §11 "Save-as test" bullet.

### - [x] F-11.0.1 — save-as does not activate the new profile [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 3bbc66e): `SaveAs` now sets `lock.Profile = opts.Profile` before writing the lock, so the saved profile becomes the target's active profile (the lock's `profile:` field), matching the §11 "Save-as test" and §7.5.3 contract. `--dry-run` writes nothing and does not activate. Covered by `TestSaveAs_ActivatesProfile`, `TestSaveAs_DryRunDoesNotActivate`, and the `TestSyncSaveAs_FreshFileDefaultsAndActivation` e2e.

(inconsistency) The §11 "Save-as test" bullet at `spec/11-verification.md:39` states that after `podium sync save-as --profile <name>`, "the lock file's `toggles:` is cleared and the new profile becomes the active one." The active profile for a target is the lock file's `profile:` field, per `spec/07-external-integration.md:320` ("The `profile:` field is the **active profile** for that target. `override`, `save-as`, and `profile edit` use it as the default when no `--profile` flag is given."). In `pkg/sync/override.go:200-248`, `SaveAs` reads the lock (`lock, err := ReadLock(opts.Target)`), writes the new profile into `cfg.Profiles[opts.Profile]` (line 237), clears `lock.Toggles` (line 242), and writes the lock back (line 243), but it never sets `lock.Profile = opts.Profile`. The CLI wrapper `syncSaveAsCmd` at `cmd/podium/main.go:599-601` adds nothing further. Consequently the saved profile is created but not activated: the lock file's `profile:` field retains its prior value, and a subsequent plain `podium sync` resolves scope from the unchanged active profile (or `defaults.profile`) rather than the newly saved profile (`pkg/sync/resolve.go:208-219`). Suggested direction: set `lock.Profile = opts.Profile` before the `WriteLock` call in `SaveAs` so the saved profile becomes the target's active profile, matching the §11 and §7 contract.

## F-12.0 — 12 Operational Risks and Mitigations

_Reviewed spec/12-operational-risks-and-mitigations.md §12.0 against the implementation._

Section 12 is a risk and mitigation table where each mitigation summarizes a behavior specified in detail elsewhere. I extracted every concrete, checkable mitigation claim and traced it to code. Most mitigations are implemented. The discovery-bounding knobs (`max_depth`, `fold_below_artifacts`, `target_response_tokens`, `featured`, `deprioritize`) exist on both the manifest and the registry resolver (`pkg/manifest/types.go:239-245`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:104-431`), and `podium domain analyze` reports sparsity, pass-through chains, and split/fold candidates (`pkg/registry/core/analyze.go:13-77`, `cmd/podium/main.go:836-865`). The offline meta-tool status that hosts surface during a transient outage is implemented for `load_domain`, `search_domains`, and `search_artifacts` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1066-1076`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:2164-2215`, `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:108-139`). Webhook HMAC verification rejects a bad signature with `ingest.webhook_invalid` before any ingest (`pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:72-83`, `pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go:50-112`), per-layer secret rotation runs through `podium layer update --rotate-webhook-secret` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:82-108`, `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:423-474`), and the audit log is hash-chained with transparency anchoring (`pkg/audit/audit.go:103-190`, `pkg/audit/anchor.go:27-30`). The ingest-time description-quality advisories (thin descriptions and colliding summaries), the stale-import and broad-glob domain lints, the server-side glob-expansion cache keyed on the visible artifact-ID snapshot, the registry rejection of untrusted runtimes, and the identity-provider startup validation are all present (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:490`, `pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:22-136`, `pkg/registry/core/import_cache.go:44-114`, `pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:84-92`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:342-349`).

Three mitigation claims do not hold against the current code: the ingest lint that the table says flags newly-set `unlisted: true` is absent, the per-file and per-package size soft caps the table says are configurable are hardcoded constants, and the profile-level adapter minimum-version pin the table names does not exist in the profile schema. All three are recorded below.

### - [x] F-12.0.1 — Ingest lint does not flag newly-set `unlisted: true` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (12f682e): the ingest pipeline's DOMAIN.md loop now emits a `lint.domain_newly_unlisted` warning advisory (`newlyUnlistedAdvisory` in `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go`) when a DOMAIN.md sets `unlisted: true` and the value is newly set, comparing against the prior stored DOMAIN.md (`prevDomains`) so a steady-state re-ingest of an already-unlisted domain stays quiet. The advisory is non-blocking and surfaces via the §7.3.1 reingest result. Covered by 4 ingest unit tests and 1 HTTP-reingest integration test.

(gap) The `unlisted: true accidentally hides artifacts` row claims `ingest-time lint flags newly-set unlisted: true for review` (`spec/12-operational-risks-and-mitigations.md:18`). No lint rule for this exists. The author-facing rule set in `pkg/lint/lint.go:100-122` (`AllRulesWithClient`) contains no unlisted-detection rule, and the ingest pipeline adds only `DescriptionAdvisoryRules` (thin and colliding descriptions) on top of the configured linter (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:480-490`). A repository-wide search for any unlisted-related lint, warn, or review path in non-test Go code returns nothing; the only `unlisted` consumers are the discovery-time visibility filters in `pkg/registry/core/domain_load.go:166-168` and `pkg/registry/core/core.go:492-604`. The `unlisted` field is read for enumeration, but no diagnostic is emitted when it is set, so the review safety net the spec promises is missing. Suggested direction: add an ingest-time advisory rule (warning severity) that emits a diagnostic when a record carries `unlisted: true`, ideally comparing against the prior ingested version so only newly-set values are flagged, and register it alongside `DescriptionAdvisoryRules` in the ingest pipeline.

### - [x] F-12.0.2 — Bundled-resource size soft caps are hardcoded, not configurable [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (12f682e): `Linter` now carries `PerFileSoftCapBytes` / `PerPackageSoftCapBytes` overrides threaded into `ruleBundledResourceSize` (zero falls back to the §4.1 default constants), and `NewIngestLinter` reads them from `PODIUM_LINT_PER_FILE_SOFT_CAP_BYTES` / `PODIUM_LINT_PER_PACKAGE_SOFT_CAP_BYTES` so an operator can tune the caps per deployment (the same wiring serverboot, the server, and the CLI already use). Covered by 4 unit tests (field override, env read, invalid-env fallback), 1 ingest-orchestrator integration test, and 1 standalone-server e2e test.

(inconsistency) The `Bundled resource bloat` row claims `Per-package and per-file size lints at ingest time; soft cap is configurable` (`spec/12-operational-risks-and-mitigations.md:15`). The lints exist, but the caps are compile-time constants with no configuration surface: `PerFileSoftCapBytes = 1 * 1024 * 1024` and `PerPackageSoftCapBytes = 10 * 1024 * 1024` in `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:16-19`, applied directly by `ruleBundledResourceSize.Check` at `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:74-93`. A repository-wide search finds no environment variable, tenant config key, or linter field that overrides these thresholds. The lints run, but an operator cannot tune the cap as the spec states. Suggested direction: thread the per-file and per-package soft caps through the linter configuration (a field on `Linter` or a tenant-level config key resolved at ingest), defaulting to the current constants, so the `soft cap is configurable` claim holds.

### - [x] F-12.0.3 — Profiles cannot pin a minimum adapter version [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (resolved by commit 9cf07f3, F-6.7.3): §6.7 establishes that adapter behavior versions alongside the MCP server binary, so the adapter-drift pin is the `min_server_version` field. That field exists on both `Profile` and `Defaults` (`pkg/sync/config.go`) and is enforced at sync (`cmd/podium/main.go`) and MCP boot (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`): a profile pinning a version above the running binary refuses the sync with `config.server_version_too_old`. Verified by `version_pin_test.go` (unit) and a new profile-level integration test `TestPodiumSync_ProfilePinRefusesOlderAdapter` (commit 3bbc66e).

(gap) The `Harness adapter drift` row claims `Adapters are versioned with the MCP server binary; profiles can pin a minimum version` (`spec/12-operational-risks-and-mitigations.md:19`). The sync `Profile` struct exposes `Include`, `Exclude`, `Type`, `Target`, and `Harness` and no version-pin field (`pkg/sync/config.go:45-51`), and the `TargetEntry` struct (`pkg/sync/config.go:54-62`) is likewise without one. A repository-wide search for an adapter minimum-version or harness-version pin in non-test Go code returns no match, and the adapter interface in `pkg/adapter/adapter.go` carries no `Version()` accessor a pin could compare against. A profile that requires a newer adapter than the running binary cannot express that requirement, so a stale binary materializes silently rather than refusing. Suggested direction: add an optional minimum-adapter-version field to `Profile` (and `TargetEntry`), expose an adapter version through the adapter registry, and refuse a sync whose resolved adapter is older than the profile's pin.

## F-13.1 — 13.1 Reference Topology (13.1.1 Evaluation Deployment / Docker Compose)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.1 against the implementation._

This audit covered the reference topology bullets in §13.1 and the Docker Compose evaluation deployment in §13.1.1. The topology claims about the default backends and the Helm chart hold against the code. The default vector backend is `pgvector` and the built-in backend IDs `pinecone`, `weaviate-cloud`, and `qdrant-cloud` exist and are selectable via `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND` (`pkg/vector/pinecone.go:70`, `pkg/vector/weaviate.go:66`, `pkg/vector/qdrant.go:66`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1697-1712`). The default embedding provider is `openai` with built-ins `voyage`, `cohere`, and `ollama` selectable via `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` (`pkg/embedding/openai.go:29`, `pkg/embedding/voyage.go:27`, `pkg/embedding/cohere.go:27`, `pkg/embedding/ollama.go:31`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1885-1911`). The Helm chart ships at `deploy/helm/podium/Chart.yaml` and defaults to `replicaCount: 3` to satisfy the "3+ replicas" front-end claim (`deploy/helm/podium/values.yaml:9`).

The §13.1.1 evaluation deployment claims also hold. The repo ships `docker-compose.yml` with the named services `registry`, `postgres` (`pgvector/pgvector:pg16`), `minio` (using `MINIO_ROOT_USER` / `MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD`), `dex`, and `bootstrap` (`docker-compose.yml:28-142`). The documented commands `podium init --global --registry http://localhost:8080` and `podium login` work against real CLI flags (`cmd/podium/main.go:999-1002`) and the device-code login flow (`cmd/podium/login.go:186-195`). The Dex config registers the registry as an OIDC client and seeds an example user (`deploy/compose/dex/config.yaml:29-44`), and `PODIUM_BOOTSTRAP_ADMINS` seeds the admin grant at registry boot (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:649`). One inconsistency surfaced: the spec attributes three setup actions to the `bootstrap` container, but the implementation distributes two of them elsewhere in the stack.

### - [ ] F-13.1.1 — Bootstrap container responsibilities diverge from spec description [Low] — DEFERRED

Deferred (only clean fix is a read-only spec edit): this is a prose-location inconsistency, not a behavioral or wire-contract gap. The functional outcome §13.1.1 describes is already achieved across the eval stack, and the structural conformance test `TestDeployCompose_BootstrapService` (`test/e2e/deployment_compose_test.go`) passes against the current split. Making the implementation literally match the spec text is blocked on two genuine constraints. First, the tenant-and-admin seeding cannot be relocated into the bootstrap container: §13.10 standalone is a single binary with no bootstrap container, so the registry must self-seed the default tenant and `PODIUM_BOOTSTRAP_ADMINS` grants at boot (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:645`-`657`), and the same binary serves the eval stack; §13.1.1's attribution of this work to the bootstrap container therefore conflicts with §13.10, and the implementation reconciles both by self-seeding. Second, the OIDC-client clause cannot move without replacing Dex's idiomatic static-client registration (`deploy/compose/dex/config.yaml:29`-`34`) with dynamic gRPC registration from the bootstrap container, which adds plaintext gRPC, a heavy `dexidp/dex/api` dependency, and reordered `depends_on` to an evaluation-only stack, and is not e2e-testable in the sandbox (no Docker or Dex). The only clean reconciliation is editing the §13.1.1 prose to describe the actual split, which Ground Rule A forbids. No code defect remains; nothing unblocks this finding.

(inconsistency) The spec describes the `bootstrap` service as a "one-shot container that creates the MinIO bucket, registers the registry as an OIDC client with Dex, creates the first tenant and admin user (configurable via env vars), then exits" (`spec/13-deployment.md:30`). The actual `bootstrap` container only runs `mc mb --ignore-existing local/podium` to create the MinIO bucket and exits (`docker-compose.yml:89-102`). The OIDC client registration is handled declaratively in the Dex config (`deploy/compose/dex/config.yaml:29-34`), and the first tenant plus admin user are seeded by the registry at boot rather than by the bootstrap container (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:632-652`). The functional outcome the spec describes is achieved across the stack, and the compose comments document the split (`docker-compose.yml:82-88`), but the spec text states the bootstrap container itself performs all three actions, which does not match the implementation. Suggested direction: update §13.1.1 to describe the bootstrap container as creating the MinIO bucket only and note that the OIDC client registration is declared in the Dex config while the tenant and admin grant are seeded by the registry at boot, or alternatively move those responsibilities into the bootstrap container if the spec wording is intended to be authoritative.

## F-13.2 — 13.2 Runbook (13.2.1 Read-Only Mode, 13.2.2 Public Mode)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.2 against the implementation._

This audit traced the checkable claims in §13.2.1 (read-only mode) and §13.2.2 (public mode) to the Go registry, the serverboot wiring, the MCP bridge, and the two SDKs. Most of the contract holds. The read-only probe pings the metadata store on a tick and flips the shared `ModeTracker` after the configured failure count, recovering after consecutive successes (`pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go:43`), and the defaults match the spec's "probe every 5 s, flip after three consecutive failures" with `PODIUM_READONLY_PROBE_INTERVAL` and `PODIUM_READONLY_PROBE_FAILURES` overrides resolved to `5` and `3` when unset (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1559`). Read responses in read-only mode carry `X-Podium-Read-Only: true` and `X-Podium-Read-Only-Lag-Seconds: <n>` uniformly via middleware (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:366`), with the lag value sourced from a Postgres replica reporter (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:820`). Transition audit events `registry.read_only_entered` / `registry.read_only_exited` are appended to the hash-chained `FileSink` (`internal/serverboot/readonly_audit.go:17`). The MCP `health` tool reports `mode: read_only` from `/healthz` (`cmd/podium-mcp/health.go:76`). Public mode reports `mode: public` on `/healthz` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:539`), records `caller` as `system:public` (`pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:137`), rejects ingest of `medium` and `high` sensitivity through a floor of `SensitivityMedium` on both the bootstrap and the webhook reingest paths (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:273`, `internal/serverboot/reingest.go:60`), continues serving pre-existing artifacts because public-mode callers set `IsPublic` and bypass layer filtering (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:1090`), emits the startup warning banner (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1160`), and surfaces the mode through `podium status` (`cmd/podium/status.go:50`).

One inconsistency affects correctness of the documented client contract: the registry rejects writes in read-only mode with the error code `config.read_only`, while §13.2.1 and both SDKs require `registry.read_only`. The remaining observation is a cosmetic field-name divergence that belongs to §8.1.

### - [x] F-13.2.1 — Read-only write rejection uses config.read_only instead of registry.read_only [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit a9eaded): every write-path handler now rejects through a single `rejectIfReadOnly` helper that emits `registry.read_only` (HTTP 503), the code §13.2.1 mandates; the undefined `config.read_only` / `ErrReadOnlyConfig` / `CheckConfig` split is removed, so the SDKs' `RegistryReadOnly` mapping fires on attempted writes. `registry.read_only` is registered as retryable in the §6.10 envelope since read-only mode self-clears on primary recovery. Covered by a server helper unit test, the existing read-only-writes handler tests (retargeted to `registry.read_only`), and the HTTP-API e2e.

(inconsistency) Spec §13.2.1 states that write endpoints (`ingest webhooks`, `layer admin operations`, `freeze toggles`, `admin grants`, `podium login`-driven token issuance) "are rejected with the structured error `registry.read_only`" (`spec/13-deployment.md:40`), and §13.2.1 further states "SDKs raise `RegistryReadOnly` on attempted writes" (`spec/13-deployment.md:51`). The string `config.read_only` does not appear anywhere in the spec. In the implementation, every write-path handler calls `ModeTracker.CheckConfig()` and emits `config.read_only` with HTTP 503: the ingest webhook (`pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:37`), admin grants (`pkg/registry/server/admin.go:33`), layer register and the other layer-config and freeze handlers (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:283`, `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:483`), the runtime-key endpoint (`pkg/registry/server/runtime_endpoint.go:76`), and the webhook config handlers (`pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go:40`). The `registry.read_only` code (`ErrReadOnly`) and its `CheckWrite()` method are defined but never invoked by any handler (`pkg/registry/server/readonly.go:13`, `pkg/registry/server/readonly.go:62`). Both SDKs map only `registry.read_only` to `RegistryReadOnly` and route every other code to the base error class: `_registry_error_from_envelope` checks `code == "registry.read_only"` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:66`) and `registryErrorFromEnvelope` checks `code === "registry.read_only"` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:310`). Because the registry returns `config.read_only`, a write rejected in read-only mode reaches an SDK caller as a generic `RegistryError`, so the documented `RegistryReadOnly` is never raised on attempted writes and the spec's enumerated write endpoints carry a code the spec does not define. Suggested direction: return `registry.read_only` (via the existing `ErrReadOnly` / `CheckWrite` path) from the write-path handlers so the wire code matches §13.2.1 and the SDK mapping, or reconcile the spec and SDKs to a documented `config.read_only` code if the split between write and config rejection is intended.

### - [x] F-13.2.2 — Public-mode audit flag serialized as caller_public_mode, not caller.public_mode [Info] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 9b83b84): the public-mode flag now serializes under the nested key `caller.public_mode` (and the identity under `caller.identity`), matching the §13.2.2 detection prose verbatim, as part of the §8.1 caller-object change (F-8.1.2). Covered by the `pkg/audit` typed-decode unit and the `TestHTTPAPI_PublicModeAudit` e2e asserting `"caller":{"identity":"system:public",...,"public_mode":true}`.

(inconsistency) Spec §13.2.2 states that audit events for read calls show "the flag `caller.public_mode: true`" (`spec/13-deployment.md:57`). The persisted audit event serializes this flag under the JSON key `caller_public_mode` (`pkg/audit/file.go:172`) rather than a nested `caller.public_mode` object, and the human-readable rendering uses `caller_public_mode=` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:138`). The caller identity is recorded as `system:public` as the spec requires (`pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go:139`), and the flag value is set for public-mode read calls (`internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:45`). The dotted form in the spec prose reads as an informal illustration of fields whose wire format is defined in §8.1, so the behavior is correct and only the field-name notation differs. Suggested direction: confirm with the §8.1 audit-schema owner that `caller_public_mode` is the intended key and, if so, adjust the §13.2.2 prose to name the actual key to avoid the dotted-path reading.

## F-13.3 — 13.3 Backup and Restore

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.3 against the implementation._

Section 13.3 (`spec/13-deployment.md:69-74`) is a four-bullet operational guidance block. It states that Postgres uses logical and physical backups with point-in-time recovery, that object storage uses cross-region replication or snapshots, that a consistent restore is achieved via PITR plus object-storage version history, and that the default targets are RPO 1h and RTO 4h. These are responsibilities of the managed database and object-storage layers (for example RDS, Cloud SQL, or Aurora PITR and S3 object versioning), configured outside the registry binary. None of the four bullets defines a wire format, HTTP endpoint, error code, CLI command, config key, environment variable, default value, or file layout that the Go implementation is required to provide.

I confirmed there is no code-level contract to trace. A search for `backup`, `restore`, `pitr`, `rpo`, `rto`, `pg_dump`, `pg_basebackup`, `wal`, `version history`, and `snapshot` across `pkg/`, `internal/`, `cmd/`, and `deploy/` surfaces no disaster-recovery backup or restore implementation. The only `restore` surface in the code is the §8.4 layer soft-delete recovery, which is a different concept: it is wired at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:249` (`/v1/layers/restore`) and `pkg/store/postgres.go:721` (`RestoreLayerConfig`), and the CLI exposes it at `cmd/podium/layer.go:34` as recovery of a layer unregistered within the §8.4 window. The object-storage backends in `pkg/objectstore/` expose no versioning or version-id API surface, which is consistent with §13.3 delegating object-storage version history to the storage provider. The reference compose stack (`docker-compose.yml`) and Helm chart (`deploy/helm/podium/values.yaml`) carry no backup, replication, or RPO/RTO configuration, and §13.3 does not require them to.

Because §13.3 states operator-facing recommendations rather than behavior the registry binary must exhibit, there is no implementation gap to report against this subsection.

No findings.

## F-13.4 — 13.4 Migrations

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.4 against the implementation._

I extracted the checkable claims from §13.4 (`spec/13-deployment.md:76`-`80`): the registry applies its metadata-store schema from the binary on startup; each backend's setup is idempotent and additive, creating tables when absent and adding new columns when absent via `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` and `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`; a binary upgrade migrates an existing database forward in place without a separate migration step and without downtime; the SQLite and Postgres schema live in their respective `applySchema` paths; and type definitions are compiled into the binary so a binary upgrade is the type-system migration with no separate versioned type-migration artifact.

Several claims hold. The metadata-store schema is applied from the binary on startup inside the store constructors (`pkg/store/sqlite.go:52`, `pkg/store/postgres.go:39`), and both backends keep their schema in `applySchema` paths (`pkg/store/sqlite.go:63`, `pkg/store/postgres.go:76`). Table and index creation is idempotent through `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` and `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` (`pkg/store/sqlite.go:65`, `pkg/store/postgres.go:78`). The type-system claim holds: the `TypeProvider` SPI registers first-class and extension validators as compiled code (`pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:1`, `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:137`), so a binary upgrade carries the type definitions and no separate type-migration artifact exists.

The additive-column claim does not hold for the metadata store. The `applySchema` paths contain only `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` and `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS`; neither path has any `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` logic, so columns added to existing tables in later binary versions are not backfilled onto a pre-existing database. The findings below record this gap and the incorrect SQLite syntax citation.

### - [x] F-13.4.1 — Metadata store never adds columns to existing tables [High] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit `b4491c4`): added `pkg/store/schema_migrate.go`, which declares every post-initial additive column once and applies it from both metadata stores' `applySchema`. Each `applySchema` now creates tables, runs the additive migration, then creates indexes (the `idx_manifests_tenant_layer` index references the backfilled `layer` column, so it must follow the migration). SQLite uses a guarded `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` that tolerates the duplicate-column error; Postgres uses `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`. A database initialized by an earlier binary (for example one predating `manifests.deleted_at`) is now migrated forward in place, so the soft-delete and retention reads succeed. Covered by unit (`pkg/store`), integration (`test/integration`), and e2e (`test/e2e`, via `migrate-to-standard` against a legacy source) tests that fail without the change.

(bug) §13.4 claims each backend's setup is "additive: tables are created when absent and new columns are added when absent (`CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`, `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`), so a binary upgrade migrates an existing database forward in place" (`spec/13-deployment.md:78`). The SQLite and Postgres `applySchema` paths build each table only with `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` (`pkg/store/sqlite.go:63`-`168`, `pkg/store/postgres.go:76`-`181`) and contain no `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` statement; a repository-wide search for `ALTER TABLE`/`ADD COLUMN`/`PRAGMA table_info`/`information_schema.columns` across `pkg/store`, `pkg/registry`, `internal/`, and `cmd/` returns nothing. `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` is a no-op on an existing table, so columns added to a table after that table first shipped are never created on a database initialized by an earlier binary. This is concretely reachable: the `manifests` table was introduced in commit `3fb9e1a` while the `deleted_at` column was added later in commit `2556f99`, so a registry upgraded against a pre-`2556f99` database would lack `deleted_at` and the soft-delete and retention reads that reference it would fail with a missing-column error. The contrast is visible inside the codebase, where the vector backends do perform additive column migration for the same `model_id` evolution (`pkg/vector/sqlitevec.go:118`, `pkg/vector/pgvector.go:75`). The spec's promise of in-place forward migration without a separate migration step therefore breaks for any column added after a table's initial schema. Suggested direction: add explicit additive column migration to both metadata-store `applySchema` paths, using `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` for Postgres and a guarded `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` that tolerates the duplicate-column error for SQLite, mirroring the pattern already used in `pkg/vector/sqlitevec.go:116`-`121`.

### - [ ] F-13.4.2 — SQLite cannot run the cited `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` syntax [Low] — DEFERRED

Deferred (depends-on read-only spec): the F-13.4.1 fix already implements the §13.4 intent for SQLite via a guarded `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` that ignores the duplicate-column error (`applyAdditiveSQLite` in `pkg/store/schema_migrate.go`), reserving `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` for the Postgres path (`applyAdditivePostgres`). The remaining inconsistency is solely in the §13.4 prose, which names a SQLite syntax the engine does not support; correcting it requires editing read-only spec text (Ground Rule A). No code defect remains, so there is nothing to change in the implementation.

(inconsistency) §13.4 cites `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` as the additive-migration mechanism for both backends, including SQLite ("The SQLite and Postgres schema live in their respective `applySchema` paths"), at `spec/13-deployment.md:78`. SQLite does not support `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`; the codebase itself documents this where the vector backend notes "SQLite has no ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS, so ignore the duplicate-column error on an already-migrated database" and instead issues a bare `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` guarded against the duplicate-column error (`pkg/vector/sqlitevec.go:115`-`121`). The spec text presents a syntax that the SQLite backend could not use even if additive migration were implemented there. Suggested direction: correct the §13.4 text to describe the SQLite path as a guarded `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` that ignores the duplicate-column error, reserving `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` for the Postgres path.

## F-13.5 — 13.5 Multi-Region

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.5 against the implementation._

Section §13.5 is a short operational note (`spec/13-deployment.md:82-84`). It states that a deployment is single-region, that cross-region read replicas are achieved via Postgres logical replication and object-storage replication, and that writes route to the primary region. These are deployment-topology and infrastructure statements rather than application-level contracts. The section names no wire formats, JSON field names, HTTP methods or paths, status codes, error envelopes, CLI commands or flags, config keys, environment variables, default values, file layouts, or validation rules that the application code must implement.

The mechanisms §13.5 references are delivered outside the application: Postgres logical replication is a database feature configured at the cluster level, object-storage replication is an S3 or object-store feature configured at the bucket level, and "writes route to the primary region" describes the deployment connecting the application to a primary Postgres endpoint rather than any in-process routing logic. A scan of `pkg/`, `internal/`, `cmd/`, and `sdks/` finds no application-level multi-region routing, "primary region" selection, or write-routing code, which is consistent with the spec framing. The only "region" identifiers in the code are unrelated S3 object-store region settings such as `pkg/objectstore/s3.go:32` and `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1464`. The read-replica replication-lag plumbing that does exist (`pkg/store/postgres.go:60`, `internal/serverboot/readiness.go:43`) measures replica replay lag via `pg_last_xact_replay_timestamp()` and is attached to §13.2.1 read-only mode, which is an adjacent subsection owned by another agent and not part of this review.

No findings.

## F-13.6 — 13.6 Sizing

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.6 against the implementation._

Section 13.6 spans `spec/13-deployment.md:86`–`spec/13-deployment.md:94` and consists entirely of deployment capacity-planning guidance. It states a baseline (10K artifacts, 100 QPS, 1 GB Postgres, 500 GB object storage on a 3-replica deployment plus a `db.m5.large` equivalent) and three scale-guidance bullets that recommend pgvector scaling and embedding sharding at 100K artifacts, additional front-end replicas and a CDN at 1K QPS, and a review of search query patterns or dedicated Elasticsearch for BM25 at 10K QPS. Every statement is an operator recommendation phrased with hedged verbs such as "consider," "scale," and "review." The section defines no wire formats, JSON field names, HTTP methods, paths, status codes, error envelopes, CLI commands, flags, config keys, environment variables, default values, file layout, ordering rules, or validation rules that the implementation must satisfy.

The mechanisms the section references do exist in the codebase, which confirms the guidance is not pointing at absent functionality: the pgvector backend is implemented in `pkg/vector/pgvector.go`, the vector backend registry that selects among backends is in `pkg/vector/registry.go`, and the hybrid-search reciprocal-rank fusion used for the BM25-style ranking lives in `pkg/registry/core/rrf.go`. None of these impose a §13.6 contract; the CDN and presigned-URL details belong to §13.7, which is out of scope for this subsection.
