Because §13.6 contains only conceptual sizing guidance with no checkable implementation contract, there is nothing in the code that can satisfy or violate it.

No findings.

## F-13.7 — 13.7 CDN

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.7 against the implementation._

Section 13.7 (`spec/13-deployment.md:96`) is brief and largely a recommendation to place CloudFront, Fastly, or Cloudflare in front of object storage. It states two concrete, checkable properties: presigned URLs are CDN-friendly, and cache headers are safe because `content_hash` keys are immutable. Both hold in the implementation. The S3 backend returns AWS Signature V4 presigned GET URLs with a configurable TTL (`pkg/objectstore/s3.go:191`), and the registry uses these for large bundled resources (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:949`). The object-store key is the bare content hash with the `sha256:` prefix stripped (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:985`), which makes the bytes for a given key immutable. The immutable `Cache-Control` value `public, max-age=31536000, immutable` is defined once (`pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:84`) and applied at both origins: the filesystem `/objects/{key}` route sets it on every GET and HEAD response (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:1066`), and the S3 backend stores it as object metadata at `Put` time so presigned GET responses inherit it (`pkg/objectstore/s3.go:120`).

I traced each checkable claim to code and re-read the cited handlers and backend methods to confirm the behavior. The presigned-URL generation, the content-hash-derived immutable key, and the immutable cache-header emission across both object-store backends all satisfy what §13.7 requires. The remaining sentence in the section recommends specific CDN products and states no implementation contract.

No findings.

## F-13.8 — 13.8 Observability

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.8 against the implementation._

I traced every concrete claim in §13.8 (`spec/13-deployment.md:100`-`104`): the Prometheus endpoint on the registry and the MCP server, the histogram, counter, and gauge families, the `PODIUM_METRICS=false` and `PODIUM_MCP_METRICS_ADDR` / `--metrics-addr` switches, the OpenTelemetry trace export, the W3C propagator, the named root and child spans, the `PODIUM_TRACING` / `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT` configuration, and the reference Grafana dashboard.

Most of the surface holds. The registry exposes the `/metrics` endpoint by default and removes it on `PODIUM_METRICS=false` (`internal/serverboot/metrics_wiring.go:16`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:723`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:974`). The histogram (`podium_request_duration_seconds`), the cache hit/miss counters, the visibility-denial counter, and the ingest success/failure counters all exist and are wired to live recording sites (`pkg/metrics/metrics.go:62`, `pkg/registry/core/import_cache.go:70`, `internal/serverboot/metrics_wiring.go:54`, `internal/serverboot/reingest.go:85`). The MCP bridge serves its metric set only when an operator names an address through `PODIUM_MCP_METRICS_ADDR` or `--metrics-addr` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:264`, `cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:131`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:506`, `cmd/podium-mcp/metrics.go:18`). Tracing is off by default and activates through `PODIUM_TRACING=stdout|otlp` or `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT`, with the W3C composite propagator always installed in both processes (`pkg/tracing/tracing.go:45`, `pkg/tracing/tracing.go:72`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:111`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1128`). The bridge opens one root span per meta-tool call plus the registry round-trip, adapter-translation, and materialization child spans (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1035`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:494`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1377`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1395`). The reference Grafana dashboard ships at `deploy/grafana-dashboard.json`.

Three deviations remain: the registry metric set has no error-rate counter even though the spec lists one for the registry and MCP server, the spec-named object-storage fetch child span is never created, and the `podium_audit_outbox_depth` queue-depth gauge is registered but never updated.

### - [x] F-13.8.1 — Registry metric set has no error-rate counter [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) The spec mandates "counters for cache hit rate, error rate, visibility-denial rate, ingest success/failure rate" on the metrics surface for "registry and MCP server" (`spec/13-deployment.md:102`). The MCP bridge implements the error counter (`podium_mcp_request_errors_total` at `pkg/metrics/mcp.go:37`, incremented in `pkg/metrics/mcp.go:80`), but the registry metric set has no error counter. The registry's only request series is `podium_request_total{endpoint}` (`pkg/metrics/metrics.go:57`), and `ObserveRequest` discards the HTTP status it receives: the signature is `ObserveRequest(endpoint string, _ int, elapsed time.Duration)` and the status argument is dropped (`pkg/metrics/metrics.go:125`). No status label and no separate error counter exist, so the registry error rate cannot be derived from its `/metrics` output, and the shipped dashboard carries no error panel (the metric names in `deploy/grafana-dashboard.json` do not include any error series). Suggested direction: add a registry error counter (for example `podium_request_errors_total{endpoint}`) incremented when `ObserveRequest` receives a status at or above 400, or add a status-class label to `podium_request_total`, and reference it from the reference dashboard.

Resolution (commit 542ab69): added the `podium_request_errors_total{endpoint}`
counter to the registry metric set. `ObserveRequest` now uses the response
status it already receives and increments the error counter for any status at or
above 400, so the per-endpoint error rate is derivable. Added an "Error rate by
endpoint" panel to `deploy/grafana-dashboard.json` and the series to the e2e
dashboard-coverage list (`assertMetricsScrape` now drives a 400 so the series is
populated).

### - [x] F-13.8.2 — Object-storage fetch child span is never created [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) The spec lists "child spans for registry round-trip, object-storage fetch, adapter translation, materialization" under one root span per meta-tool call (`spec/13-deployment.md:103`). The implementation creates the root span (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1035`), the registry round-trip span via the otelhttp transport (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:494`), the `adapter.translate` span (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1377`), and the `materialize` span (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1395`), but no span is opened for the object-storage fetch. A repository-wide search for span-start sites returns only those three explicit `tracing.Tracer().Start` calls plus the otelhttp transport and handler wrappers; the object-storage read on the registry side (`pkg/objectstore`) is not wrapped in any `tracing.Tracer().Start`, and the registry's per-request otelhttp server span has no child span for the storage read. The named child span the spec requires is absent. Suggested direction: open a child span (for example `objectstore.fetch`) around the registry-side object-storage read so the four spans the spec names all appear in an exported trace.

Resolution (commit 542ab69): `fetchLargeResources` (the bridge's §6.6 step 1
data-plane read of each large_resource from object storage via its presigned
URL) now opens an `objectstore.fetch` child span under the active meta-tool root
span, as a sibling to the registry round-trip, `adapter.translate`, and
`materialize` spans, so an exported `load_artifact` trace carries all four named
child spans. The span is opened only when the manifest carries large resources,
so a manifest-only call records no empty span.

### - [x] F-13.8.3 — `podium_audit_outbox_depth` gauge is registered but never updated [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) The spec requires "gauges for queue depths" (`spec/13-deployment.md:102`). The implementation registers two outbox gauges, `podium_vector_outbox_depth` and `podium_audit_outbox_depth` (`pkg/metrics/metrics.go:91`, `pkg/metrics/metrics.go:95`). The vector gauge is driven from the drain worker through `SetVectorOutboxDepth` (`internal/serverboot/vector_outbox.go:98`), but `SetAuditOutboxDepth` (`pkg/metrics/metrics.go:160`) has no caller anywhere in `pkg/`, `internal/`, or `cmd/`, so the audit gauge always reports 0. No audit-export outbox queue mechanism exists to feed it (`pkg/audit` contains no outbox or queue-depth source). The gauge advertises a queue depth that is never observed. Suggested direction: either wire `SetAuditOutboxDepth` to the audit-export backlog once that queue exists, or remove the gauge so `/metrics` does not export a series that is permanently 0.

Resolution (commit 542ab69): removed the phantom `podium_audit_outbox_depth`
gauge (the field, the `GaugeFunc`, and the dead `SetAuditOutboxDepth` setter).
No audit-export outbox queue exists to feed it (`EndpointSink` POSTs each event
synchronously with no backlog), so the series was permanently 0. §13.8's "gauges
for queue depths" is satisfied by the live `podium_vector_outbox_depth`. Dropped
the audit target from the dashboard's outbox panel and the series from the e2e
dashboard-coverage list.

## F-13.9 — 13.9 Health and Readiness

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.9 against the implementation._

I reviewed the §13.9 claims for the registry `/healthz` liveness endpoint, the `/readyz` readiness endpoint (including its Postgres and object-storage reachability probes, its `mode: ready | read_only | not_ready` field, its load-balancer status semantics, and its replication-lag body field), and the MCP `health` tool (registry connectivity, observed mode, cache size, and last-successful-call timestamp). Every concrete claim in §13.9 is satisfied by the current code.

The registry exposes both endpoints: `mux.HandleFunc("/healthz", s.handleHealth)` and `mux.HandleFunc("/readyz", s.handleReady)` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:325-326`. `/healthz` is liveness-only and reports the mode string via `modeBanner()` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:529-546`), returning `public`, `read_only`, or `ready`. `/readyz` computes its state in `readyMode` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:578-591`) with the documented precedence: a failing dependency probe yields `not_ready`, then the §13.2.1 tracker yields `read_only`, then `ready`. The mode strings match the spec exactly (`pkg/registry/server/readonly.go:32-42`: `ready`, `read_only`, `not_ready`). The load-balancer status semantics are correct: `read_only` and `ready` return HTTP 200 (in rotation) and `not_ready` returns 503 (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:564-567`). The `/readyz` body carries the observed replication lag as `replication_lag_seconds` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:549-552`, `replicationLagSeconds` at 596-604, clamped to 0 for no-replica deployments).

The readiness probes are wired in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:811-815`: a metadata-store probe (`storeReadinessCheck` pinging `GetTenant` at `internal/serverboot/readiness.go:17-22`) and a conditionally-added object-store probe (`objectStoreReadinessCheck` at `internal/serverboot/readiness.go:33-41`), which together satisfy the "Postgres and object-storage reachability" claim. Probes are bounded by a 2-second deadline (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:98`, `handleReady:560`). Replication lag is sourced from `Postgres.ReplicationLagSeconds` via `pg_last_xact_replay_timestamp()` (`pkg/store/postgres.go:60-71`), with non-Postgres backends reporting 0 (`internal/serverboot/readiness.go:47-59`). Both health paths are exempted from identity verification (`pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go:64`) and latency instrumentation (`pkg/registry/server/latency.go:64`). The MCP `health` tool is registered (`cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:106-110`), dispatched (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1080-1083`), and reports all required fields: `registry` and `connected` (connectivity), `mode` mapped to `ready`/`read_only`/`unreachable`, `cache_size`, and `last_successful_call` (`cmd/podium-mcp/health.go:19-86`). The build compiles and the §13.9 tests under `pkg/registry/server` and `cmd/podium-mcp` pass.

No findings.

## F-13.10 — 13.10 Standalone Deployment

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.10 against the implementation._

This review traced the §13.10 standalone-deployment contract through `cmd/podium/serve.go`, `internal/serverboot` (the shared bootstrap), `pkg/registry/server` (startup validation, public mode, health endpoints), `pkg/registry/filesystem` (the `--layer-path` dispatch), `pkg/registry/ingest` (the public-mode sensitivity ceiling), and `cmd/podium-mcp` (the MCP `health` tool and signature-verification resolution). Most concrete claims hold. The zero-flag standalone defaults resolve correctly: the metadata store defaults to `~/.podium/standalone/podium.db` and the object store to `~/.podium/standalone/objects/` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1622`, `:1628`), the bind to `127.0.0.1:8080` (`:1445`), the vector backend to `sqlite-vec` and the embedding provider to `ollama` (`:1585`, `:1592`). The first-run notice text matches the spec (`internal/serverboot/standalone_bootstrap.go:32`), and the bootstrap writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (`defaults.registry`, `verify_signatures: never`) and `~/.podium/registry.yaml` only when absent (`standalone_bootstrap.go:118`, `:128`). The `--strict` / `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE` hard-error path and the explicit-`--config`-missing-file error are both present (`serverboot.go:604`, `standalone_bootstrap.go:29`). Public-mode guards are correct: `config.public_mode_with_idp` and the loopback-bind refusal (`pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go:62`, `:69`), the verbatim startup banner (`serverboot.go:1164`), the visibility short-circuit via `id.IsPublic` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:1090`), the `ingest.public_mode_rejects_sensitive` ceiling (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:543`), and the `system:public` audit caller (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1608`). The `--layer-path` single-layer / filesystem-registry dispatch and the `config.layer_path_ambiguous` safety check are implemented (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:132`, `:201`). The `--sign registry-key` opt-in and the web-UI non-loopback guard are present (`internal/serverboot/signing.go:21`, `config_validate.go:77`). The findings below cover one public-mode surfacing gap, one missing override env var, and two error-string / field-naming mismatches.

### - [x] F-13.10.1 — MCP `health` tool never surfaces `mode: public` [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 2db2f42): `probeRegistryMode` now probes `/healthz` (the public-mode signal) after the `/readyz` readiness probe and returns `public` when the registry reports it, so the MCP `health` tool surfaces `mode: public` per §13.10. `/readyz` is unchanged (its vocabulary stays ready/read_only/not_ready); public outranks read_only and ready, matching the registry's `modeBanner` precedence. The `public` value joins the tool's mode vocabulary alongside ready/read_only/unreachable. Tests: 3 cmd/podium-mcp units (public detected, public outranks read_only, non-public keeps readiness), 1 integration (real binary against a public-mode in-process registry), and 1 e2e (real binary against `podium serve --public-mode`).

(gap) §13.10 line 214 states the public mode "is surfaced in `/healthz` (`mode: public`), in the MCP `health` tool, in `podium status`, and as a flag (`caller.public_mode: true`) on every audit event so downstream tooling can detect it without inspecting startup config." The MCP `health` tool probes the registry's `/readyz` endpoint, not `/healthz` (`cmd/podium-mcp/health.go:56`), and `/readyz` deliberately omits the `public` state because public mode is a `/healthz`-only signal (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:571`-`:573`, comment: "public mode is a /healthz signal, not a readiness state, so it is intentionally absent here"). Even if `/readyz` did report `public`, `probeRegistryMode` maps every non-`read_only` 2xx response to `"ready"` (`cmd/podium-mcp/health.go:79`-`:80`), so the tool's `mode` field can only be `ready`, `read_only`, or `unreachable`. A consumer that reads the MCP `health` tool cannot detect that the registry is running in public mode, contradicting the spec's explicit list of checkpoints. The other three surfaces (`/healthz` via `modeBanner` at `server.go:539`, `podium status` via `decodeHealthMode` at `cmd/podium/status.go:52`, and the `caller_public_mode` audit flag at `pkg/audit/file.go:172`) do report it. Suggested direction: have the MCP `health` tool probe `/healthz` (or additionally read its `mode`) and pass `public` through its mode vocabulary so downstream tooling can detect public mode as the spec requires.

### - [x] F-13.10.2 — `PODIUM_ENFORCE_SANDBOX_PROFILE` override env var is absent [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 826bd1a): implemented the `PODIUM_ENFORCE_SANDBOX_PROFILE` registry ingest gate. When set, the registry refuses to ingest an artifact whose `sandbox_profile` the local host cannot honor; the host's enforceable set comes from `PODIUM_HOST_SANDBOXES` (default `unrestricted`), and the empty profile and `unrestricted` are always enforceable. Rejection uses the new `ingest.sandbox_profile_unenforceable` code. The gate is off by default, so standalone keeps `sandbox_profile` informational (the permissive default holds). It threads through `ingest.Request` / `SourceIngestOptions` and all three serverboot ingest sites (declared layers, the `--layer-path` bootstrap, and manual reingest / inbound webhook). The MCP host already read this env var for the separate §4.4.1 materialize-time gate; this adds the §13.10 registry-side behavior the spec documents. Covered by a `pkg/registry/ingest` unit table test, an orchestrator-threading integration test, and standalone e2e tests for both the enforced rejection and the permissive default.

(gap) §13.10 line 179 states that in standalone "`sandbox_profile:` is informational ... the registry does not refuse to ingest artifacts whose profiles can't be enforced locally. Override with `PODIUM_ENFORCE_SANDBOX_PROFILE=true` in multi-user setups," and line 182 states "Any of these defaults can be flipped to standard-mode behavior via the named env var without otherwise changing the deployment." The string `PODIUM_ENFORCE_SANDBOX_PROFILE` does not appear anywhere in `internal/` or `pkg/` (no enforcement gate reads it; the ingest pipeline has no `sandbox_profile` enforcement path at all, confirmed by the absence of any such check in `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go`). The permissive default holds trivially because no enforcement exists, but the documented knob to flip it to standard-mode behavior is unimplemented, so an operator setting `PODIUM_ENFORCE_SANDBOX_PROFILE=true` for a multi-user standalone gets no effect. Suggested direction: either implement the `PODIUM_ENFORCE_SANDBOX_PROFILE` ingest gate that rejects artifacts whose `sandbox_profile` cannot be enforced, or reconcile the spec if the enforcement behavior is intentionally out of scope.

### - [x] F-13.10.3 — `config.layer_path_ambiguous` error code is not surfaced as that string at startup [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit a9eaded): `ErrLayerPathAmbiguous`'s message now leads with the literal `config.layer_path_ambiguous` code, so the §13.10 startup/sync refusal surfaces the documented code verbatim through the existing bootstrap and CLI error wraps while still naming the conflicting top-level manifest paths. Covered by the filesystem unit test, the serverboot bootstrap unit test, and the sync integration and e2e tests, each tightened to assert the code string.

(inconsistency) §13.10 line 156 states that when `multi_layer: true` is set but the safety check fails, "the server refuses to start with `config.layer_path_ambiguous`, naming the conflicting top-level manifest paths." The implementation refuses to start and names the manifest paths (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:218`: "top-level manifest(s): ..."), but the error value is `ErrLayerPathAmbiguous` whose message is `"filesystem: layer path ambiguous (multi_layer: true but manifests at top level)"` (`registry.go:29`), and the bootstrap wraps it only as `"open layer path %s: %w"` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:339`). The literal code `config.layer_path_ambiguous` never appears in the surfaced startup error; a `grep` for it across `internal/serverboot` and `cmd/podium` returns nothing. The refusal and the manifest-naming behavior are correct; only the named error code differs. Suggested direction: include the `config.layer_path_ambiguous` code in the surfaced error (for example by setting `ErrLayerPathAmbiguous`'s message to that code or mapping it at startup) so operators and tooling see the documented code.

### - [x] F-13.10.4 — Audit public-mode flag is `caller_public_mode`, spec illustrates `caller.public_mode` [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 9b83b84): the audit event now emits the public-mode flag under the nested key `caller.public_mode`, matching the §13.10 line-214 illustration, via the §8.1 caller-object change (F-8.1.2). The flag is still set on every public-mode event and participates in the tamper-evident hash chain. Covered by the same `pkg/audit` and serverboot/e2e tests as F-8.1.2.

(inconsistency) §13.10 line 214 illustrates the per-event public-mode flag as `caller.public_mode: true`. The audit event serializes this flag under the JSON key `caller_public_mode` (`pkg/audit/file.go:172`: `PublicMode bool \`json:"caller_public_mode,omitempty"\``), and the file-line encoder emits `caller_public_mode=` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:138`). The flag is present and set correctly on every event in public mode, so the behavioral contract holds; only the dotted-versus-underscore field name in the spec's prose illustration differs from the wire key. Suggested direction: treat the spec illustration as informal and align it to the actual `caller_public_mode` key, or rename the wire key if the dotted form is intended; no code behavior change is required for correctness.

## F-13.11 — 13.11 Filesystem Registry (13.11.1 Layout, 13.11.2 Config, 13.11.3 Availability, 13.11.4 Watch, 13.11.5 Shared Dir, 13.11.6 Migrate to Server)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.11 against the implementation._

I traced every concrete claim in §13.11 to the filesystem-registry source under `pkg/registry/filesystem`, the sync orchestrator under `pkg/sync`, the CLI dispatch in `cmd/podium/main.go`, and the standalone `--layer-path` bootstrap in `internal/serverboot`. The directory-layout dispatch holds: `filesystem.Open` returns `ModeSingleLayer` when `.registry-config` is absent or sets `multi_layer: false`, and `ModeMultiLayer` only when `multi_layer: true`, with one `local`-source layer per subdirectory (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:128-199`). `multi_layer` defaults to `false` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:60-63`), layer order follows `layer_order:` lowest-precedence-first then alphabetical (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:223-273`, with highest-precedence-wins composition at `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:46-77`), layer IDs default to the subdirectory name (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:180-191`), and the `multi_layer: true` safety check refuses top-level manifests with `config.layer_path_ambiguous` naming the offending files (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:201-221`).

The configuration claims in §13.11.2 hold: relative `defaults.registry` resolves against the workspace and absolute paths pass through (`pkg/sync/config.go:73-87`), an unset registry across all scopes errors with `config.no_registry` and points at `podium init` with no implicit `<workspace>/.podium/registry/` fallback (`cmd/podium/main.go:262-271`), and scope precedence lets a higher-precedence path override an inherited URL (`pkg/sync/resolve.go:88-129`). The §13.11.3 availability claims hold: the filesystem source runs the shared composer, `extends:` resolver (`manifest.MergeExtends` via `pkg/registry/filesystem/extends.go:29-115`), and harness adapters; it writes the lock at `<target>/.podium/sync.lock` (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:66`); `override` and `save-as` re-materialize through the same `Run` path (`pkg/sync/override.go:124-150`); and no auth token is read for a filesystem source (`cmd/podium/main.go:317-320`). The §13.11.4 watch mode uses `fsnotify` over both the registry path and the workspace overlay (`pkg/sync/watch.go:97-103`, `pkg/sync/watch_fsnotify.go:27-64`), with a poll fallback when `fsnotify` cannot initialize, and both reruns and one-shot sync share the same stale-file cleanup via `Run` (`pkg/sync/sync.go:263-283`). The §13.11.6 migration claims hold: the standalone `--layer-path` bootstrap reuses the same `filesystem.Open` dispatch (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:333-402`), and `podium admin migrate-to-standard` exists (`cmd/podium/admin.go:57-58`).

No findings.

## F-13.12 — 13.12 Backend Configuration Reference (metadata store, object storage, vector, embedding, identity, config file format)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md §13.12 against the implementation._

This section audits the server-side backend configuration surface: the metadata-store, object-storage, vector, embedding, and identity selectors, their per-backend environment variables and defaults, the `registry.yaml` config-file format, and the precedence rule. The bulk of the contract is implemented in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` (`LoadConfig`, `validate`, `openStore`, `openObjectStore`, `openVectorBackend`, `openEmbedder`) and `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go` (the `registry.yaml` parser and overlay). Most concrete claims hold. The metadata-store selector, defaults, and required-DSN check are correct (`serverboot.go:1454`, `serverboot.go:1663`, `serverboot.go:1742`). The object-storage selectors, the `~/.podium/standalone/podium.db` and `~/.podium/standalone/objects` defaults, the `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` default of 3600 (`objectstore/objectstore.go:71`), the S3 endpoint URL-scheme TLS derivation (`objectstore/s3.go:97`), and the IAM-fallback credential chain (`objectstore/s3.go:85`) are all correct. The embedding-provider defaults match the spec exactly: `text-embedding-3-small` (`embedding/openai.go:36`), `https://api.openai.com/v1` (`embedding/openai.go:57`), `voyage-3` (`embedding/voyage.go:34`), `embed-v4` (`embedding/cohere.go:34`), `nomic-embed-text` and `http://localhost:11434` (`embedding/ollama.go:38`, `embedding/ollama.go:61`). The Pinecone `default` namespace fallback (`serverboot.go:1551`), the `config.public_mode_with_idp` mutual-exclusion error (`pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go:62`), the self-embedding optionality of the embedding provider (`serverboot.go:1719`), the empty-string embedding disable (`serverboot.go:1588`), the "refuses to start ... naming the missing keys" hard-error (`serverboot.go:1666`), and the reserved-and-unread gRPC env vars (no reads found for `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_GRPC_URL` / `PODIUM_QDRANT_GRPC_PORT`) are all correct.

The findings below cover a config-file coverage gap where several documented env vars have no `registry.yaml` key, a config-file embedding-model value that is parsed but never applied to the built-in providers, the unimplemented Pinecone host auto-resolution, and a narrow `bind` precedence edge case.

### - [x] F-13.12.1 — Several documented env vars have no `registry.yaml` config-file key [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit dfc044b): added the missing `registry.yaml` keys and routed them with env precedence — `object_store.access_key_id` / `secret_access_key` / `presign_ttl_seconds`, `vector_backend.host` (Pinecone) / `url` (Weaviate/Qdrant), and `embedding_provider.base_url` / `org` (OpenAI) / `url` (Ollama). `openEmbedder` now reads OpenAI base URL/org from the resolved Config fields rather than env-only, so a deployment can be configured entirely via `registry.yaml`. The reserved-and-unread gRPC vars are intentionally left without keys.

(gap) §13.12 states at `spec/13-deployment.md:345` that "All env vars below are also valid config-file keys (snake-cased under the relevant section)". The `registry.yaml` parser does not provide keys for a number of the documented env vars. `yamlObjectCfg` (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:100`) has no `access_key_id` / `secret_access_key` field for `PODIUM_S3_ACCESS_KEY_ID` / `PODIUM_S3_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` (`spec/13-deployment.md:369`) and no `presign_ttl_seconds` for `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` (`spec/13-deployment.md:372`); `yamlVectorCfg` (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:115`) has no `host` for `PODIUM_PINECONE_HOST` and no `url` for `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_URL` (`spec/13-deployment.md:401`) or `PODIUM_QDRANT_URL` (`spec/13-deployment.md:411`); `yamlEmbedCfg` (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:129`) has no key for `PODIUM_OPENAI_BASE_URL`, `PODIUM_OPENAI_ORG`, or `PODIUM_OLLAMA_URL`. Consequently `c.weaviateURL` and `c.qdrantURL` are sourced from env only (`serverboot.go:1484`, `serverboot.go:1489`), so a `weaviate-cloud` or `qdrant-cloud` deployment cannot be configured entirely via `registry.yaml` even though those backends mark the URL as required. The `${ENV_VAR}` interpolation does not close the gap because the YAML still needs a key to hold the interpolated value. Suggested direction: add the missing `registry.yaml` keys (`object_store.access_key_id` / `secret_access_key` / `presign_ttl_seconds`, `vector_backend.host` / `url`, `embedding_provider.base_url` / `org` / `url`) and route them in `applyYAML` / `applyVectorYAML` / `applyEmbeddingYAML`, or narrow the spec claim to the keys the example actually shows.

### - [x] F-13.12.2 — `embedding_provider.model` from `registry.yaml` is parsed but never applied to the built-in embedders [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit dfc044b): `openEmbedder` now resolves each built-in provider's model via `embeddingModelFor` (per-provider `PODIUM_*_MODEL` env wins, then `c.embeddingModel`, which carries the generic `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_MODEL` env or the registry.yaml `embedding_provider.model` key), so a config-file `model:` takes effect instead of falling back to the provider's hardcoded default.

(bug) The §13.12 config-file format documents `embedding_provider.model` (`spec/13-deployment.md:499`, shown as `model: text-embedding-3-large`). The parser reads it into `c.embeddingModel` (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:299`), but `openEmbedder` constructs each built-in provider with `Model_: envFirst("PODIUM_OPENAI_MODEL", "PODIUM_EMBEDDING_MODEL")` (`serverboot.go:1891`, and the analogous lines `1901`, `1909`, `1914`), reading the model from environment variables only and never from `c.embeddingModel`. `c.embeddingModel` is consumed only by `config show` (`serverboot.go:1407`) and the custom-provider settings map (`serverboot.go:1810`), so a deployment that sets the model only in `registry.yaml` for a built-in provider silently falls back to that provider's hardcoded default model. Suggested direction: have `openEmbedder` fall back to `c.embeddingModel` when the per-provider and generic `PODIUM_*_MODEL` env vars are unset, so the documented config-file `model:` key takes effect for the built-in providers.

### - [x] F-13.12.3 — Pinecone host is not auto-resolved from the index name [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit dfc044b): implemented `vector.ResolvePineconeHost`, which queries the Pinecone control-plane describe-index endpoint (`GET /indexes/{name}`, `Api-Key` header) and returns the data-plane host. `OpenBuiltin` now resolves the host from the index when `PODIUM_PINECONE_HOST` is empty (bounded 10s context; a failure surfaces an error so Run degrades to BM25 rather than starting half-configured). A `PODIUM_PINECONE_CONTROL_PLANE` override (also honored by the MCP overlay) makes the lookup testable and supports private deployments. An index-only Pinecone deployment is now functional as the spec advertises.

(inconsistency) §13.12 documents `PODIUM_PINECONE_HOST` with a default of "(auto-resolved from index name)" (`spec/13-deployment.md:393`) and marks only `PODIUM_PINECONE_INDEX` as required, implying a deployment that supplies the index alone is functional. `openVectorBackend` instead returns a hard error when the host is empty and only the index is set (`serverboot.go:1957`), and `NewPinecone` itself requires a non-empty host (`pkg/vector/pinecone.go:52`). No code path resolves the host from the index name. Because the validate step requires only `host || index` (`serverboot.go:1701`), validation passes but `openVectorBackend` then errors and Run downgrades to BM25-only search (`serverboot.go:733`) rather than honoring the index-only configuration the spec advertises. Suggested direction: either implement host resolution from the index name (a Pinecone control-plane lookup) or update §13.12 to mark `PODIUM_PINECONE_HOST` as required for serverless and drop the "auto-resolved" default.

### - [x] F-13.12.4 — `registry.yaml` `bind` can override an explicit env value equal to the loopback default [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit dfc044b): the `bind` overlay now guards on `os.Getenv("PODIUM_BIND") == ""` instead of comparing `c.bind` against the literal default `127.0.0.1:8080`, matching the store/region/force-path-style overlays. An explicit `PODIUM_BIND=127.0.0.1:8080` (or the `--bind` flag, which sets the same env var) is no longer overridden by the config-file `bind:`, restoring env-over-file precedence.

(bug) §13.12 specifies "Server-side precedence: CLI flag > env var > config file" (`spec/13-deployment.md:345`). `applyYAML` overlays the config-file `bind:` whenever the current value is empty or equals the literal default `127.0.0.1:8080` (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:242`). When an operator sets `PODIUM_BIND=127.0.0.1:8080` explicitly (a value that coincides with the hardcoded default), the code cannot distinguish the explicit env value from the default, so the config-file `bind:` overrides it, inverting the documented env-over-file precedence for that one value. Other env-overlay checks consult `os.Getenv` directly to avoid this (for example `serverboot.go` store/object-store overlays at `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:265` and `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:286`), but the `bind` path does not. Suggested direction: guard the `bind` overlay with `os.Getenv("PODIUM_BIND") == ""` the way the store, object-store region, and force-path-style overlays do, instead of comparing against the literal default string.

## F-14.1 — 14.1 Local registry folder, one-shot, single workspace

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.1 against the implementation._

This scenario describes a developer keeping artifacts in a local folder and materializing a subset into one project for Claude Code through a single CLI invocation against a filesystem-source registry. The checkable claims are the `podium init --global --registry <path>` command that writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry`, the interpretation of a filesystem path as a single `local`-source layer with multi-layer opt-in via `<path>/.registry-config` and `multi_layer: true`, the artifact directory layout (`ARTIFACT.md` plus `SKILL.md` for skills), the `profiles:` block with `include`/`exclude` glob lists in `.podium/sync.yaml`, the `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile myapp` command with a CWD-default target and a lock file at `<cwd>/.podium/sync.lock`, the `podium serve --standalone --layer-path <path>` graduation path pointing at `http://127.0.0.1:8080`, and the `podium profile edit` and `podium sync override --add/--remove` adjustment commands.

Every concrete claim holds against the current code. `initCmd` writes `defaults:\n  registry: <value>` to `~/.podium/sync.yaml` under `--global` (`cmd/podium/main.go:1052`, `cmd/podium/main.go:1091`). The filesystem registry defaults to `ModeSingleLayer` (one `local`-source layer rooted at the path) and switches to `ModeMultiLayer` only when `.registry-config` sets `multi_layer: true` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:132`, `pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:37`), and the recognized manifest filenames include `ARTIFACT.md` and `SKILL.md` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:95`). The `profiles:` block parses into `map[string]Profile` with `Include`/`Exclude` slices (`pkg/sync/config.go:26`, `pkg/sync/config.go:45`). `syncCmd` exposes `--harness`, `--profile`, and `--target`, defaults the target to `.` (`cmd/podium/main.go:197`, `cmd/podium/main.go:204`, `cmd/podium/main.go:286`), and the lock file is written at `<target>/.podium/sync.lock` (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:65`, `pkg/sync/sync.go:321`). The `claude-code` adapter is implemented (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:26`). `serveCmd` provides `--standalone` and `--layer-path` (`cmd/podium/serve.go:25`, `cmd/podium/serve.go:30`) and the server's default bind is `127.0.0.1:8080`, matching the `http://127.0.0.1:8080` URL in the graduation step (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1445`). `profileCmd` implements `podium profile edit <name>` (`cmd/podium/main.go:618`) and `syncOverrideCmd` implements `--add`/`--remove` (`cmd/podium/main.go:484`, `cmd/podium/main.go:491`).

No findings.

## F-14.2 — 14.2 Local registry folder, one-shot, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.2 against the implementation._

Section 14.2 is a scenario walkthrough that reuses the §14.1 single-workspace mechanics and asserts a small set of checkable contracts: the `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile <name>` invocation form, a per-workspace lock file at `<workspace>/.podium/sync.lock`, both workspaces reading from the same artifact directory, and the absence of any shared cache or registry process when the source is a filesystem registry. Each of these holds in the code. The `--harness` and `--profile` flags are both registered on the `sync` flag set (`cmd/podium/main.go:197` and `cmd/podium/main.go:204`), and the profile name resolves a named scope from `sync.yaml` profiles with collision and missing-profile handling (`pkg/sync/resolve.go:208`-`pkg/sync/resolve.go:226`). The lock file path is computed purely from the target directory as `<target>/.podium/sync.lock` (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:65`-`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:67`), and the target defaults to the current working directory when `--target` is unset (`cmd/podium/main.go:285`-`cmd/podium/main.go:288`), so each workspace gets its own lock keyed to its own directory with no shared global lock state (`pkg/sync/sync.go:208`, `pkg/sync/sync.go:321`). A filesystem-source registry is read directly off disk through `filesystem.Open` and `Walk` (`pkg/sync/sync.go:445`-`pkg/sync/sync.go:454`), and the §7.4 cache modes are explicitly a no-op for a filesystem source (`pkg/sync/sync.go:180`-`pkg/sync/sync.go:184`, `pkg/sync/sync.go:95`-`pkg/sync/sync.go:101`), which matches the claim that "no shared cache or registry process is needed."

No findings.

## F-14.3 — 14.3 Local registry folder, MCP discovery, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.3 against the implementation._

I traced every checkable claim in §14.3 (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:41`–`47`) to the Go implementation. The subsection describes graduating from a filesystem source to a standalone server for MCP progressive disclosure. Each concrete claim holds. The `podium serve --standalone --layer-path <dir>` command is implemented: the `--standalone` flag is defined at `cmd/podium/serve.go:25` and `--layer-path` at `cmd/podium/serve.go:30`, the latter setting `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` (`cmd/podium/serve.go:58`), which the server ingests at startup through `bootstrapLayerPath` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:705`). The auto-bootstrap of `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080` is correct: `standaloneStartup` runs from `Run()` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:623`) and calls `bootstrapStandaloneFiles`, which writes `defaults.registry: <publicURL>` (`internal/serverboot/standalone_bootstrap.go:118`); `publicURL` defaults to `http://` plus `bind` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1639`–`1640`) and `bind` defaults to `127.0.0.1:8080` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1445`), so the written value matches the spec literally.

The MCP claims also hold. The meta-tools `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` are registered (`cmd/podium-mcp/descriptions.go:49`, `61`, `74`, `89`) and dispatched (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:1068`–`1077`). The MCP server resolves the registry from `~/.podium/sync.yaml` `defaults.registry` with no extra environment variable: when `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is unset, `loadConfig` falls back to `registryFromSyncYAML()` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:287`–`288`), which reads `defaults.registry` from the workspace overlay and then the home-global file (`cmd/podium-mcp/cliconfig.go:143`–`166`). The optional per-workspace `.podium/overlay/` is supported: `resolveWorkspaceOverlay` defaults the overlay to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` when present (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:908`–`928`). The bootstrap is correctly gated to the standalone (SQLite) deployment, which is the default store type (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1454`), so the §14.3 command path triggers it.

No findings.

## F-14.4 — 14.4 Local registry, custom harness via SDK, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.4 against the implementation._

Section §14.4 (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:49-59`) describes a scenario where each workspace runs an app built on `podium-py` or `podium-ts` plus an agent SDK. The checkable claims are that the SDK speaks HTTP against a standalone server started via `podium serve --standalone`, that the Python entry point is `from podium import Client` with `client = Client.from_env()`, that `from_env()` resolves the registry URL from `sync.yaml` plus an overlay path, and that the discovery flow uses `search_artifacts` and `load_artifact`. Each of these claims holds. `Client` is exported from `sdks/podium-py/podium/__init__.py:24`, and `Client.from_env()` is defined at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:384`; it resolves the registry from `PODIUM_REGISTRY` then the `sync.yaml`/`sync.local.yaml` scopes via `_config.resolve_registry` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/_config.py:88-115`) and resolves the overlay path at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:361-363`. The methods `search_artifacts` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:534`) and `load_artifact` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:633`) issue HTTP `GET` requests to `/v1/search_artifacts` and `/v1/load_artifact`. The TypeScript SDK mirrors the surface with `Client`, `fromEnv` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:390`), `searchArtifacts` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:517`), and `loadArtifact` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:586`), all over HTTP. The `podium serve --standalone` flag is registered at `cmd/podium/serve.go:25`.

The section is a brief illustrative scenario rather than a contract-dense specification, and every concrete identifier, method name, and command flag it names is present and consistent across both SDKs and the CLI.

No findings.

## F-14.5 — 14.5 Remote registry, one-shot, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.5 against the implementation._

This subsection is a scenario walkthrough that chains together CLI commands and behaviors defined in detail in other sections (`§7.7` init and login, `§6.3` device-code flow, `§7.5.2` sync resolution, `§4.6` layer visibility, `§7.3.1` ingest). It makes a small set of concrete, checkable claims about the per-developer commands, and every one of them holds against the code.

The claim that `podium init --global --registry <url>` writes the user-global config is satisfied: `initCmd` defines the `--global`, `--registry`, `--local`, `--standalone`, `--harness`, `--target`, and `--force` flags (`cmd/podium/main.go:999-1005`), treats `--global` and `--registry` as compatible (only `--global` and `--local` are mutually exclusive at `cmd/podium/main.go:1010-1013`), and under `--global` writes `defaults.registry` to `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (`cmd/podium/main.go:1052-1058`, `cmd/podium/main.go:1091`). The claim that `podium login` completes the device-code flow once and caches the token is satisfied: `loginCmd` runs `identity.DeviceCodeFlow.Initiate`/`Poll` under a 10-minute deadline (`cmd/podium/login.go:80-122`) and persists the access and refresh tokens to the OS keychain keyed by registry URL (`cmd/podium/login.go:124-128`, `cmd/podium/login.go:233-243`); the underlying flow uses the RFC 8628 `urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:device_code` grant (`pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:162-163`). The claim about `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile <name>` is satisfied: `syncCmd` defines both the `--harness` and `--profile` flags (`cmd/podium/main.go:197`, `cmd/podium/main.go:204`), `claude-code` is a registered adapter ID (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:26`), and named profiles from `sync.yaml` are merged and selected during resolution (`pkg/sync/resolve.go:138-163`). The claim that each workspace has its own lock file is satisfied: the lock is per-target at `<target>/.podium/sync.lock` (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:64-66`), so distinct workspace target directories get distinct lock files. The operator-side prerequisites it references (git-source layers and the webhook ingest endpoint) also exist (`pkg/layer/source/source.go`, `pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go`).

No findings.

## F-14.6 — 14.6 Remote registry + workspace local overlay, one-shot

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.6 against the implementation._

Section 14.6 (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:76`) describes a per-workspace flow over the §14.5 remote-registry operator setup: a developer drops in-progress artifacts under `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/`, then runs `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile <name>`. The section makes two checkable claims. First, the `--harness` and `--profile` flags exist on `podium sync`. Second, the overlay path auto-resolves to `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` per §6.4 with no environment variable set. The referenced §6.4 contract (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:74`) requires the overlay to merge as the highest-precedence layer in the caller's effective view, resolved by the consumer client-side because a server-source registry cannot see the local directory.

Both flags are present: `harness` at `cmd/podium/main.go:197` and `profile` at `cmd/podium/main.go:204`. The auto-resolution is implemented in `overlay.ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` (`pkg/overlay/overlay.go:64`), which honors `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` first and otherwise falls back to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` when that directory exists. The CLI wires this with `ws` set to the current working directory (`cmd/podium/main.go:229`, `os.Getwd()`) and passes it to the resolver at `cmd/podium/main.go:309`, so the fallback target is `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` exactly as §14.6 claims. The overlay is merged client-side at the highest precedence for both server and filesystem sources via `applyOverlay` (`pkg/sync/sync.go:409`), which replaces same-canonical-ID base records with overlay records and appends otherwise, matching §4.6 highest-wins semantics. The merge runs inside `resolveRecords` (`pkg/sync/sync.go:380`) before the dry-run branch (`pkg/sync/sync.go:259`), so the overlay is reflected in both real and dry-run output. End-to-end behavior is exercised by `TestRun_ServerSource_OverlayOverridesServer` (`pkg/sync/server_auth_overlay_test.go:75`), which confirms an overlay artifact overrides the server-sourced artifact at the same canonical ID. Every concrete claim in §14.6 holds against the current code.

No findings.

## F-14.7 — 14.7 Remote registry + local overlay, MCP, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.7 against the implementation._

This subsection describes the MCP consumer path: configure the harness's MCP server entry with `PODIUM_REGISTRY` and `PODIUM_HARNESS`, leave `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` optional (resolving the overlay from MCP roots per §6.4 when unset), complete the OAuth device-code flow via MCP elicitation on first call with the token cached in the OS keychain, and drop workspace-local artifacts under `.podium/overlay/` where the MCP server's watcher picks up changes. Most of the concrete claims hold. The MCP server reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY` and `PODIUM_HARNESS` at startup (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:235` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:224`) and refuses to start on an unknown harness value (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:355`). `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is optional and, when unset, the bridge issues a `roots/list` request and defaults the overlay to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` only if that directory exists (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:860`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:912`, and `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:64`), with the env var correctly taking precedence over roots (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:861`). The device-code flow surfaces the verification URL and code via an `elicitation/create` request and persists both access and refresh tokens to the keychain on success (`cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:108`, `cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go:185`, and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:501`). The overlay watcher is started in the serve loop and re-resolves records on change (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:732`, `cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:25`).

The one divergence found concerns the watcher mechanism. Both §14.7 and the §6.4 contract it references name fsnotify explicitly, while the MCP server implements the overlay watcher as a fixed-interval poller.

### - [x] F-14.7.1 — MCP overlay watcher polls instead of using fsnotify [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit c808db3): same fix as F-6.4.3. The MCP overlay watcher now uses fsnotify (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go`, reusing `sync.TreeWatcher`), so §14.7 step 3 ("The MCP server's fsnotify watcher picks up changes") and the §6.4 contract it references both hold; a content-fingerprint poll remains only as the fsnotify-init fallback. Covered by the F-6.4.3 unit tests and the `TestPodiumMCP_OverlayWatchReindexesOnChange` integration test.

(inconsistency) §14.7 step 3 states "The MCP server's fsnotify watcher picks up changes" (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:89`), and the §6.4 contract it references states "The MCP server watches the resolved path via fsnotify and re-indexes on change" (`spec/06-mcp-server.md:85`). The implementation does not use fsnotify for the overlay; `startOverlayWatch` installs a 500 ms ticker poll loop that re-resolves the overlay whenever a tree fingerprint (path, modtime, size) changes (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:18`, `cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:66`, and `pkg/sync/watch.go:158`). The source comment acknowledges the divergence: "§6.4 names fsnotify, but the behavioral contract it states is 're-indexes on change', which the poller satisfies" (`cmd/podium-mcp/overlay_watch.go:13`). The repository already depends on `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify` and uses a real fsnotify watcher for `podium sync --watch` in `pkg/sync/watch_fsnotify.go:1`, so the divergence is specific to the MCP overlay watcher. The behavioral contract ("picks up changes" / "re-indexes on change") is met because the poller detects modtime and size changes within the tree, so the blast radius is limited to detection latency of up to one poll interval and to the literal mechanism named in the spec. Suggested direction: either reuse the existing `pkg/sync` fsnotify watcher for the MCP overlay path so the implementation matches the spec wording, or amend §14.7 and §6.4 to describe the mechanism as "watches the resolved path and re-indexes on change" without naming fsnotify.

## F-14.8 — 14.8 Remote registry + local overlay, custom harness via SDK

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.8 against the implementation._

Section 14.8 (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:91-103`) describes an SDK-driven workspace that reaches a remote registry, merges a workspace-local overlay, and runs the `oauth-device-code` login flow. The only concrete, checkable contract in the section is the Python example: a `Client(registry=..., identity_provider="oauth-device-code", overlay_path="./.podium/overlay/")` constructor, a `client.login()` device-code flow that runs before any catalog call, and subsequent `search_artifacts` / `load_artifact` use. The operator setup is delegated to §14.5, which other agents cover.

Each claim holds against the code. The Python `Client.__init__` accepts `registry` positionally plus the keyword arguments `identity_provider` (default `"oauth-device-code"`) and `overlay_path` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:346-363`), and `Client` is exported from the package root (`sdks/podium-py/podium/__init__.py:4-12`). `client.login()` runs the RFC 8628 device-code flow, discovering the IdP from the registry's RFC 8414 metadata, printing the verification URL and user code, polling the token endpoint, and storing the access token on the client (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:452-505`, `sdks/podium-py/podium/_oauth.py:47-165`). `search_artifacts` and `load_artifact` exist and fuse the overlay client-side (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:534-584`, `633-674`), with the overlay path resolved through the §6.4 precedence order where an explicit `overlay_path` wins (`sdks/podium-py/podium/_overlay.py:25-40`). The TypeScript SDK mirrors the same surface: a `Client` constructed from `ClientOptions` with `registry`, `identityProvider`, and `overlayPath` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:335-381`), a `login()` device-code flow (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:460-495`), and `searchArtifacts` / `loadArtifact` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:517-616`). The end-to-end behavior is exercised by `sdks/podium-py/tests/test_resolution_overlay_login.py:258-266`, which logs in via a stub IdP and confirms the resulting token authenticates the next `search_artifacts` call as `Bearer tok-abc`. The registry server itself does not serve `/.well-known/oauth-authorization-server`; that metadata is the operator-deployed external OIDC IdP's responsibility per §14.5 and §13.1, and the CLI `podium login` discovers from the same URL (`cmd/podium/login.go:172-193`), so this is consistent design rather than a §14.8 gap.

No findings.

## F-14.9 — 14.9 Enterprise multi-layer setup

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.9 against the implementation._

§14.9 describes the enterprise deployment with multiple Git-source admin layers, per-layer visibility per §4.6, signing and freeze windows, a CI `podium lint` check, webhook-driven ingest, and personal user-defined layers capped per identity. Most of the section restates contracts defined in detail in §4.6, §7.3.1, and §14.5–14.8; the §14.9-specific concrete claims are the operator `layers:` config with `source.git.{repo, ref, root}` and `visibility.{organization, groups, public}`, the effective-view composition over admin layers (visibility-filtered) plus user-defined layers plus the workspace local overlay, the `podium layer register --id --repo --ref` invocation for personal layers, and the default cap of 3 user-defined layers per identity.

Each of these holds against the code. The operator `layers:` block parses with the exact §14.9 keys: `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:147-181` defines `yamlLayerEntry.ID`, `yamlLayerSource.Git.{Repo, Ref, Root}`, and `yamlLayerVisibility.{Public, Organization, Groups, Users}`, and `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:543-593` seeds each entry as a `store.LayerConfig` with resolved visibility and assigns precedence 1..N in list order per §4.6. Visibility filtering implements the §4.6 union (`public`, `organization`, `groups`, `users`) at `pkg/layer/composer.go:64-99`, and the effective view applies it through `visibleManifests` at `pkg/registry/core/effective_view.go:34-52`. The `podium layer register --id <id> --repo <repo> --ref <ref> [--root <subpath>]` command exists with those flags at `cmd/podium/layer.go:175-246`, and an authenticated non-admin caller registering without `--user-defined` is resolved server-side to a personal layer at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:510-521`. The default cap of 3 per identity is `DefaultMaxUserLayers = 3` at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:28`, enforced at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:572-599` where a fourth owned layer is rejected with `quota.layer_count_exceeded`. The workspace local overlay sits as the highest-precedence layer per `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:1-5`. No defects were found in the §14.9 contracts.

No findings.

## F-14.10 — 14.10 Standalone registry with a Git-source layer

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.10 against the implementation._

The section describes a single-developer standalone setup with three concrete commands and one bootstrap claim: `podium serve --standalone --layer-path ~/podium-artifacts` (which auto-bootstraps `~/.podium/sync.yaml` pointing at the local server), `podium layer register --id <id> --repo <url> --ref main`, `podium layer reingest <id>`, and `podium layer watch <id> --interval 1h`. The flags and subcommands exist. `podium serve` accepts `--standalone` (`cmd/podium/serve.go:25`) and `--layer-path` (`cmd/podium/serve.go:30`), and the standalone startup writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: <publicURL>` (`internal/serverboot/standalone_bootstrap.go:117-123`), where `publicURL` defaults to `http://127.0.0.1:8080` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1639-1640`, `:1445`). `podium layer register` accepts `--id`, `--repo`, `--ref`, and `--root` and POSTs to `/v1/layers` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:175-239`). `podium layer reingest <id>` POSTs to `/v1/layers/reingest?id=<id>` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:352-392`). `podium layer watch <id> --interval 1h` parses `--interval` as a Go duration, so the documented `1h` value works (`cmd/podium/layer.go:150`). The server returns the webhook URL on git-layer registration (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:653-655`). The findings below concern how the registry URL reaches those layer commands and the form of the printed webhook URL.

### - [x] F-14.10.1 — layer commands ignore the bootstrapped sync.yaml registry [High] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 9da4f98): `layer register`, `layer reingest`, and `layer watch` now resolve the registry through `resolveLayerRegistry`, which falls back to `defaults.registry` in the merged `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (via `sync.LoadMergedConfig`) when both `--registry` and `PODIUM_REGISTRY` are empty, the same precedence `podium sync` uses. The §14.10 commands work against the standalone server that `podium serve --standalone` bootstrapped, with no explicit `--registry`. Covered by `TestMergedRegistry_ReadsHomeSyncYAML`, `TestMergedRegistry_EmptyWhenNoConfig`, `TestResolveLayerRegistry_FlagValueWins`, `TestLayerRegister_FallsBackToSyncYAMLRegistry` (unit) and `TestStandaloneLayer_ResolvesBootstrappedRegistry` / `TestStandaloneLayer_NoRegistryAnywhereRefuses` (e2e).

(gap) §14.10 step 1 states that `podium serve --standalone --layer-path ~/podium-artifacts` "auto-bootstraps `~/.podium/sync.yaml` pointing at the local server" (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:138`), and steps 2 and 3 then run `podium layer register`, `podium layer reingest`, and `podium layer watch` with no `--registry` flag (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:141-148`). The implied contract is that these commands resolve the registry from the bootstrapped `~/.podium/sync.yaml`. The standalone bootstrap does write `defaults.registry` into that file (`internal/serverboot/standalone_bootstrap.go:117-123`), but every `podium layer` subcommand resolves the registry only from the `--registry` flag defaulted to `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:178`, `:355`, `:145` for register, reingest, and watch), and aborts with exit code 2 and `error: --registry is required` when both are empty (`cmd/podium/layer.go:196-199`, `:372-374`, `:155-157`). The bootstrap writes a file but never exports `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, and the layer dispatch in `cmd/podium/main.go:61-62` adds no merged-config fallback, so the layer commands never read the bootstrapped `defaults.registry`. By contrast, `podium sync` does fall back to the merged sync.yaml registry (`cmd/podium/main.go:548-554`), which makes the omission specific to the layer commands. Following §14.10 literally, every command in steps 2 and 3 fails with `error: --registry is required` because no scope ever sets `PODIUM_REGISTRY`. Suggested direction: have the `layer register`, `reingest`, and `watch` subcommands resolve the registry through the same `--registry` / `PODIUM_REGISTRY` / merged `~/.podium/sync.yaml` `defaults.registry` precedence chain that `podium sync` uses, so the §14.10 commands work against the bootstrapped standalone server without an explicit `--registry`.

### - [x] F-14.10.2 — register prints a relative webhook path rather than a usable URL [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit 9da4f98): the registry now advertises an absolute webhook URL. `LayerEndpoint` carries a `publicBaseURL` (wired by serverboot from `cfg.publicURL`, i.e. `PODIUM_PUBLIC_URL` or `http://<bind>`), and `webhookURL` builds `<base>/v1/ingest/webhook/<id>` for both the register and secret-rotation paths, falling back to the relative path when no base is configured. `podium layer register` also prints the URL on its own `webhook URL: <url>` line in addition to the raw JSON. Covered by `TestLayerEndpoint_RegisterGitLayer_AbsoluteWebhookURL` / `TestLayerEndpoint_RegisterGitLayer_RelativeWebhookURLWithoutBase` (unit), the retargeted `TestHTTPAPI_IngestWebhookInvalid` and `TestServerOps_WebhookInvalidHMAC` (e2e absolute-URL assertions), and the labeled-line assertion in `TestStandaloneLayer_ResolvesBootstrappedRegistry` (e2e).

(inconsistency) §14.10 step 3 states that "The CLI prints the webhook URL it would expect" (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:144`). `podium layer register` prints the raw JSON response body (`cmd/podium/layer.go:244`), which carries `webhook_url` from the server, but the server populates that field with the relative path `/v1/ingest/webhook/<id>` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:654`, field declared at `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:225`). A relative path lacks the scheme and host of the running server, so it is not a webhook URL a developer could paste into a Git host's webhook configuration, and the CLI does not surface it as a distinct line. The wording in §14.10 is informal, so this is a minor deviation rather than a contract break. Suggested direction: return an absolute webhook URL built from the server's `publicURL` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1639-1640`) and, optionally, have `podium layer register` print the webhook URL on its own labeled line instead of only embedding it in the raw JSON.

## F-14.11 — 14.11 CI / build pipeline materialization

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.11 against the implementation._

The §14.11 scenario describes a non-interactive build pipeline that materializes a deterministic artifact set with `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile production --target ./build/.claude/`, authenticated by a runtime-issued JWT read from `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE`, and commits the resulting `.podium/sync.lock` for reproducibility. Most of the concrete contracts hold. The `injected-session-token` provider and the three environment variables (`PODIUM_REGISTRY`, `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`, `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE`) exist (`pkg/identity/identity.go:64`, `pkg/identity/registry.go:66`, `cmd/podium/main.go:1201`). All four `sync` flags (`--harness`, `--profile`, `--target`, `--dry-run`, `--json`) are wired (`cmd/podium/main.go:193`, `cmd/podium/main.go:197`, `cmd/podium/main.go:198`, `cmd/podium/main.go:200`, `cmd/podium/main.go:204`). The lock file lives at `<target>/.podium/sync.lock` and records the `(id, version, content_hash)` triple plus the materialized path per artifact (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:65`, `pkg/sync/lockfile.go:40`), and `--dry-run` returns before any write or lock write (`pkg/sync/sync.go:259`). The non-interactive CI credential path attaches `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` as the `Authorization: Bearer` token only for a server source (`cmd/podium/main.go:317`, `cmd/podium/main.go:1201`), and `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is honored in the resolution precedence (`pkg/sync/resolve.go:233`).

The findings concern the fidelity of the recorded `content_hash` for a server-source sync, the absence of `content_hash` from the recommended `--dry-run --json` pre-flight envelope, and a target-layout mismatch between the documented `--target ./build/.claude/` and the claude-code adapter's own `.claude/` path prefix.

### - [x] F-14.11.1 — Server-source lock records a recomputed content_hash, not the registry's authoritative value [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit ece18d6): `serverLoadResponse` now decodes `content_hash`, `materialRecord` carries it, and `fetchServerRecord` populates it from the `/v1/load_artifact` response. The new `lockContentHash` helper pins the registry's authoritative value verbatim when present, falling back to `contentHashFor` only for a filesystem source (no recorded hash). The committed server-source lock now matches the registry's system-of-record `content_hash`; the integration guard against the real in-process server confirmed the prior recomputed digest diverged for every reference-fixture artifact, not only extends-merged ones. Covered by `TestLockContentHash_PrefersRegistryValue`, `TestLockContentHash_FallsBackToComputed`, `TestRun_ServerSourceLockPinsRegistryContentHash` (unit), `TestSyncServerSource_LockPinsRegistryContentHash` (integration), and `TestSyncServerSource_LockContentHashIsRegistryAuthoritative` (e2e).

(bug) §14.11 states that the lock file "captures exactly which `(artifact_id, version, content_hash)` triples landed in the image" and instructs the operator to "Commit it alongside the build for reproducibility" (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:167`). For a remote registry (the scenario uses `PODIUM_REGISTRY=https://podium.acme.com`), the registry already supplies an authoritative `content_hash` in the `/v1/load_artifact` response (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:467`). The sync client discards it: `serverLoadResponse` does not decode the `content_hash` field (`pkg/sync/server.go:46`), and `materialRecord` has no field to carry it (`pkg/sync/sync.go:112`). Instead the lock entry's `content_hash` is recomputed locally by `contentHashFor`, which concatenates the served frontmatter or skill bytes plus the inline and fetched resources and hashes them (`pkg/sync/sync.go:252`, `pkg/sync/sync.go:335`). The registry itself flags that an extends-merged manifest's served bytes "no longer reproduce ContentHash" (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:480`), so the locally recomputed digest can diverge from the registry's recorded `content_hash` for the same artifact. When that happens the committed lock records a hash that does not correspond to the registry's system-of-record value, which undermines the reproducibility guarantee the scenario relies on. Suggested direction: decode `content_hash` from the `/v1/load_artifact` response into `serverLoadResponse` and `materialRecord`, and have the server path persist the registry's authoritative value into the lock rather than recomputing one from the served bytes.

### - [x] F-14.11.2 — Doubled `.claude/` when `--target` already names the harness config directory [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (commit `48955a0`): `sync.Run` now strips an adapter-emitted file's leading path segment when it equals the sync target's final directory component, so a `--target ./build/.claude/` (the §14.11 mental model, also §7.5/§7.5.3/§7.7's `target: .claude/`) materializes a single `.claude/` deep instead of `.claude/.claude/`, and the committed lock records `materialized_path: agents/pay-invoice.md` relative to the target per the §7.5.3 example. Neutral buckets (`.podium/`, `.mcp.json`) and ordinary workspace-root targets are untouched. The spec is read-only (Rule A); the implementation follows its `--target`-is-the-harness-config-dir model rather than editing the §14.11 example.

(inconsistency) §14.11's pipeline step runs `podium sync --harness claude-code ... --target ./build/.claude/` (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:165`), and §7.5.3's lock example shows `materialized_path: agents/pay-invoice.md` relative to `target: /Users/alice/.claude/` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:292`, `spec/07-external-integration.md:301`), indicating the documented mental model is that `--target` points at the harness config directory and the materialized paths are relative to it. The claude-code adapter unconditionally prefixes `.claude/` onto every emitted path (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:73` writes `.claude/agents/<name>.md`), and `materialize.Write` joins each such path under the destination root with `filepath.Join(dest, rel)` (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:299`). With `--target ./build/.claude/`, the result is `./build/.claude/.claude/agents/<name>.md`, a doubled `.claude/` segment, and the lock then records `materialized_path: .claude/agents/...` rather than the spec's `agents/...`. No target normalization strips a trailing `.claude` before the join. The contract's primary home is the §6.7 / §7.5 target-layout convention, so this is scoped Low for §14.11, but the §14.11 example reproduces the same defective pattern and would not lay out the build directory as written. Suggested direction: reconcile the documented `--target .../.claude/` usage with the adapter's `.claude/` prefix, either by treating `--target` as the workspace root in the spec examples or by stripping a trailing harness-config segment from the target before materializing.

### - [ ] F-14.11.3 — `--dry-run --json` pre-flight envelope omits content_hash [Info] — DEFERRED

Deferred (Rule A — spec read-only): §7.5 defines the `--json` envelope as exactly `{profile, target, harness, scope, artifacts: [{id, version, type, layer}, ...]}` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:175`), which the implementation matches; §14.11 attaches the `(id, version, content_hash)` triple to the committed lock file (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:167`), not to the pre-flight envelope, and its fidelity is now authoritative via F-14.11.1 (same commit ece18d6). Adding `content_hash` to the envelope would diverge from §7.5; reconciling §7.5 and §14.11 so pre-flight can show the full triple requires a spec edit, which Rule A forbids. No code change. The §7.5 envelope contract and the §14.11 lock triple are guarded by `TestSync_DryRunJSONEnvelopeOmitsContentHash` (e2e). Not unblocked by code (the blocker is the §7.5 definition).

(inconsistency) §14.11 emphasizes the `(artifact_id, version, content_hash)` triple as what lands in the image and recommends `podium sync --dry-run --json` "in pre-flight to sanity-check what the build will include" (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:167`, `spec/14-common-scenarios.md:169`). The `--json` envelope emits per-artifact `id`, `version`, `type`, and `layer` only; the `artOut` struct has no `content_hash` field even though `sync.Result` carries `ContentHash` per artifact (`cmd/podium/main.go:1411`, `pkg/sync/sync.go:252`). A pre-flight `--dry-run --json` therefore cannot show the `content_hash` half of the triple that §14.11 highlights, so a build cannot confirm the exact triples before committing the lock. This matches the envelope contract defined in §7.5, which lists exactly `{id, version, type, layer}` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:175`), so the JSON output is consistent with its own spec; the gap is between §7.5's envelope and §14.11's emphasis on the triple, recorded here as an ambiguity to confirm rather than a code defect. Suggested direction: confirm whether §7.5's `--json` envelope should include `content_hash` so the §14.11 pre-flight check can verify the full triple, and add the field to both the envelope and the spec if so.

## F-14.12 — 14.12 Air-gapped enterprise

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.12 against the implementation._

Section 14.12 (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:171`-`182`) describes an air-gapped enterprise deployment. The prose is largely conceptual and aggregates capabilities defined in other sections, so the checkable contracts are the named providers and backends and the air-gapped signing path. Each concrete claim is satisfied by the implementation.

The `ollama` embedding provider is selectable via `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` and points at a local endpoint with no external API key requirement (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1911`-`1915`, `pkg/embedding/ollama.go:23`-`117`, default base URL `http://localhost:11434`). The pgvector vector backend is supported as a store-collocated backend that needs no external managed service, selectable via `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND` with `PODIUM_PGVECTOR_DSN`/`PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:1939`-`1941`, `pkg/vector/pgvector.go`). Internal S3-compatible object storage (MinIO) is supported with a custom endpoint and path-style addressing via `PODIUM_S3_ENDPOINT` and `PODIUM_S3_FORCE_PATH_STYLE` (`pkg/objectstore/s3.go:29`-`64`, `pkg/objectstore/s3.go:97`).

The signing claim, that "Sigstore-keyless requires public OIDC infrastructure; air-gapped deployments use the registry-managed signing key path instead", holds. The sigstore-keyless provider requires a Fulcio URL and an OIDC token and fails without them (`pkg/sign/sigstore.go:38`-`47`, `pkg/sign/sigstore.go:104`). The registry-managed Ed25519 key path is a complete air-gapped alternative with `Sign` and `Verify` and no external dependency (`pkg/sign/registry_managed.go:52`-`102`), selectable at ingest via `PODIUM_SIGN=registry-key` with a locally generated keypair under `PODIUM_SIGN_KEY_PATH` (`internal/serverboot/signing.go:21`-`53`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:669`-`674`). No public OIDC infrastructure is needed for this path.

No findings.

## F-14.13 — 14.13 Mixed-harness developer

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.13 against the implementation._

Section 14.13 describes a single developer who runs Claude Code on one project and Cursor on another while sharing one OAuth identity and one content cache. The subsection states four checkable claims: `podium login --registry https://podium.acme.com` caches a token in the OS keychain; Project A runs Claude Code with the §6.11 Claude Code MCP snippet and a workspace overlay at `<project-a>/.podium/overlay/`; Project B runs Cursor with the §6.11 Cursor MCP snippet and a workspace overlay at `<project-b>/.podium/overlay/`; and both projects share the same OS-keychain token, the same `~/.podium/cache/`, and the same user-wide audit log at `~/.podium/audit.log`. The subsection is a scenario that composes mechanisms specified in detail in §6.2, §6.3, §6.4, §6.11, §7.7, and §8.3.

Every claim traces to working code. `podium login` exposes the `--registry` flag and saves the access token to the keychain (`cmd/podium/login.go:33`, `cmd/podium/login.go:124`, `cmd/podium/login.go:233`), with the keychain entry keyed by registry URL (`pkg/identity/keychain.go:44`). The `claude-code` and `cursor` adapters are both registered in the default registry (`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:157`, `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:160`), and the MCP bridge reads `PODIUM_HARNESS` and `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` from the §6.11 env contract (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:224`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:235`) and defaults the workspace overlay to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:916`, `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:62`). The cache directory defaults to `~/.podium/cache` in both the MCP bridge and the CLI (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:321`, `cmd/podium/cache.go:55`). The shared token works across both harnesses because `podium login` and the MCP bridge use the same default keychain service name `podium` and the same registry-URL key (`cmd/podium/login.go:124`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:246`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:501`). The shared audit log at `~/.podium/audit.log` supports concurrent multi-process appends via `O_APPEND` writes and a per-writer-chain forest verification model (`pkg/audit/file.go:39`, `pkg/audit/file.go:97`, `pkg/audit/file.go:125`).

No findings.

## F-14.14 — 14.14 Promote-to-shared workflow

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.14 against the implementation._

Section 14.14 (`spec/14-common-scenarios.md:193`) describes a conceptual workflow in which a developer iterates on an artifact in a workspace overlay and then promotes it to a shared Git layer. It states no new wire formats or endpoints of its own; every concrete, checkable claim refers to features specified in detail in other sections. I extracted and traced each concrete claim: the workspace overlay path `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/finance/cashflow/forecast/ARTIFACT.md` plus `SKILL.md` (step 1), the MCP server / sync / SDK seeing overlay edits immediately (step 1), the `podium lint` command (step 4), the inbound webhook that fires registry ingest (step 5), and `podium sync save-as` capturing a curated set of overrides as a profile in `sync.yaml` (closing paragraph).

Each claim traces to working code. The overlay directory layout matches: the built-in provider documents `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` and resolves it via the `§6.4` precedence rules at `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:32` and `pkg/overlay/overlay.go:59`, and `podium init` scaffolds `.podium/overlay/` at `cmd/podium/main.go:1108`. The overlay opens as a filesystem registry and walks its artifacts recursively, so a nested domain path such as `finance/cashflow/forecast` is supported (`pkg/overlay/overlay.go:50`). The MCP server re-indexes on overlay filesystem changes through `startOverlayWatch` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:732`), backing the "sees it immediately" claim. The `podium lint` command validates a filesystem registry with the same lint rules the ingest pipeline runs (`cmd/podium/main.go:721` and `pkg/lint/description_rules.go:38`). The inbound webhook handler verifies the provider signature and then drives the ingest pipeline (`pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:29`, with the ingest dispatch at `pkg/registry/server/webhook_ingest.go:82`). `podium sync save-as` writes the captured scope and toggles as a profile into `.podium/sync.yaml` and clears the lock-file toggles (`pkg/sync/override.go:200` and `cmd/podium/main.go:583`, with the canonical config path at `pkg/sync/config.go:66`).

No findings.

## F-14.15 — 14.15 Read-only viewer / auditor

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md §14.15 against the implementation._

The §14.15 scenario describes a read-only viewer who sets `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, runs `podium login`, and then browses the catalog with `podium domain show`, `podium search --type skill --json`, and `podium artifact show --version`, with `podium sync --dry-run` offered as the same view in materialization form. Each command, flag, and environment variable in the scenario block maps to working code. `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is the default for the read commands' `--registry` flag and is resolved by `podium login` (`cmd/podium/main.go:778`, `cmd/podium/login.go:148`). `podium login` runs the device-code flow and caches the token keyed by registry URL (`cmd/podium/login.go:124-128`); the read commands attach that token as a bearer credential so server-side visibility filtering applies to the caller identity (`cmd/podium/main.go:1241-1243`).

`podium domain show` accepts an optional path argument and forwards it as the `path` query parameter to `/v1/load_domain`, rendering a nested-bullet tree by default and a JSON envelope under `--json` (`cmd/podium/main.go:872-899`, `cmd/podium/main.go:1320-1375`). `podium search` exposes `--type` and `--json` and forwards `type` to `/v1/search_artifacts`, which threads it into `core.SearchArtifacts` (`cmd/podium/main.go:775-817`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:670-678`). `podium artifact show` exposes `--version` and forwards `version` to `/v1/load_artifact` (`cmd/podium/main.go:957-994`). `podium sync --dry-run` resolves the artifact set and returns before any disk write or stale-file cleanup, so it writes nothing (`pkg/sync/sync.go:259-261`), and the dry-run JSON envelope carries the resolved `profile` and `scope` that the scenario describes (`cmd/podium/main.go:1422-1438`).

The implementation satisfies every checkable claim in §14.15.

No findings.
